Fifth Tanbih: Judgments Contrary to Consensus Are Unenforceable
Rule that rulings against ijma, including the four schools, are void

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that judgments contradicting the consensus of the four schools are unenforceable and apply it to identify which opinions a mufti may rely upon.

Core Idea
A mufti may only act within the four schools – any other view is outside consensus.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir establishes an important principle for muftis: a judgment or fatwa that contradicts the consensus of the four Sunni schools is void. Even if a minority opinion exists outside these schools, it cannot be acted upon. This rule ensures practical uniformity in fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule's scope
The rule addresses any judicial judgment (qada) that contradicts consensus (ijma). It also applies to fatwas by extension, as fatwas guide practice.
2
Understand the definition of consensus here
Consensus here is not the theoretical consensus of all scholars, but the practical consensus of the four Sunni schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali). The text equates contradicting these four with contradicting consensus.
This is a later development in Hanafi usul, reflecting the crystallization of the four schools.
3
Analyze the proof
The authority cited (al-Tahrir) argues that the four schools are well-defined (inqibad), widespread (intishar), and have many followers (kathrat atba'). This makes them the reliable standard.
4
Apply the rule to mufti practice
A mufti cannot rely on a ruling from a fifth school (e.g., Zahiri, Zaydi, or a modern ijtihad) if it contradicts the four schools, even if that ruling has some scholarly support.
This is a severe restriction, but it is the operative position in later Hanafi fatwa manuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : مما لا ينفذ القضاء به ما إذا قضى بشيء مخالف للإجماع وهو ظاهر وما خالف الأئمة الأربعة مخالف للإجماع، وإن كان فيه خلاف لغيرهم، فقد صرّح في التحرير أن الإجماع انعقد على عدم العمل بمذهب مخالف للأربعة لانضباط مذاهبهم وانتشارها وكثرة أتباعهم .
Fifth: Among that which the judgment is not enforceable is when he judges something contrary to consensus, and that is apparent. And whatever contradicts the four Imams is contrary to consensus, even if there is a disagreement among others. For it is stated in al-Tahrir that consensus has been established on not acting upon a school that contradicts the four, due to the precision of their schools, their prevalence, and the number of their followers.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
The fifth note states that any judgment that violates consensus (ijma) is not enforceable. It further asserts that contradicting the four schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) is tantamount to contradicting consensus, because the consensus of the ummah has effectively solidified around the four schools. Even if there are minority opinions outside these schools, they are not considered valid for judicial action. This is based on the authority of al-Tahrir, which argues that the four schools are well-defined, widespread, and have many followers, making them the reliable standard. Thus, a judge who follows a non-four-school opinion renders a judgment that is unenforceable.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the Muslim scholars; here, specifically the consensus represented by the four Sunni schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth tanbih, what is the status of a judgment that contradicts the four schools?
A) It is enforceable if based on a minority opinion
B) It is not enforceable because it contradicts consensus
C) It is valid if the judge is a mujtahid
D) It is valid if it follows the school of the judge's choice

Key Takeaway
A mufti must restrict his fatwas to the four established schools, as contradicting them is tantamount to contradicting consensus.

When Halal and Haram Combine, Haram Prevails (القاعدة الثانية)
Presentation and application of a legal maxim with numerous furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim, explain its usul justification (minimizing abrogation), and apply it to at least five furuat while recognizing the exception of necessity.

Core Idea
When halal and haram are inseparable, haram dominates — a precautionary principle rooted in minimizing abrogation.

The second maxim in Ibn Nujaym's Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir addresses a recurring challenge in fatwa: how to rule when an action or object contains both permissible and prohibited elements. This lesson unpacks the maxim's textual basis, its usul rationale, and a wide range of applications from menstruation to mixed meats, showing how the Hanafi school consistently gives precedence to prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the maxim
State the Arabic and English versions: 'إذا اجتمع الحلال والحرام غلب الحرام' — 'When halal and haram combine, haram prevails.'
This is a sughra maxim but governs all fiqh chapters.
2
Understand the hadith evidence
Note that the hadith is weak but accepted in meaning. It is transmitted as a saying of Ibn Mas'ud and also as marfu'. The maxim is also supported by rational reasoning.
Al-`Iraqi said it has no basis, but al-Zayla`i mentioned it as marfu' in the book of hunting.
3
Grasp the usul rationale
The maxim minimizes abrogation: if permissibility (original ruling) is taken as later, prohibition would be abrogated twice; if prohibition is later, it abrogates only once. Also precaution (ihtiyat).
This reasoning is from the usul works like al-Tahrir and Sharh al-Manar.
4
Analyze the first furu: conflicting proofs
When two dalils conflict, one for halal and one for haram, haram is given precedence. Example: 'Uthman's ruling on combining two sisters through right hand possession.
This applies to any case where a verse or hadith permits and another prohibits.
5
Examine the menstruation dispute
Two hadith: (1) 'For you from the menstruating woman is what is above the izar' (prohibits below). (2) 'Do everything except intercourse' (permits everything else). The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Malik, Shafi'i) apply the maxim and forbid touching between navel and knee. Muhammad and Ahmad follow the permissive hadith.
This is a key intra- and inter-madhhab ikhtilaf.
6
Apply the maxim to the remaining furuat
Work through the furuat in order: animal hybrids (dog-sheep, donkey-horse), mixed dog teams in hunting, Magian assistance in slaughter, tree/game partly in Haram, mixed skins of slaughtered and dead animals, mixed fat with oil. Notice the pattern: whenever permissible and impermissible are inseparably combined, the whole becomes impermissible.
Some cases allow taharrī if the majority is permissible, but not if equal or majority is prohibited.
7
Identify the exception
Extreme hunger (makhmasah) permits consumption of mixed impure food. This is governed by the maxim 'Necessity permits prohibited things' (al-darurah tubih al-mahzurat).
This is the only major exception to the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاعدة الثانية : إذا اجتمع الحلال والحرام غلب الحرام
وبمعناها ما اجتمع محرم ومبيح إلا غلب المحرم والعبارة الأولى لفظ حديث أورده جماعة ما اجتمع الحلال والحرام إلا غلب الحرام الحلال». قال العراقي : لا أصل له وضعفه البيهقي وأخرجه عبد الرزاق موقوفا على ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه، وذكره الزيلعي شارح الكنز في كتاب الصيد مرفوعًا. فمن فروعها ما إذا تعارض دليلان أحدهما يقتضي التحريم والآخر الإباحة قدَّم التحريم، وعلله الأصوليون بتقليل النسخ لأنه لو قدم المبيح للزم تكرار النسخ لأن الأصل في الأشياء الإباحة، فإذا جعل المبيح متأخرا كان المحرم ناسخا للإباحة الأصلية ثم يصير منسوخا بالمبيح. ولو جعل المحرم متأخرًا لكان ناسخًا للمبيح وهو لم ينسخ شيئًا لكونه على وفق الأصل. وفي التحرير يقدم المحرم تقليلاً للنسخ واحتياطا. وقد أوضحناه في شرح المنار في باب ثَمة قال عثمان رضي الله تعالى عنه، لمَّا سُئِلَ عن الجمع بين أختين من ملك اليمين : أحلَّتهما آية وحرَّمتهما آية التحريم أحب إلينا. وذكر بعضهم أن النوع حديث لك من الحائض ما فوق الإزار (۱) وحديث «اصنعوا كل شيء إلا النكاح (۲) فإن الأول يقتضي تحريم ما بين السرة والركبة. والثاني يقتضي إباحة ما عدا الوطء فرجح التحريم احتياطا، وهو قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومالك والشافعي . وخص محمد رحمه الله شعار الدم وبه قال أحمد عملاً بالثاني. ومنها لو اشتبه محرمه بأجنبيات محصورات لم يحل، كما قدمناه في قاعدة الأصل في الأبضاع التحريم. ومنها من أحد أبويه مأكول والآخر غير مأكول لا يحلّ أكله على الأصح. فإذا نزا كلب على شاة فولدت لا يؤكل الولد. وكذا إذا نزا حمار على فرس فولدت بغلاً لم يؤكل، والأهلي إذا نزا على الوحشي فنتج لا تجوز الأضحية كذا في الفوائد التاجية . ومنها لو شارك الكلب المعلّم غير المعلم، أو كلب مجوسي أو كلب لم يذكر اسم الله تعالى عليه عمدًا حرم كما في الهداية . ومنها ما في صيد الخانية: مجوسي أخذ بيد مسلم فذبح والسكين في يد المسلم لا يحلّ أكله لاجتماع المحرم والمبيح فيحرم كما لو عجز مسلم عن قوسه بنفسه فأعانه على مده مجوسي لا يحل أكله. (انتهى). ومنها عدم جواز وطء الجارية المشتركة. ومنها لو كان بعض الشجرة في الحلّ وبعضها في الحرم. ومنها لو كان بعض الصيد في الحلّ والبعض في الحرم. والمنقول في الثانية كما ذكره الأسبيجابي أن الاعتبار لقوائمه لا لرأسه حتى لو كان قائما في الحلّ ورأسه في الحرم فلا شيء بقتله ولا يشترط أن يكون جميع قوائمه في الحرم حتى لو كان بعضها في الحرم وبعضها في الحلّ وجب الجزاء بقتله لتغليب الحظر على الإباحة. (انتهى) . أقسام : القسمة . وأما المنقول في الأولى ففي الأجناس : الأغصان تابعة لأصلها وذلك على ثلاثة أحدها أن يكون أصلها في الحرم والأغصان في الحلّ فعلى قاطع أغصانها والثاني أن يكون أصلها في الحلّ وأغصانها في الحرم فلا ضمان على القاطع في أصلها وأغصانها. والثالث أن يكون بعض أصلها في الحلّ وبعضه في الحرم فعلى القاطع الضمان سواء كان الغصن من جانب الحلّ أو من جانب الحرم. (انتهى). ومنها لو اختلطت مساليخ المذكاة بمساليخ الميتة ولا علامة تميز، وكانت الغلبة للميتة أو استويا لم يجز تناول شيء منها ولا بالتحري إلا عند المخمصة. وأما إذا كانت الغلبة للمذكاة فإنه يجوز التحرّي . ومنها لو اختلط ودك الميتة بالزيت ونحوه لم يؤكل إلا عند الضرورة. والمسألتان في صلاة الخلاصة من فصل اشتباه القبلة ومقتضى الثانية أنه لو اختلط لبن بقر بلبن أتان، أو ماء وبول عدم جواز التناول ولا بالتحرّي.
The second maxim: When halal and haram combine, haram prevails. Its meaning is that whenever a prohibited thing and a permitted thing come together, the prohibited prevails except that the prohibited prevails. The first expression is the wording of a hadith that a group narrated: 'Halal and haram do not combine except that haram prevails over halal.' Al-`Iraqi said: It has no basis, and al-Bayhaqi declared it weak. `Abd al-Razzaq transmitted it as a saying of Ibn Mas`ud (may Allah be pleased with him), and al-Zayla`i, commentator of al-Kanz, mentioned it in the book of hunting as marfu`. Among its branches: if two proofs conflict, one indicating prohibition and the other permissibility, prohibition is given precedence. The legal theorists explain this as minimizing abrogation, because if permissibility were given precedence, repeated abrogation would be necessary, since the original ruling for things is permissibility. So if permissibility is made later, the prohibition would abrogate the original permissibility, then it would become abrogated by the permissibility. If prohibition is made later, it would abrogate the permissibility, and it would not have abrogated anything because it aligns with the original ruling. In al-Tahrir, prohibition is given precedence to minimize abrogation and as a precaution. We have explained this in Sharh al-Manar in the chapter on that. `Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) said when asked about combining two sisters through right hand possession: 'One verse made them lawful and one verse made them unlawful; the prohibition is more beloved to us.' Some mentioned that the two types are: the hadith 'For you from the menstruating woman is what is above the lower garment' and the hadith 'Do everything except intercourse.' The first implies prohibition of what is between the navel and knee, and the second implies permissibility of everything except intercourse, so prohibition was given precedence as a precaution. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Malik, and al-Shafi`i. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) specified the sign of blood, and Ahmad followed him, acting on the second hadith. Among them: if a mahram woman is confused among a limited number of non-mahram women, she is not permissible, as we have mentioned in the maxim: the original ruling regarding private parts is prohibition. Among them: one whose one parent is edible and the other is not edible, its consumption is not permissible according to the most correct view. If a dog mounts a sheep and it gives birth, the offspring is not eaten. Similarly, if a donkey mounts a horse and a mule is born, it is not eaten, and if a domestic animal mounts a wild one and offspring results, sacrifice with it is not permissible. Likewise in al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyyah. Among them: if a trained dog is joined by an untrained dog, or a Magian dog, or a dog on which the name of Allah was deliberately not mentioned, it becomes prohibited, as in al-Hidayah. Among them: in Sayd al-Khaniyyah: A Magian took the hand of a Muslim and slaughtered while the knife was in the Muslim's hand, it is not permissible to eat it because of the combination of the prohibited and permissible, so it becomes prohibited, just as if a Muslim was unable to draw his bow himself and a Magian helped him draw it, it is not permissible to eat. (End). Among them: the impermissibility of intercourse with a jointly owned slave girl. Among them: if part of a tree is in the Hill and part in the Haram. Among them: if part of the game is in the Hill and part in the Haram. What is transmitted concerning the second, as al-Asbijabi mentioned, is that consideration is for its legs, not its head, so if it is standing in the Hill and its head is in the Haram, there is no penalty for killing it. It is not required that all its legs be in the Haram, so if some of its legs are in the Haram and some in the Hill, compensation is obligatory for killing it, to give precedence to restriction over permission. (End). Sections: Division. As for what is transmitted concerning the first, in al-Ajnas: Branches are subservient to their origin. This is of three types: one: the origin is in the Haram and the branches are in the Hill, then the cutter of its branches (is liable). Two: the origin is in the Hill and its branches are in the Haram, then there is no liability on the cutter for its origin or its branches. Three: part of the origin is in the Hill and part in the Haram, then the cutter is liable, whether the branch is from the Hill side or the Haram side. (End). Among them: if the skins of slaughtered animals are mixed with skins of dead animals without distinguishing marks, and the majority is dead or equal, it is not permissible to consume any of them, even by ijtihad, except in extreme hunger. If the majority is slaughtered, then ijtihad is permissible. Among them: if the fat of a dead animal is mixed with oil or similar, it is not eaten except in necessity. These two issues are in Salah al-Khulasah from the chapter on confusion of the qibla. The consequence of the second is that if cow's milk is mixed with donkey's milk, or water with urine, consumption is not permissible, even by ijtihad.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the second legal maxim from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: 'When halal and haram combine, haram prevails.' The text first discusses the hadith evidence for this maxim, noting that the hadith is weak but accepted in meaning. The primary reasoning given is to minimize abrogation: since permissibility is the original ruling, giving precedence to prohibition avoids repeatedly abrogating and re-abrogating. The author then provides a comprehensive list of furuat (applications) across various chapters of fiqh. In the case of conflicting proofs, prohibition takes precedence. The example of `Uthman's ruling on combining two sisters through right hand possession illustrates that when two verses conflict, prohibition is preferred. The menstrual woman example shows that despite a hadith permitting everything except intercourse, the prohibition of touching between navel and knee is given precedence, adhering to the maxim. This view is held by Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Malik, and al-Shafi`i, while Muhammad and Ahmad follow the permissive hadith. Other branches cover: mixed parentage animals (e.g., dog-sheep hybrid), hunting with mixed dog teams, slaughter by a Magian, jointly owned slave girls, trees partly in the Haram, game partly in the Haram, mixed meat from slaughtered and dead animals, and mixed liquids. The common thread is that when the permissible and prohibited are inseparable, the prohibited aspect dominates, rendering the whole impermissible except in cases of necessity (e.g., extreme hunger). This maxim is a powerful tool for fatwa, emphasizing caution and conservatism in ambiguous situations.

Key Terms
الحرام (al-haram): That which is legally prohibited by a definitive or preponderant evidence, carrying sin for the doer.
المبيح (al-mubih): That which makes something permissible or indicates permissibility.
التحري (al-taharrī): The effort to determine the permissible through ijtihad when signs are ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on eating an animal that has one edible parent and one inedible parent?
A) Permissible because one parent is edible.
B) Not permissible.
C) Permissible only if slaughtered properly.
D) Not permissible except in necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that haram prevails when it combines with halal is a precautionary principle applied across all fiqh chapters, with the sole exception of dire necessity.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
advanced

The Hanafi Maxim of Taghlib al-Hathr: Applications and Exceptions
List of furuat illustrating the Hanafi maxim of taghlib al-hathr ala al-ibaha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim of taghlib al-hathr to mixed food, hunting, and marriage scenarios, and identify when taharri is permitted or prohibited.

Core Idea
When halal and haram factors combine, prohibition prevails unless a clear exception applies.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents the Hanafi legal maxim of taghlib al-hathr 'ala al-ibaha (precedence of prohibition over permissibility) through a series of concrete furuat (applications). The maxim operates as a precautionary principle: whenever a factor of permissibility and a factor of prohibition coexist, the prohibition is given precedence. The author lists numerous cases from hunting, slaughter, marriage, and foods, and then provides three exceptions where the maxim is set aside due to welfare (the child of mixed parents), the possibility of taharri (vessels and clothes), or necessity. The passage also includes an intra-madhhab dispute on the validity of marriage when a man becomes Muslim with more than four wives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
Define taghlib al-hathr 'ala al-ibaha and identify the fiqh chapters it governs (hunting, slaughter, marriage, foods, etc.).
The maxim is explicitly applied in the hunting case: 'li taghlib al-hathr 'ala al-ibaha'.
2
Analyze the furuat
For each case (mixed dog, Magian slaughter, jointly owned slave-girl, tree/game across Haram boundary, mixed skins/fat/milk, wife mixed with others, game falling after shot), identify the conflicting halal and haram factors.
Focus on how the factors are 'mixed' – e.g., training vs. untrained, Muslim vs. Magian, ownership, location.
3
Apply the maxim to each furu
State why the ruling is prohibition (haram or impermissible) by giving precedence to the prohibition factor.
In some cases, taharri (ijtihad) is still prohibited (e.g., wife mixed), while in others it is allowed (e.g., skins when majority are pure).
4
Examine the exceptions
Understand the three exceptions: (1) child of Kitabi and Majusi – considered Kitabi for child's welfare; (2) vessels – taharri allowed when impure are fewer; (3) clothes – taharri always allowed due to necessity of covering 'awrah.
These exceptions are governed by other qawaid: nazar li al-saghir, al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir, and al-darar yuzal.
5
Evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute
Compare the two positions: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule the marriage invalid, while Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i give choice. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
The mufta bihi is the position of the two shaykhs as per al-Majma'.

به، في الفوائد
لم يؤكل، والأهلي إذا نزا على الوحشي فنتج لا تجوز الأضحية كذا التاجية .
ومنها لو شارك الكلب المعلّم غير المعلم، أو كلب مجوسي أو كلب لم يذكر اسم الله تعالى عليه عمدًا حرم كما في الهداية
ومنها ما في صيد الخانية: مجوسي أخذ بيد مسلم فذبح والسكين في يد المسلم لا يحلّ أكله لاجتماع المحرم والمبيح فيحرم كما لو عجز مسلم عن قوسه بنفسه فأعانه على مده مجوسي لا يحل أكله. (انتهى).
ومنها عدم جواز وطء الجارية المشتركة.
ومنها لو كان بعض الشجرة في الحلّ وبعضها في الحرم.
ومنها لو كان بعض الصيد في الحلّ والبعض في الحرم. والمنقول في الثانية كما ذكره الأسبيجابي أن الاعتبار لقوائمه لا لرأسه حتى لو كان قائما في الحلّ ورأسه في الحرم فلا شيء بقتله ولا يشترط أن يكون جميع قوائمه في الحرم حتى لو كان بعضها في الحرم وبعضها في الحلّ وجب الجزاء بقتله لتغليب الحظر على الإباحة.
(انتهى) .
أقسام :
القسمة .
·
وأما المنقول في الأولى ففي الأجناس : الأغصان تابعة لأصلها وذلك على ثلاثة
أحدها أن يكون أصلها في الحرم والأغصان في الحلّ فعلى قاطع أغصانها
والثاني أن يكون أصلها في الحلّ وأغصانها في الحرم فلا ضمان على القاطع في أصلها وأغصانها.
والثالث أن يكون بعض أصلها في الحلّ وبعضه في الحرم فعلى القاطع الضمان
سواء كان الغصن من جانب الحلّ أو من جانب الحرم. (انتهى).
ومنها لو اختلطت مساليخ المذكاة بمساليخ الميتة ولا علامة تميز، وكانت الغلبة للميتة أو استويا لم يجز تناول شيء منها ولا بالتحري إلا عند المخمصة. وأما إذا كانت الغلبة للمذكاة فإنه يجوز التحرّي .
ومنها لو اختلط ودك الميتة بالزيت ونحوه لم يؤكل إلا عند الضرورة.
·
والمسألتان في صلاة الخلاصة من فصل اشتباه القبلة ومقتضى الثانية أنه لو اختلط لبن بقر بلبن أتان، أو ماء وبول عدم جواز التناول ولا بالتحرّي.

ومنها لو اختلطت زوجته بغيرها فليس له الوطء ولا بالتحري سواء كنَّ محصورات أو لا، كما ذكره أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى في الطلاق المبهم وقالوا لو طلق إحدى زوجتيه مبهما حرم الوطء قبل التعيين ولهذا كان وطء أحديهما تعيينا لطلاق الأخرى. ومن صورها ما لو أسلم على أكثر من أربع فإنه يحرم عليه الوطء قبل الاختيار، على قول من خيَّره وهو محمد والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى. وأما الشيخان فقالا يبطلان النكاح. قال في المجمع من فصل نكاح الكافر: لو أسلم وتحته خمس، أو أختان أو أم وبنت بطل النكاح وإن رتَّب فالأخير، وخيره في اختيار أربع مطلقا أو إحدى الأختين والبنت أو الأم . .(انتهى) .
ومنها لو رمى صيدا فوقع في ماء أو على سطح أو جبل ثم تردَّى منه إلى الأرض حرم للاحتمال والاحتياط الحرمة بخلاف ما إذا وقع على الأرض ابتداء فإنه يحلّ لأنه لا يمكن التحرّز عنه فسقط اعتباره وخرجت عن هذه القاعدة مسائل :
،
الأولى : من أحد أبويه كتابي والآخر مجوسي فإنه يحلّ نكاحه وذبيحته ويجعل كتابيا وهو يقتضي أن يجعل مجوسيا وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى، ولو كان الكتابي الأب في الأظهر عنده تغليبًا لجانب التحريم. لكن أصحابنا تركوا ذلك نظرًا للصغير، فإن المجوسي شرٌّ من الكتابي فلا يجعل الولد تابعا له .
الثانية : الاجتهاد في الأواني إذا كان بعضها طاهرا وبعضها نجسا والأقل نجس فالتحرّي جائز ويريق ما غلب على ظنه أنه نجس، مع أن الاحتياط أنه يريق الكل ويتيمم كما إذا كان الأقل طاهرا عملاً بالأغلب فيهما.
·
الثالثة : الاجتهاد في ثياب مختلطة بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر جائز سواء كان الأكثر نجسا أو لا والفرق بين الثياب والأواني أنه لا خلف لها في ستر العورة وللوضوء خلف في التطهير وهو التيمم. وهذا كله في حالة الاختيار، وأما في حالة الضرورة فيتحرى للشرب اتفاقا كذا في شرح المجمع قبيل التيمم.
وينبغي أن يلحق بمسألة الأواني الثوب المنسوج لحمته من حرير وغيره، فيحلّ إن كان الحرير أقل وزنًا أو استويا بخلاف ما إذا زاد وزنا ولم أره الآن. وفي الخلاصة من التحرّي في كتاب الصلاة : لو اختلطت أوانيه بأواني أصحابه في السفر وهم غيب أو اختلط رغيفه بأرغفة غيره. قال بعضهم يتحرى، وقال بعضهم لا يتحرى ويتربص حتى يجيء أصحابه وهذا في حالة الاختيار وأما في حالة الاضطرار جاز التحرّي مطلقا. (انتهى).
In the benefits: It is not eaten, and if a domestic animal leaps upon a wild one and produces offspring, the sacrifice is not permissible, as in al-Tajiyya. From them: If a trained dog is joined by an untrained dog, or a Magian's dog, or a dog that was not blessed with the name of Allah intentionally, then it is unlawful, as in al-Hidaya. From them: In the hunting chapter of al-Khaniyya: A Magian took the hand of a Muslim and slaughtered while the knife was in the Muslim's hand, it is not permissible to eat it because the forbidden and the permissive are combined, so it becomes forbidden, just as if a Muslim is unable to draw his bow himself and a Magian helps him pull it, then it is not permissible to eat. (End). From them: The impermissibility of intercourse with a jointly owned slave-girl. From them: If part of a tree is in the Halal and part in the Haram. From them: If part of the game is in the Halal and part in the Haram. What is transmitted in the second, as al-Asbijabi mentioned, is that consideration is for its legs, not its head; so if it is standing in the Halal and its head is in the Haram, there is no penalty for killing it, and it is not required that all its legs be in the Haram, so if some are in the Haram and some in the Halal, a penalty is incurred for killing it to give precedence to prohibition over permissibility. (End). Sections: Division. As for what is transmitted in the first, in al-Ajnas: branches follow their origin, and that is in three ways: first, that their origin is in the Haram and the branches are in the Halal, then the cutter of its branches must [pay]; second, that its origin is in the Halal and its branches are in the Haram, then there is no liability on the cutter for its origin and branches; third, that part of its origin is in the Halal and part in the Haram, then the cutter is liable whether the branch is from the side of the Halal or from the side of the Haram. (End). From them: If skins of properly slaughtered animals are mixed with skins of carrion with no distinguishing mark, and the carrion is dominant or equal, it is not permissible to consume any of them, nor by taharri, except in starvation. If the properly slaughtered is dominant, then taharri is permissible. From them: If the fat of carrion is mixed with oil and the like, it is not eaten except in necessity. The two issues are in Salah al-Khulasa from the chapter on confusion of qibla, and the implication of the second is that if cow's milk is mixed with she-ass's milk, or water with urine, it is impermissible to consume, nor by taharri. From them: If his wife is mixed with other women, he may not have intercourse, nor by taharri, whether they are limited or not, as our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) mentioned in ambiguous divorce. They said: if he divorces one of his two wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden before specification, and for this reason intercourse with one of them is a specification of divorce for the other. Among its forms is if he becomes Muslim with more than four women, then intercourse is prohibited before choice, according to the one who gives him choice, which is Muhammad and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them); as for the two shaykhs, they said the marriage becomes invalid. He said in al-Majma' from the chapter on marriage of a disbeliever: if he becomes Muslim with five wives, or two sisters, or a mother and daughter, the marriage is invalid, and if arranged, then the last one [is valid?], and he is given choice to select four absolutely or one of the two sisters and the daughter or the mother... (End). From them: If he shoots game and it falls into water, or on a roof, or a mountain, then falls from there to the ground, it is unlawful due to probability and precaution mandates prohibition, unlike if it fell to the ground directly, then it is permissible because it cannot be avoided, so its consideration is dropped. And exceptions to this rule are issues: First: If one of his parents is a scriptuary and the other a Magian, then his marriage and his slaughtered meat are permissible, and he is considered a scriptuary; this would require him to be considered a Magian, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said that, and if the father is the scriptuary in the more apparent view, it is to give precedence to the side of prohibition. But our companions left that for consideration of the child, because the Magian is worse than the scriptuary, so the child is not made to follow him. Second: ijtihad in vessels: if some are pure and some impure, and the impure are fewer, then taharri is permissible, and he pours out what he thinks is impure, even though caution would be that he pours out all and performs tayammum, just as if the pure are fewer acting according to the majority in both. Third: ijtihad in clothes mixed between impure and pure is permissible whether the majority is impure or not. The difference between clothes and vessels is that there is no substitute for covering the private parts, while for wudu there is a substitute for purification, which is tayammum. All this is in the state of choice; as for the state of necessity, one does taharri for drinking by consensus, as in Sharh al-Majma' before tayammum. It is appropriate to add to the issue of vessels the cloth woven with a weft of silk and other material: it is permissible if the silk is less in weight or equal, unlike if its weight exceeds, but I have not seen that now. In al-Khulasa on taharri in the book of salah: if his vessels are mixed with the vessels of his companions in travel while they are absent, or his loaf is mixed with loaves of others; some said he does taharri, others said he does not and waits until his companions come; this is in the state of choice, but in the state of necessity taharri is permissible absolutely. (End).
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a collection of furuat (applications) under the Hanafi maxim of taghlib al-hathr 'ala al-ibaha (giving precedence to prohibition over permissibility). The author presents numerous cases from various chapters of fiqh where a combination of aspects of permissibility and prohibition leads to the prohibition being upheld due to precaution. The maxim is explicitly stated in the context of hunting in the Haram: 'giving precedence to prohibition over permissibility' (li taghlib al-hathr 'ala al-ibaha). The examples include: a mixed hunting dog, a Magian assisting in slaughter, a joint ownership of a slave-girl, trees and game across the Haram boundary, mixtures of halal and haram skins, fats, milk, etc., and a wife mixed with other women. Also included is the case of a Muslim with more than four wives upon conversion, where the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule the marriage invalid, while Muhammad and al-Shafi'i allow choice. The passage then lists three exceptions to the maxim: (1) a child of mixed parents (Kitabi and Majusi) is considered Kitabi, not Majusi, for the child's benefit; (2) ijtihad in impure vessels when the majority are pure is allowed; (3) ijtihad in impure clothes is allowed even if majority impure, due to the necessity of covering the 'awrah. The author also notes that in necessity, taharri is allowed by consensus. The passage concludes with additional related rulings on silk cloth and mixture of belongings in travel. Throughout, the Hanafi approach emphasizes precaution but recognizes practical exceptions where taharri (ijtihad) is permitted or where consideration of welfare overrides.

Key Terms
تغليب الحظر على الإباحة (taghlīb al-ḥathr ʿalā al-ibāḥa): A legal maxim meaning that when a factor indicating prohibition and a factor indicating permissibility conflict, the prohibition is given precedence as a precaution.
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Ijtihad or striving to determine the correct ruling when faced with ambiguous situations, such as identifying the pure vessel or the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a man becomes Muslim with more than four wives according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)?
A) He may choose four and keep them.
B) The marriage is invalid (bāṭil).
C) He must divorce all but one.
D) He may keep all if they agree.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim of taghlib al-hathr mandates that when halal and haram factors coexist, prohibition is given precedence, but this is balanced by exceptions for necessity, majority, and welfare.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate

The Maxim of Precaution in Cases of Conflict
Applying the maxim to cases of uncertainty in family law and hunting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'precaution takes precedence' to cases of uncertainty and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute on the convert with more than four wives.

Core Idea
When doubt arises, prohibition wins; but if avoidance is impossible, precaution drops.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi legal maxim: when a preventive factor (mani') and a permissive factor (muqtada) conflict, the preventive is given precedence as a precaution (ihtiyat). The author, Ibn Nujaym, illustrates this with several concrete cases from nikah, talaq, and hunting. Understanding this maxim is essential for a mufti when resolving cases of uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim being applied
State the maxim in Arabic and English. Note that it is a sub-maxim (dabt) governing cases where two conflicting factors arise due to uncertainty.
The maxim is not explicitly stated in the passage but is the lesson's title.
2
Analyze the first application: mixed wife
A man's wife is mixed with other women. The preventive factor (prohibition of intercourse with a non-wife) conflicts with the permissive factor (permissibility of intercourse with his wife). Precaution requires forbidding intercourse entirely, even by ijtihad.
Uncertainty about identity triggers the maxim.
3
Examine the ambiguous divorce case
A man divorces one of two wives ambiguously. Intercourse is forbidden until specification because each act of intercourse could be with the divorced woman.
The maxim applies even when the women are limited (mahsurat).
4
Analyze the convert with more than four wives
A man accepts Islam while having five wives. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i say he must choose four and cannot have intercourse before choice (precaution takes precedence); Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the marriages are invalidated entirely.
Note the practical difference: the first view preserves four marriages; the second requires re-marriage.
5
Distinguish the game scenario
Game that falls into water then rolls to ground is forbidden due to doubt. However, if it falls directly on ground, it is permissible because avoidance is impossible—precaution is dropped.
This introduces the exception: 'ma la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu' (what cannot be avoided).

ومنها لو اختلطت زوجته بغيرها فليس له الوطء ولا بالتحري سواء كنَّ محصورات أو لا، كما ذكره أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى في الطلاق المبهم وقالوا لو طلق إحدى زوجتيه مبهما حرم الوطء قبل التعيين ولهذا كان وطء أحديهما تعيينا لطلاق الأخرى. ومن صورها ما لو أسلم على أكثر من أربع فإنه يحرم عليه الوطء قبل الاختيار، على قول من خيَّره وهو محمد والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى. وأما الشيخان فقالا يبطلان النكاح. قال في المجمع من فصل نكاح الكافر: لو أسلم وتحته خمس، أو أختان أو أم وبنت بطل النكاح وإن رتَّب فالأخير، وخيره في اختيار أربع مطلقا أو إحدى الأختين والبنت أو الأم . .(انتهى) . ومنها لو رمى صيدا فوقع في ماء أو على سطح أو جبل ثم تردَّى منه إلى الأرض حرم للاحتمال والاحتياط الحرمة بخلاف ما إذا وقع على الأرض ابتداء فإنه يحلّ لأنه لا يمكن التحرّز عنه فسقط اعتباره وخرجت عن هذه القاعدة مسائل : الأولى : من أحد أبويه كتابي والآخر مجوسي فإنه يحلّ نكاحه وذبيحته ويجعل كتابيا وهو يقتضي أن يجعل مجوسيا وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى، ولو كان الكتابي الأب في الأظهر عنده تغليبًا لجانب التحريم. لكن أصحابنا تركوا ذلك نظرًا للصغير، فإن المجوسي شرٌّ من الكتابي فلا يجعل الولد تابعا له . الثانية : الاجتهاد في الأواني إذا كان بعضها طاهرا وبعضها نجسا والأقل نجس فالتحرّي جائز ويريق ما غلب على ظنه أنه نجس، مع أن الاحتياط أنه يريق الكل ويتيمم كما إذا كان الأقل طاهرا عملاً بالأغلب فيهما. الثالثة : الاجتهاد في ثياب مختلطة بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر جائز سواء كان الأكثر نجسا أو لا والفرق بين الثياب والأواني أنه لا خلف لها في ستر العورة وللوضوء خلف في التطهير وهو التيمم. وهذا كله في حالة الاختيار، وأما في حالة الضرورة فيتحرى للشرب اتفاقا كذا في شرح المجمع قبيل التيمم. وينبغي أن يلحق بمسألة الأواني الثوب المنسوج لحمته من حرير وغيره، فيحلّ إن كان الحرير أقل وزنًا أو استويا بخلاف ما إذا زاد وزنا ولم أره الآن. وفي الخلاصة من التحرّي في كتاب الصلاة : لو اختلطت أوانيه بأواني أصحابه في السفر وهم غيب أو اختلط رغيفه بأرغفة غيره. قال بعضهم يتحرى، وقال بعضهم لا يتحرى ويتربص حتى يجيء أصحابه وهذا في حالة الاختيار وأما في حالة الاضطرار جاز التحرّي مطلقا. (انتهى). وقد جوّز أصحابنا رحمهم الله مس كتب التفسير للمحدث ولم يفصلوا بين كون الأكثر تفسيرًا أو قرآنا ولو قيل به اعتبارًا للغالب لكان حسنًا. الرابعة : لو سقى شاة خمرًا ثم ذبحها من ساعته فإنها تحلّ بلا كراهة كذا في البزازية ومقتضى القاعدة التحريم، ومقتضى الفرع أنه لو علفها علفا حراما، لم يحرم لبنها ولحمها وإن كان الورع الترك، ثم قال في البزازية بعده ولو بعد ساعة إلى يوم تحلّ مع الكراهة. (انتهى). الخامسة : أن يكون الحرام مستهلكا فلو أكل المحرم شيئا قد استهلك فيه الطيب فلا فدية. وقد أوضحناه في شرح الكنز في جنابات الإحرام. السادسة : إذا اختلط مائع طاهر بماء مطلق فالعبرة للغالب، فإن غلب الماء جازت الطهارة به وإلا فلا وبيَّنا في الطهارات من شرح الكنز بماذا تعتبر الغلبة . السابعة : لو اختلط لبن المرأة بماء أو بدواء أو بلبن شاة فالمعتبر الغالب وتثبت الحرمة إذا استويا احتياطا كما في الغاية. واختلف فيما إذا اختلط لبن امرأة بلبن أخرى والصحيح ثبوت الحرمة فيهما من غير اعتبار الغلبة كما بيناه في الرضاع. الثامنة : إذا كان غالب مال المهدي حلالاً، فلا بأس بقبول هديته وأكل ماله ما لم يتبيَّن أنه من حرام وإن كان غالب ماله الحرام لا يقبلها ولا يأكل إلا إذا قال إنه حلال ورثه أو استقرضه قال الحلواني : وكان الإمام أبو القاسم الحاكم يأخذ جوائز السلطان، والحيلة فيه أن يشتري شيئًا بمال مطلق ثم ينقده من أي مال شاء كذا رواه الثاني عن الإمام وعن الإمام أن المبتلى بطعام السلطان والظلمة يتحرى فإن وقع في قلبه حلّه قبل وأكل وإلا لا لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : «استفتِ قلبك . . . .» الحديث (۱) ، وجواب الإمام فيمن فيه ورع وصفاء قلب ينظر بنور الله تعالى ويدرك بالفراسة كذا في البزازية من الكراهة . التاسعة : إذا اختلطت حمامة المملوك بغير المملوك فظاهر كلامهم أنه لا تحرم وإنما تُكره قال في البزازية من اللقطة اتخذ برج حمام في قرية فينبغي : أن يحفظها ويعلفها ولا يتركها بلا علف كيلا يتضرر الناس فإن اختلط حمام غير صاحبها لا ينبغي له أن يأخذها ولو أخذها طلب صاحبها كالضالة إلى آخر ما فيها .
Among them: if his wife is mixed with other women, he may not have intercourse with her, nor by ijtihad, whether they are limited or not, as our scholars mentioned in the chapter on ambiguous divorce. They said: if he divorces one of his two wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden before specification, and for this reason, intercourse with one of them is a specification for the divorce of the other. Among its forms: if he accepts Islam while having more than four wives, then intercourse is forbidden before choice, according to the one who gave him the choice, which is Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them. As for the two shaykhs, they said that the marriage is invalidated. It is stated in al-Majma' in the chapter on the marriage of the disbeliever: if he accepts Islam while having five, or two sisters, or a mother and daughter, the marriage is invalidated; if he arranged them, then the last one [is invalidated], and he is given the choice to choose four absolutely or one of the two sisters and the daughter or the mother... (end). Among them: if he shoots at game and it falls into water, or on a roof, or a mountain, then rolls down from it to the ground, it is forbidden due to probability and precaution; contrary to when it falls on the ground initially, for it is permissible because it is impossible to avoid it, so its consideration is dropped. And arising from this rule are issues: First: one whose one parent is a People of the Book and the other is a Magian: his marriage and slaughter are permissible and he is considered a Kitabi; this necessitates that he be considered a Magian, and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said the same. If the Kitabi is the father, according to the more apparent view of his, he is given precedence to the side of prohibition. But our scholars abandoned that out of consideration for the minor, for the Magian is worse than the Kitabi, so the child is not made a follower of him. Second: ijtihad regarding vessels: if some are pure and some impure, and the minority is impure, then ijtihad is permissible and he pours out what he thinks is impure, even though the precaution is that he pours out all and performs tayammum, just as if the minority is pure, acting according to the majority in both. Third: ijtihad regarding mixed clothes, some impure and some pure, is permissible, whether the majority is impure or not; the difference between clothes and vessels is that clothes have no substitute for covering the awrah, while for wudu there is a substitute for purification which is tayammum. All this is in the state of choice, but in the state of necessity, he performs ijtihad for drinking by agreement, as in Sharh al-Majma' before tayammum. It should be attached to the issue of vessels: a cloth woven with silk weft and other material: it is permissible if the silk is lesser in weight or equal, contrary to when it exceeds in weight, and I have not seen it now. And in al-Khulasa on ijtihad in the Book of Prayer: if his vessels are mixed with those of his companions while traveling and they are absent, or his loaf is mixed with loaves of others. Some said: he performs ijtihad; some said: he does not perform ijtihad and waits until his companions come. This is in the state of choice; in the state of necessity, ijtihad is absolutely permissible. (end). Our scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, permitted touching books of tafsir for a person in a state of hadath, and they did not differentiate whether the majority is tafsir or Qur'an; if it were said that consideration is given to the majority, it would be good. Fourth: if he gives wine to a sheep and then slaughters it immediately, it is permissible without dislike, as in al-Bazzaziyya. The implication of the rule is prohibition, and the implication of the branch is that if he feeds it forbidden fodder, its milk and meat are not forbidden, though wara' is to leave it. Then al-Bazzaziyya said after it: if after an hour up to a day, it is permissible with dislike. (end). Fifth: that the forbidden be consumed; so if a pilgrim in ihram eats something in which perfume has been consumed, there is no fidyah. We have explained it in Sharh al-Kanz in the chapter on violations of ihram. Sixth: if a pure liquid is mixed with absolute water, consideration is given to the majority; if water predominates, purification with it is permissible, otherwise not. We have explained in the chapter on purifications from Sharh al-Kanz how the predominance is considered. Seventh: if a woman's milk is mixed with water, or medicine, or ewe's milk, then the majority is considered, and the prohibition is established if they are equal as a precaution, as in al-Ghaya. There is difference of opinion regarding when a woman's milk is mixed with another woman's milk; the correct view is that prohibition is established in both without considering predominance, as we have explained in the chapter on rada'. Eighth: if the majority of the gift-giver's wealth is permissible, there is no harm in accepting his gift and eating his wealth as long as it is not known to be unlawful; if the majority of his wealth is unlawful, he should not accept nor eat unless he says it is permissible from inheritance or a loan. Al-Halwani said: Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim used to accept the gifts of the sultan, and the legal stratagem is that he buys something with absolute money then pays it from any money he wishes, as narrated from the Imam. And from the Imam: one who is afflicted with the food of the sultan and oppressors performs ijtihad; if his heart determines it is permissible, he accepts and eats, otherwise not, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Ask your heart...' the hadith. The response of the Imam is regarding one who has piety and purity of heart, who sees by the light of Allah and perceives through intuition, as in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on dislike. Ninth: if a owned pigeon is mixed with non-owned pigeons, then apparent from their words is that it is not forbidden, only disliked. It is said in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on luqta: if he sets up a dovecote in a village, he should keep them and feed them and not leave them without food so that people are not harmed. If pigeons of someone else are mixed, he should not take them; if he takes them, he seeks their owner like a lost item, etc.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the legal maxim: 'When a preventive factor (mani') and a permissive factor (muqtada) conflict, the preventive takes precedence as a precaution (ihtiyat).' The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents numerous applications from various chapters of fiqh to illustrate how this principle operates and where exceptions arise due to impossibility or necessity. The passage begins with the scenario of a man whose wife is mixed with other women: he cannot have intercourse even by ijtihad, because the probability of error is precluded by precaution. Similarly, if a man divorces one of his wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden until specification. In the case of a convert with more than four wives, according to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, he must choose and cannot have intercourse before that, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the marriages are invalidated outright. The ruling on game that falls into water and then rolls down: it is forbidden due to doubt, unlike if it falls directly on the ground because avoidance is impossible. Then nine specific exceptions or applications are listed: (1) a child of mixed parents (Kitabi and Magian) is considered Kitabi in Hanafi school, contrary to what the precautionary reasoning would suggest; (2) ijtihad in impure vessels is allowed when the minority is impure, though precaution would require discarding all; (3) ijtihad in mixed clothes is allowed even if the majority is impure, unlike vessels, because clothes have no substitute; (4) a sheep given wine and immediately slaughtered: permissible without dislike, though the rule would suggest prohibition; (5) consumption of a prohibited substance that has been fully absorbed: no penalty for a pilgrim; (6) mixing of pure liquid with absolute water: the majority rules; (7) mixing of milk: if equal, prohibition applies as precaution; (8) accepting gifts from one whose wealth is mostly permissible; if mostly unlawful, ijtihad is required; (9) mixed pigeons: not forbidden, only disliked. The passage emphasizes that the maxim is applied flexibly, with the underlying rationale of human incapacity to avoid certain situations (la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu).

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Ijtihad based on probability when certainty is impossible; acting on the stronger presumption.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyāt): Choosing the safer option that avoids potential prohibition.
المانع (al-māni'): A legal preventive factor that prohibits an action due to uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hunter shoots at game, which falls onto a mountain and then rolls down to the ground. According to the Hanafi maxim, what is the ruling?
A) Permissible, because it fell on the ground.
B) Forbidden, because there is doubt about the cause of death.
C) Permissible if the hunter performs ijtihad.
D) Forbidden only if the game landed in water.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'precaution takes precedence' governs cases of uncertainty, but is dropped when avoidance is impossible.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Exceptions to the Precaution Maxim: Impossibility and Consideration
Listing exceptions where precaution is dropped due to impossibility, welfare, or necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three numbered exceptions to the precaution maxim from the passage and explain the rationale for each: impossibility, consideration for the minor, and substitute for covering awrah.

Core Idea
Precaution yields to impossibility, welfare of the minor, and necessity of covering the awrah.

After establishing the maxim, Ibn Nujaym lists issues that seem to contradict it. These are not contradictions but instances where the maxim's own exception—'la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu'—or other considerations override the default precaution. This lesson examines the first three exceptions: a child of mixed parents, ijtihad in impure vessels, and ijtihad in mixed clothes.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the first exception: child of mixed parents
One parent is Kitabi, the other Magian. Precaution would suggest following the stricter parent (Magian), but Hanafis consider the child Kitabi out of consideration for the minor.
The opposite school (Shafi'i) follows the father if he is Kitabi.
2
Analyze the second exception: ijtihad in vessels
If some vessels are impure and some pure, and the minority is impure, ijtihad is allowed. Precaution would require discarding all and using tayammum, but this is not required.
When the minority is pure, the majority rule applies.
3
Analyze the third exception: ijtihad in mixed clothes
If some clothes are impure and some pure, ijtihad is allowed even if the majority is impure, unlike vessels. Reason: clothes have no substitute for covering the awrah, whereas wudu can be substituted with tayammum.
This distinction is based on the existence of a substitute (khalaf).
4
Identify the underlying principle
The common thread: when avoidance is impossible or leads to hardship (no substitute), precaution is dropped. In the child case, the consideration of the minor's welfare overrides strict precaution.
This is the dabt: 'la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu'.

ومنها لو اختلطت زوجته بغيرها فليس له الوطء ولا بالتحري سواء كنَّ محصورات أو لا، كما ذكره أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى في الطلاق المبهم وقالوا لو طلق إحدى زوجتيه مبهما حرم الوطء قبل التعيين ولهذا كان وطء أحديهما تعيينا لطلاق الأخرى. ومن صورها ما لو أسلم على أكثر من أربع فإنه يحرم عليه الوطء قبل الاختيار، على قول من خيَّره وهو محمد والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى. وأما الشيخان فقالا يبطلان النكاح. قال في المجمع من فصل نكاح الكافر: لو أسلم وتحته خمس، أو أختان أو أم وبنت بطل النكاح وإن رتَّب فالأخير، وخيره في اختيار أربع مطلقا أو إحدى الأختين والبنت أو الأم . .(انتهى) . ومنها لو رمى صيدا فوقع في ماء أو على سطح أو جبل ثم تردَّى منه إلى الأرض حرم للاحتمال والاحتياط الحرمة بخلاف ما إذا وقع على الأرض ابتداء فإنه يحلّ لأنه لا يمكن التحرّز عنه فسقط اعتباره وخرجت عن هذه القاعدة مسائل : الأولى : من أحد أبويه كتابي والآخر مجوسي فإنه يحلّ نكاحه وذبيحته ويجعل كتابيا وهو يقتضي أن يجعل مجوسيا وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى، ولو كان الكتابي الأب في الأظهر عنده تغليبًا لجانب التحريم. لكن أصحابنا تركوا ذلك نظرًا للصغير، فإن المجوسي شرٌّ من الكتابي فلا يجعل الولد تابعا له . الثانية : الاجتهاد في الأواني إذا كان بعضها طاهرا وبعضها نجسا والأقل نجس فالتحرّي جائز ويريق ما غلب على ظنه أنه نجس، مع أن الاحتياط أنه يريق الكل ويتيمم كما إذا كان الأقل طاهرا عملاً بالأغلب فيهما. الثالثة : الاجتهاد في ثياب مختلطة بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر جائز سواء كان الأكثر نجسا أو لا والفرق بين الثياب والأواني أنه لا خلف لها في ستر العورة وللوضوء خلف في التطهير وهو التيمم. وهذا كله في حالة الاختيار، وأما في حالة الضرورة فيتحرى للشرب اتفاقا كذا في شرح المجمع قبيل التيمم. وينبغي أن يلحق بمسألة الأواني الثوب المنسوج لحمته من حرير وغيره، فيحلّ إن كان الحرير أقل وزنًا أو استويا بخلاف ما إذا زاد وزنا ولم أره الآن. وفي الخلاصة من التحرّي في كتاب الصلاة : لو اختلطت أوانيه بأواني أصحابه في السفر وهم غيب أو اختلط رغيفه بأرغفة غيره. قال بعضهم يتحرى، وقال بعضهم لا يتحرى ويتربص حتى يجيء أصحابه وهذا في حالة الاختيار وأما في حالة الاضطرار جاز التحرّي مطلقا. (انتهى). وقد جوّز أصحابنا رحمهم الله مس كتب التفسير للمحدث ولم يفصلوا بين كون الأكثر تفسيرًا أو قرآنا ولو قيل به اعتبارًا للغالب لكان حسنًا. الرابعة : لو سقى شاة خمرًا ثم ذبحها من ساعته فإنها تحلّ بلا كراهة كذا في البزازية ومقتضى القاعدة التحريم، ومقتضى الفرع أنه لو علفها علفا حراما، لم يحرم لبنها ولحمها وإن كان الورع الترك، ثم قال في البزازية بعده ولو بعد ساعة إلى يوم تحلّ مع الكراهة. (انتهى). الخامسة : أن يكون الحرام مستهلكا فلو أكل المحرم شيئا قد استهلك فيه الطيب فلا فدية. وقد أوضحناه في شرح الكنز في جنابات الإحرام. السادسة : إذا اختلط مائع طاهر بماء مطلق فالعبرة للغالب، فإن غلب الماء جازت الطهارة به وإلا فلا وبيَّنا في الطهارات من شرح الكنز بماذا تعتبر الغلبة . السابعة : لو اختلط لبن المرأة بماء أو بدواء أو بلبن شاة فالمعتبر الغالب وتثبت الحرمة إذا استويا احتياطا كما في الغاية. واختلف فيما إذا اختلط لبن امرأة بلبن أخرى والصحيح ثبوت الحرمة فيهما من غير اعتبار الغلبة كما بيناه في الرضاع. الثامنة : إذا كان غالب مال المهدي حلالاً، فلا بأس بقبول هديته وأكل ماله ما لم يتبيَّن أنه من حرام وإن كان غالب ماله الحرام لا يقبلها ولا يأكل إلا إذا قال إنه حلال ورثه أو استقرضه قال الحلواني : وكان الإمام أبو القاسم الحاكم يأخذ جوائز السلطان، والحيلة فيه أن يشتري شيئًا بمال مطلق ثم ينقده من أي مال شاء كذا رواه الثاني عن الإمام وعن الإمام أن المبتلى بطعام السلطان والظلمة يتحرى فإن وقع في قلبه حلّه قبل وأكل وإلا لا لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : «استفتِ قلبك . . . .» الحديث (۱) ، وجواب الإمام فيمن فيه ورع وصفاء قلب ينظر بنور الله تعالى ويدرك بالفراسة كذا في البزازية من الكراهة . التاسعة : إذا اختلطت حمامة المملوك بغير المملوك فظاهر كلامهم أنه لا تحرم وإنما تُكره قال في البزازية من اللقطة اتخذ برج حمام في قرية فينبغي : أن يحفظها ويعلفها ولا يتركها بلا علف كيلا يتضرر الناس فإن اختلط حمام غير صاحبها لا ينبغي له أن يأخذها ولو أخذها طلب صاحبها كالضالة إلى آخر ما فيها .
Among them: if his wife is mixed with other women, he may not have intercourse with her, nor by ijtihad, whether they are limited or not, as our scholars mentioned in the chapter on ambiguous divorce. They said: if he divorces one of his two wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden before specification, and for this reason, intercourse with one of them is a specification for the divorce of the other. Among its forms: if he accepts Islam while having more than four wives, then intercourse is forbidden before choice, according to the one who gave him the choice, which is Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them. As for the two shaykhs, they said that the marriage is invalidated. It is stated in al-Majma' in the chapter on the marriage of the disbeliever: if he accepts Islam while having five, or two sisters, or a mother and daughter, the marriage is invalidated; if he arranged them, then the last one [is invalidated], and he is given the choice to choose four absolutely or one of the two sisters and the daughter or the mother... (end). Among them: if he shoots at game and it falls into water, or on a roof, or a mountain, then rolls down from it to the ground, it is forbidden due to probability and precaution; contrary to when it falls on the ground initially, for it is permissible because it is impossible to avoid it, so its consideration is dropped. And arising from this rule are issues: First: one whose one parent is a People of the Book and the other is a Magian: his marriage and slaughter are permissible and he is considered a Kitabi; this necessitates that he be considered a Magian, and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said the same. If the Kitabi is the father, according to the more apparent view of his, he is given precedence to the side of prohibition. But our scholars abandoned that out of consideration for the minor, for the Magian is worse than the Kitabi, so the child is not made a follower of him. Second: ijtihad regarding vessels: if some are pure and some impure, and the minority is impure, then ijtihad is permissible and he pours out what he thinks is impure, even though the precaution is that he pours out all and performs tayammum, just as if the minority is pure, acting according to the majority in both. Third: ijtihad regarding mixed clothes, some impure and some pure, is permissible, whether the majority is impure or not; the difference between clothes and vessels is that clothes have no substitute for covering the awrah, while for wudu there is a substitute for purification which is tayammum. All this is in the state of choice, but in the state of necessity, he performs ijtihad for drinking by agreement, as in Sharh al-Majma' before tayammum. It should be attached to the issue of vessels: a cloth woven with silk weft and other material: it is permissible if the silk is lesser in weight or equal, contrary to when it exceeds in weight, and I have not seen it now. And in al-Khulasa on ijtihad in the Book of Prayer: if his vessels are mixed with those of his companions while traveling and they are absent, or his loaf is mixed with loaves of others. Some said: he performs ijtihad; some said: he does not perform ijtihad and waits until his companions come. This is in the state of choice; in the state of necessity, ijtihad is absolutely permissible. (end). Our scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, permitted touching books of tafsir for a person in a state of hadath, and they did not differentiate whether the majority is tafsir or Qur'an; if it were said that consideration is given to the majority, it would be good. Fourth: if he gives wine to a sheep and then slaughters it immediately, it is permissible without dislike, as in al-Bazzaziyya. The implication of the rule is prohibition, and the implication of the branch is that if he feeds it forbidden fodder, its milk and meat are not forbidden, though wara' is to leave it. Then al-Bazzaziyya said after it: if after an hour up to a day, it is permissible with dislike. (end). Fifth: that the forbidden be consumed; so if a pilgrim in ihram eats something in which perfume has been consumed, there is no fidyah. We have explained it in Sharh al-Kanz in the chapter on violations of ihram. Sixth: if a pure liquid is mixed with absolute water, consideration is given to the majority; if water predominates, purification with it is permissible, otherwise not. We have explained in the chapter on purifications from Sharh al-Kanz how the predominance is considered. Seventh: if a woman's milk is mixed with water, or medicine, or ewe's milk, then the majority is considered, and the prohibition is established if they are equal as a precaution, as in al-Ghaya. There is difference of opinion regarding when a woman's milk is mixed with another woman's milk; the correct view is that prohibition is established in both without considering predominance, as we have explained in the chapter on rada'. Eighth: if the majority of the gift-giver's wealth is permissible, there is no harm in accepting his gift and eating his wealth as long as it is not known to be unlawful; if the majority of his wealth is unlawful, he should not accept nor eat unless he says it is permissible from inheritance or a loan. Al-Halwani said: Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim used to accept the gifts of the sultan, and the legal stratagem is that he buys something with absolute money then pays it from any money he wishes, as narrated from the Imam. And from the Imam: one who is afflicted with the food of the sultan and oppressors performs ijtihad; if his heart determines it is permissible, he accepts and eats, otherwise not, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Ask your heart...' the hadith. The response of the Imam is regarding one who has piety and purity of heart, who sees by the light of Allah and perceives through intuition, as in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on dislike. Ninth: if a owned pigeon is mixed with non-owned pigeons, then apparent from their words is that it is not forbidden, only disliked. It is said in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on luqta: if he sets up a dovecote in a village, he should keep them and feed them and not leave them without food so that people are not harmed. If pigeons of someone else are mixed, he should not take them; if he takes them, he seeks their owner like a lost item, etc.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the legal maxim: 'When a preventive factor (mani') and a permissive factor (muqtada) conflict, the preventive takes precedence as a precaution (ihtiyat).' The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents numerous applications from various chapters of fiqh to illustrate how this principle operates and where exceptions arise due to impossibility or necessity. The passage begins with the scenario of a man whose wife is mixed with other women: he cannot have intercourse even by ijtihad, because the probability of error is precluded by precaution. Similarly, if a man divorces one of his wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden until specification. In the case of a convert with more than four wives, according to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, he must choose and cannot have intercourse before that, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the marriages are invalidated outright. The ruling on game that falls into water and then rolls down: it is forbidden due to doubt, unlike if it falls directly on the ground because avoidance is impossible. Then nine specific exceptions or applications are listed: (1) a child of mixed parents (Kitabi and Magian) is considered Kitabi in Hanafi school, contrary to what the precautionary reasoning would suggest; (2) ijtihad in impure vessels is allowed when the minority is impure, though precaution would require discarding all; (3) ijtihad in mixed clothes is allowed even if the majority is impure, unlike vessels, because clothes have no substitute; (4) a sheep given wine and immediately slaughtered: permissible without dislike, though the rule would suggest prohibition; (5) consumption of a prohibited substance that has been fully absorbed: no penalty for a pilgrim; (6) mixing of pure liquid with absolute water: the majority rules; (7) mixing of milk: if equal, prohibition applies as precaution; (8) accepting gifts from one whose wealth is mostly permissible; if mostly unlawful, ijtihad is required; (9) mixed pigeons: not forbidden, only disliked. The passage emphasizes that the maxim is applied flexibly, with the underlying rationale of human incapacity to avoid certain situations (la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu).

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Ijtihad based on probability when certainty is impossible; acting on the stronger presumption.
الخلف (al-khalaf): A substitute alternative that can replace an obligatory act when the original is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ijtihad allowed in mixed clothes even if the majority is impure, but not in vessels if the majority is impure?
A) Because clothes are more important than vessels.
B) Because clothes have no substitute for covering the awrah, whereas wudu has tayammum as a substitute.
C) Because the impurity in clothes is less severe.
D) Because the majority rule does not apply to clothes.

Key Takeaway
Exceptions to the precaution maxim arise when avoidance is impossible, when welfare of a minor is involved, or when there is no substitute for a necessary act.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Further Applications of the Precaution Maxim in Fiqh
Further applications of the maxim in diverse fiqh chapters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the precaution maxim to six additional furuat: sheep fed wine, pilgrim consuming perfume, mixing liquids, mixing milk, gifts from mixed wealth, and mixed pigeons.

Core Idea
The maxim of precaution yields to the majority or necessity in cases of consumed impurities, mixed liquids, and gifts from mixed wealth.

Ibn Nujaym continues listing applications of the precaution maxim, now focusing on cases where the preventive factor (doubt) is overridden by considerations of majority, consumption, or practicality. These cases are numbered four to nine in the original text. They cover diverse areas: permissible slaughter after wine consumption, pilgrim's exemption from fidyah, predominance in mixed liquids, milk mixing, gifts from mixed wealth, and mixed pigeons.

Guided Path
1
Examine the fourth issue: sheep fed wine
A sheep is given wine and slaughtered immediately: it is permissible without dislike. If slaughtered after an hour, it is permissible with dislike. The precaution maxim would suggest prohibition, but here the immediate slaughter renders the wine effectively non-existent.
The underlying rule: if the forbidden substance is consumed before it can affect the animal, it is overlooked.
2
Analyze the fifth issue: pilgrim consuming perfume
A pilgrim in ihram eats food in which perfume has been fully absorbed (mustahlik). There is no fidyah (expiation). The precaution would require fidyah, but because the perfume is consumed, the prohibition is dropped.
The concept of 'istihlak' (complete consumption) removes the preventive factor.
3
Analyze the sixth and seventh issues: mixing liquids and milk
Sixth: If a pure liquid (e.g., water mixed with milk?) Actually the sixth: pure liquid mixed with absolute water: the majority governs. Seventh: a woman's milk mixed with water or medicine: the majority governs; if equal, prohibition applies as precaution. For mixing of two women's milk, the correct view is that prohibition is established in both without considering majority.
The milk case of two women is different: both are potentially breastfeeding, so precaution establishes prohibition in both.
4
Analyze the eighth issue: gifts from mixed wealth
If the majority of the gift-giver's wealth is permissible, accepting gifts is fine. If the majority is unlawful, one should not accept unless the donor says it is from a permissible source. There is also a discussion about accepting gifts from rulers and the legal stratagem (hila).
The precaution maxim would suggest rejecting all gifts, but practical need and possibility of ijtihad allow acceptance.
5
Analyze the ninth issue: mixed pigeons
If a owned pigeon is mixed with non-owned pigeons, it is not forbidden to take the mixed pigeons, only disliked. The owner should seek the owner of the non-owned ones, like lost property.
The maxim is overridden by the difficulty of identification; only dislike (karahah) remains.

ومنها لو اختلطت زوجته بغيرها فليس له الوطء ولا بالتحري سواء كنَّ محصورات أو لا، كما ذكره أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى في الطلاق المبهم وقالوا لو طلق إحدى زوجتيه مبهما حرم الوطء قبل التعيين ولهذا كان وطء أحديهما تعيينا لطلاق الأخرى. ومن صورها ما لو أسلم على أكثر من أربع فإنه يحرم عليه الوطء قبل الاختيار، على قول من خيَّره وهو محمد والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى. وأما الشيخان فقالا يبطلان النكاح. قال في المجمع من فصل نكاح الكافر: لو أسلم وتحته خمس، أو أختان أو أم وبنت بطل النكاح وإن رتَّب فالأخير، وخيره في اختيار أربع مطلقا أو إحدى الأختين والبنت أو الأم . .(انتهى) . ومنها لو رمى صيدا فوقع في ماء أو على سطح أو جبل ثم تردَّى منه إلى الأرض حرم للاحتمال والاحتياط الحرمة بخلاف ما إذا وقع على الأرض ابتداء فإنه يحلّ لأنه لا يمكن التحرّز عنه فسقط اعتباره وخرجت عن هذه القاعدة مسائل : الأولى : من أحد أبويه كتابي والآخر مجوسي فإنه يحلّ نكاحه وذبيحته ويجعل كتابيا وهو يقتضي أن يجعل مجوسيا وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى، ولو كان الكتابي الأب في الأظهر عنده تغليبًا لجانب التحريم. لكن أصحابنا تركوا ذلك نظرًا للصغير، فإن المجوسي شرٌّ من الكتابي فلا يجعل الولد تابعا له . الثانية : الاجتهاد في الأواني إذا كان بعضها طاهرا وبعضها نجسا والأقل نجس فالتحرّي جائز ويريق ما غلب على ظنه أنه نجس، مع أن الاحتياط أنه يريق الكل ويتيمم كما إذا كان الأقل طاهرا عملاً بالأغلب فيهما. الثالثة : الاجتهاد في ثياب مختلطة بعضها نجس وبعضها طاهر جائز سواء كان الأكثر نجسا أو لا والفرق بين الثياب والأواني أنه لا خلف لها في ستر العورة وللوضوء خلف في التطهير وهو التيمم. وهذا كله في حالة الاختيار، وأما في حالة الضرورة فيتحرى للشرب اتفاقا كذا في شرح المجمع قبيل التيمم. وينبغي أن يلحق بمسألة الأواني الثوب المنسوج لحمته من حرير وغيره، فيحلّ إن كان الحرير أقل وزنًا أو استويا بخلاف ما إذا زاد وزنا ولم أره الآن. وفي الخلاصة من التحرّي في كتاب الصلاة : لو اختلطت أوانيه بأواني أصحابه في السفر وهم غيب أو اختلط رغيفه بأرغفة غيره. قال بعضهم يتحرى، وقال بعضهم لا يتحرى ويتربص حتى يجيء أصحابه وهذا في حالة الاختيار وأما في حالة الاضطرار جاز التحرّي مطلقا. (انتهى). وقد جوّز أصحابنا رحمهم الله مس كتب التفسير للمحدث ولم يفصلوا بين كون الأكثر تفسيرًا أو قرآنا ولو قيل به اعتبارًا للغالب لكان حسنًا. الرابعة : لو سقى شاة خمرًا ثم ذبحها من ساعته فإنها تحلّ بلا كراهة كذا في البزازية ومقتضى القاعدة التحريم، ومقتضى الفرع أنه لو علفها علفا حراما، لم يحرم لبنها ولحمها وإن كان الورع الترك، ثم قال في البزازية بعده ولو بعد ساعة إلى يوم تحلّ مع الكراهة. (انتهى). الخامسة : أن يكون الحرام مستهلكا فلو أكل المحرم شيئا قد استهلك فيه الطيب فلا فدية. وقد أوضحناه في شرح الكنز في جنابات الإحرام. السادسة : إذا اختلط مائع طاهر بماء مطلق فالعبرة للغالب، فإن غلب الماء جازت الطهارة به وإلا فلا وبيَّنا في الطهارات من شرح الكنز بماذا تعتبر الغلبة . السابعة : لو اختلط لبن المرأة بماء أو بدواء أو بلبن شاة فالمعتبر الغالب وتثبت الحرمة إذا استويا احتياطا كما في الغاية. واختلف فيما إذا اختلط لبن امرأة بلبن أخرى والصحيح ثبوت الحرمة فيهما من غير اعتبار الغلبة كما بيناه في الرضاع. الثامنة : إذا كان غالب مال المهدي حلالاً، فلا بأس بقبول هديته وأكل ماله ما لم يتبيَّن أنه من حرام وإن كان غالب ماله الحرام لا يقبلها ولا يأكل إلا إذا قال إنه حلال ورثه أو استقرضه قال الحلواني : وكان الإمام أبو القاسم الحاكم يأخذ جوائز السلطان، والحيلة فيه أن يشتري شيئًا بمال مطلق ثم ينقده من أي مال شاء كذا رواه الثاني عن الإمام وعن الإمام أن المبتلى بطعام السلطان والظلمة يتحرى فإن وقع في قلبه حلّه قبل وأكل وإلا لا لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : «استفتِ قلبك . . . .» الحديث (۱) ، وجواب الإمام فيمن فيه ورع وصفاء قلب ينظر بنور الله تعالى ويدرك بالفراسة كذا في البزازية من الكراهة . التاسعة : إذا اختلطت حمامة المملوك بغير المملوك فظاهر كلامهم أنه لا تحرم وإنما تُكره قال في البزازية من اللقطة اتخذ برج حمام في قرية فينبغي : أن يحفظها ويعلفها ولا يتركها بلا علف كيلا يتضرر الناس فإن اختلط حمام غير صاحبها لا ينبغي له أن يأخذها ولو أخذها طلب صاحبها كالضالة إلى آخر ما فيها .
Among them: if his wife is mixed with other women, he may not have intercourse with her, nor by ijtihad, whether they are limited or not, as our scholars mentioned in the chapter on ambiguous divorce. They said: if he divorces one of his two wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden before specification, and for this reason, intercourse with one of them is a specification for the divorce of the other. Among its forms: if he accepts Islam while having more than four wives, then intercourse is forbidden before choice, according to the one who gave him the choice, which is Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them. As for the two shaykhs, they said that the marriage is invalidated. It is stated in al-Majma' in the chapter on the marriage of the disbeliever: if he accepts Islam while having five, or two sisters, or a mother and daughter, the marriage is invalidated; if he arranged them, then the last one [is invalidated], and he is given the choice to choose four absolutely or one of the two sisters and the daughter or the mother... (end). Among them: if he shoots at game and it falls into water, or on a roof, or a mountain, then rolls down from it to the ground, it is forbidden due to probability and precaution; contrary to when it falls on the ground initially, for it is permissible because it is impossible to avoid it, so its consideration is dropped. And arising from this rule are issues: First: one whose one parent is a People of the Book and the other is a Magian: his marriage and slaughter are permissible and he is considered a Kitabi; this necessitates that he be considered a Magian, and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said the same. If the Kitabi is the father, according to the more apparent view of his, he is given precedence to the side of prohibition. But our scholars abandoned that out of consideration for the minor, for the Magian is worse than the Kitabi, so the child is not made a follower of him. Second: ijtihad regarding vessels: if some are pure and some impure, and the minority is impure, then ijtihad is permissible and he pours out what he thinks is impure, even though the precaution is that he pours out all and performs tayammum, just as if the minority is pure, acting according to the majority in both. Third: ijtihad regarding mixed clothes, some impure and some pure, is permissible, whether the majority is impure or not; the difference between clothes and vessels is that clothes have no substitute for covering the awrah, while for wudu there is a substitute for purification which is tayammum. All this is in the state of choice, but in the state of necessity, he performs ijtihad for drinking by agreement, as in Sharh al-Majma' before tayammum. It should be attached to the issue of vessels: a cloth woven with silk weft and other material: it is permissible if the silk is lesser in weight or equal, contrary to when it exceeds in weight, and I have not seen it now. And in al-Khulasa on ijtihad in the Book of Prayer: if his vessels are mixed with those of his companions while traveling and they are absent, or his loaf is mixed with loaves of others. Some said: he performs ijtihad; some said: he does not perform ijtihad and waits until his companions come. This is in the state of choice; in the state of necessity, ijtihad is absolutely permissible. (end). Our scholars, may Allah have mercy on them, permitted touching books of tafsir for a person in a state of hadath, and they did not differentiate whether the majority is tafsir or Qur'an; if it were said that consideration is given to the majority, it would be good. Fourth: if he gives wine to a sheep and then slaughters it immediately, it is permissible without dislike, as in al-Bazzaziyya. The implication of the rule is prohibition, and the implication of the branch is that if he feeds it forbidden fodder, its milk and meat are not forbidden, though wara' is to leave it. Then al-Bazzaziyya said after it: if after an hour up to a day, it is permissible with dislike. (end). Fifth: that the forbidden be consumed; so if a pilgrim in ihram eats something in which perfume has been consumed, there is no fidyah. We have explained it in Sharh al-Kanz in the chapter on violations of ihram. Sixth: if a pure liquid is mixed with absolute water, consideration is given to the majority; if water predominates, purification with it is permissible, otherwise not. We have explained in the chapter on purifications from Sharh al-Kanz how the predominance is considered. Seventh: if a woman's milk is mixed with water, or medicine, or ewe's milk, then the majority is considered, and the prohibition is established if they are equal as a precaution, as in al-Ghaya. There is difference of opinion regarding when a woman's milk is mixed with another woman's milk; the correct view is that prohibition is established in both without considering predominance, as we have explained in the chapter on rada'. Eighth: if the majority of the gift-giver's wealth is permissible, there is no harm in accepting his gift and eating his wealth as long as it is not known to be unlawful; if the majority of his wealth is unlawful, he should not accept nor eat unless he says it is permissible from inheritance or a loan. Al-Halwani said: Imam Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim used to accept the gifts of the sultan, and the legal stratagem is that he buys something with absolute money then pays it from any money he wishes, as narrated from the Imam. And from the Imam: one who is afflicted with the food of the sultan and oppressors performs ijtihad; if his heart determines it is permissible, he accepts and eats, otherwise not, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Ask your heart...' the hadith. The response of the Imam is regarding one who has piety and purity of heart, who sees by the light of Allah and perceives through intuition, as in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on dislike. Ninth: if a owned pigeon is mixed with non-owned pigeons, then apparent from their words is that it is not forbidden, only disliked. It is said in al-Bazzaziyya in the chapter on luqta: if he sets up a dovecote in a village, he should keep them and feed them and not leave them without food so that people are not harmed. If pigeons of someone else are mixed, he should not take them; if he takes them, he seeks their owner like a lost item, etc.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the legal maxim: 'When a preventive factor (mani') and a permissive factor (muqtada) conflict, the preventive takes precedence as a precaution (ihtiyat).' The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents numerous applications from various chapters of fiqh to illustrate how this principle operates and where exceptions arise due to impossibility or necessity. The passage begins with the scenario of a man whose wife is mixed with other women: he cannot have intercourse even by ijtihad, because the probability of error is precluded by precaution. Similarly, if a man divorces one of his wives ambiguously, intercourse is forbidden until specification. In the case of a convert with more than four wives, according to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, he must choose and cannot have intercourse before that, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the marriages are invalidated outright. The ruling on game that falls into water and then rolls down: it is forbidden due to doubt, unlike if it falls directly on the ground because avoidance is impossible. Then nine specific exceptions or applications are listed: (1) a child of mixed parents (Kitabi and Magian) is considered Kitabi in Hanafi school, contrary to what the precautionary reasoning would suggest; (2) ijtihad in impure vessels is allowed when the minority is impure, though precaution would require discarding all; (3) ijtihad in mixed clothes is allowed even if the majority is impure, unlike vessels, because clothes have no substitute; (4) a sheep given wine and immediately slaughtered: permissible without dislike, though the rule would suggest prohibition; (5) consumption of a prohibited substance that has been fully absorbed: no penalty for a pilgrim; (6) mixing of pure liquid with absolute water: the majority rules; (7) mixing of milk: if equal, prohibition applies as precaution; (8) accepting gifts from one whose wealth is mostly permissible; if mostly unlawful, ijtihad is required; (9) mixed pigeons: not forbidden, only disliked. The passage emphasizes that the maxim is applied flexibly, with the underlying rationale of human incapacity to avoid certain situations (la yumkin al-taharrur 'anhu).

Key Terms
الاستهلاك (al-istihlāk): Complete consumption of a forbidden substance so that it no longer has an effect.
الغالب (al-ghālib): The predominant element in a mixture; used to determine the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the eighth issue, what should a person do if the majority of a gift-giver's wealth is unlawful?
A) Refuse the gift under all circumstances.
B) Accept the gift and perform ijtihad about its source.
C) Accept the gift only if the donor says it is from a permissible source.
D) Accept the gift and give it in charity.

Key Takeaway
The precaution maxim is applied flexibly: consumption, majority, and the possibility of specification can override the default prohibition.
