⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملك، والأصح أنه لا الفساد إلى الملك لأن الوقف مال نعم إذا كان مسجدا يسري عامرًا فهو كالحرّ بخلاف الغامر بالمعجمة أي الخراب فكالمدبر. ومن هذا القبيل ما إذا شرط الخيار فيه أكثر من ثلاثة فإنه لا يصح في الثلاثة ويبطل فيما زاد، بل يبطل في الكل، لكن إذا أسقط الزائد قبل دخوله انقلب البيع صحيحًا .
ومنها ما إذا جمع بين مجهول ومعلوم في البيع فإن كان المجهول لا تُفضي جهالته إلى المنازعة لا يضرّ وإلا فسد في الكل كما علم في البيوع . ومنها الإجارة ؛ فهي كالبيع لاشتراكهما في أنهما يبطلان بالشرط الفاسد وصرَّحوا بأنه لو استأجر دارًا في كل شهر بكذا فإنه يصح في الشهر الأول فقط . ولم أرَ الآن حكم ما إذا استأجر نساجًا لينسج له ثوبًا طوله كذا، وعرضه كذا فخالف بزيادة أو نقصان. هل يستحق بقدره أو لا يستحق أصلا؟ ومنها الكفالة والإبراء وينبغي أن لا يتعدى إلى الجائز. وقالوا لو قال لها ضمنت لك نفقتك كل شهر فإنه يصح في شهر واحد.
ومنها الهبة وهي لا تبطل بالشرط الفاسد فلا يتعدى إلى الجائز .
ومنها الإهداء ؛ قالوا لو أهدي إلى القاضي من له عادة بالإهداء له قبل القضاء وزاد، يردّ القاضي الزائد لا الكل كما في فتح القدير، فلم يتعد إلى الجائز. وظاهر كلامه أنه إن زاد في القدر. وأما إذا زاد في المعنى كما إذا كانت عادته إهداء ثوب كتان فأهدى ثوبا حريرًا لم أره الآن لأصحابنا رحمهم الله. وينبغي وجوب ردّ الكل لا بقدر ما زاد في قيمته لعدم تمييزها من الجائز .
ومنها الوصية ؛ فلو أوصى لأجنبي ووارثه فللأجنبي نصفها وبطلت للوارث؛ كما في الكنز، وكذا لو أوصى للقاتل وللأجنبي.
ومنها الإقرار ؛ قال الزيلعي فيما لو أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه ولأجنبي لم يصح في حق الأجنبي أيضًا. (انتهى). وفي المجمع من الإقرار لو أقر لوارث مع أجنبي فتكاذبا الشركة صححه في الأجنبي. (انتهى) .
ومنها باب الشهادة، فإذا جمع فيها بين مَن تجوز شهادته ومَن لا تجوز؛ ففي الظهيرية منها : رجل مات وأوصى لفقراء جيرانه بشيء وأنكرت الورثة وصيته فشهد على الوصية رجلان من جيرانه لهما أولاد محاويج . قال محمد رحمه الله : لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما شهدا لأولادهما فيما يخص أولادهما فبطلت شهادتهما في ذلك، فإذا بطلت شهادتهما في حق الأولاد بطلت أصلاً لأن الشهادة واحدة، كما لو شهدا على رجل أنه قذف أمتهما وفلانة لا تقبل شهادتهما. وذكر محمد رحمه الله في وقف الأصل؛ إذا وقف على فقراء جيرانه فشهد بذلك فقيران من جيرانه جازت شهادتهما ؛ قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله ما ذكر في الوقف قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله، أما على قياس قول محمد رحمه الله فينبغي ألا تقبل في الوقف أيضًا لأن عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يجوز أن تبطل الشهادة في البعض وتبقى في البعض وعلى قول محمد رحمه الله لا تقبل أصلاً ويحتمل أن ما ذكره في الوقف محمول على ما إذا كانوا قليلين يحصون. (انتهى). وفي القنية : أخ وأخت ادعيا أرضا وشهد زوجها ورجل آخر ترد شهادتهما في حق الأخت والأخ ؛ فإن الشهادة متى ردّ بعضها ترد كلها. وفي روضة الفقهاء إذا شهد لمَن لا تجوز له الشهادة ولغيره لا تجوز لمن لا تجوز له الشهادة بالاتفاق واختلف في حق الآخر فقيل تبطل وقيل لا تبطل. (انتهى).
وكتبنا في شرح الكنز أن شهادة العدو لا تُقبَل إذا كانت لأجل الدنيا؛ سواء كانت على عدوّه أو غيره بناء على أنها فسق وهو لا يتجزى. ومن هذا القبيل اختلاف الشاهدين مانع من قبولها لأن أحدهما طابق الدعوى والآخر خالفها. وكتبنا في الفوائد ذلك . المستثنى من البزازية .
ومنها القضاء ؛ فإذا امتنع القضاء للبعض امتنع للباقين، كما في شهادات
ومنها باب العبادات ؛ فلو نوى صوم جميع الشهر بطل فيما عدا اليوم الأول. وليس منه ما إذا عجل زكاة سنتين فإنه إن كان بعد ملك النصاب فهو صحيح فيهما وإلا فلا فيهما . وليس منه أيضًا ما إذا نوى حجتين وأحرم بهما معا؛ فإنَّا نقول بدخوله فيهما لكن اختلفوا في وقت رفضه لإحديهما كما علم في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وليس منه ما إذا نوى التيمم لفرضين، لأنَّا نقول يجوز له أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل .
ومنها : ما إذا صلى على حي وميت، وينبغي أن تصح على الميت.
ومنها : ما إذا استنجى للبول بحجر ثم نام فاحتلم فأمنى فأصاب ثوبه لم يظهر بالفرك لأن البول لا يطهر به فلا يطهر المني كما صرحوا به، ولهذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله : مسألة المنيّ مشكلة لأن كل فحل يمذي أولاً والمذي لا يطهر بالفرك إلا أن يجعل تبعا له. (انتهى).
And ownership, and the correct opinion is that invalidity does not transfer to ownership because waqf is property. Yes, if it is a mosque, it extends to the inhabited part, so it is like a free person, unlike the ruined (al-ghamir with a jeem, meaning ruin) which is like a mudabbar. Of this type is: if one stipulates an option more than three days, it is not valid for three days and becomes void for the extra, rather it becomes void entirely, but if he drops the extra before it enters, the sale becomes valid. And among them: if one combines an unknown and a known in a sale: if the unknown does not lead to dispute, it does not harm; otherwise the whole is invalidated, as known in sales. And among them: ijarah; it is like a sale in that both are invalidated by a corrupt condition. They explicitly stated that if one rents a house for each month for a certain amount, it is valid only for the first month. I have not seen now the ruling if one hires a weaver to weave a cloth of such length and width and he deviates by increase or decrease: does he deserve payment proportional to it or not at all? And among them: kafalah and ibra'; it should not transfer to the permissible. They said: if he said to her 'I guarantee your maintenance each month,' it is valid for one month. And among them: hibah; it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so it does not transfer to the permissible. And among them: iqra' (giving gifts); they said: if a gift is given to a judge by someone who customarily gave gifts before his judgeship and (the gift) increased, the judge returns the increase, not the whole, as in Fath al-Qadir. So it did not transfer to the permissible. The apparent meaning of his words is if the increase is in quantity. But if the increase is in kind, as if his custom was to gift a linen garment and he gifted a silk one, I have not seen it now from our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). And it should be obligatory to return the whole, not just the amount of increase in value, because it is not distinguishable from the permissible. And among them: wasiyyah; if one bequeaths to a non-relative and to his heir, the non-relative gets half, and (the bequest) is invalid for the heir, as in al-Kanz. Similarly, if one bequeaths to a killer and to a non-relative. And among them: iqrar; al-Zayla'i said: regarding one who acknowledges a specific property or debt to his heir and to a non-relative, it is not valid for the non-relative either. (End). And in al-Majma' from iqrar: if one acknowledges to an heir and a non-relative and they both deny partnership, it is considered valid for the non-relative. (End). And among them: the chapter of testimony: if one combines in it one whose testimony is acceptable and one whose testimony is not acceptable; in al-Zahiriyyah from it: a man died and bequeathed something to poor neighbors and the heirs denied his will. Two men from among the neighbors whose children are needy testified to the will. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: their testimony is not accepted because they testified for their children regarding what pertains to their children, so their testimony in that matter is invalidated, and if their testimony regarding the children is invalidated, it is invalidated entirely because testimony is one. Similarly, if they testify against a man that he slandered their slave woman and (also) a certain woman, their testimony is not accepted. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in Waqf al-Asl: if one made a waqf for poor neighbors and two poor neighbors testified to that, their testimony is valid. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth (may Allah have mercy on him) said: what was mentioned in waqf is the view of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him); but by analogy to Muhammad's (may Allah have mercy on him) view, it should not be accepted in waqf either, because according to Abu Yusuf, it is possible that testimony is invalidated in part and remains in part, whereas according to Muhammad, it is not accepted at all. It is possible that what he mentioned in waqf is interpreted as when they are few enough to be counted. (End). And in al-Qunyah: a brother and sister claimed land, and her husband and another man testified; their testimony is rejected regarding the sister and the brother, because whenever part of testimony is rejected, all of it is rejected. And in Rawdat al-Fuqaha: if one testifies for someone whose testimony is not acceptable and for another, it is not acceptable for the one whose testimony is not acceptable by consensus, but for the other there is disagreement: some say it is invalidated, others say it is not. (End). And we wrote in Sharh al-Kanz that the testimony of an enemy is not accepted if it is for worldly purposes, whether against his enemy or another, based on it being fisq (immorality), which is indivisible. Of this type is the disagreement of two witnesses preventing acceptance, because one conforms to the claim and the other contradicts it. We wrote that in al-Fawa'id. The exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah. And among them: the chapter of qada'; if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest, as in testimonies. And among them: the chapter of worship; if one intends to fast the whole month, it is invalid for days other than the first. Not from this is if one pays zakat early for two years: if it is after owning the nisab, it is valid for both; otherwise it is not valid for either. Nor is it from this if one intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together; we say he enters both, but they differed on the time of abandoning one of them, as known in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram. Nor is it from this if one intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers, because we say he can perform as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes with one tayammum. And among them: if one prays over a living and a dead person; it should be valid for the dead. And among them: if one cleans after urine with a stone and then sleeps, has a wet dream, ejaculates, and it gets on his garment, it does not become pure by rubbing, because urine is not purified by it, so semen is not purified by it either, as they explicitly stated. Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: the issue of semen is problematic because every male first releases madhi, and madhi is not purified by rubbing unless it is made subsidiary to it. (End).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exploration of a central qawida in Hanafi fiqh: When a contract or legal transaction combines both permissible (ja'iz) and impermissible (ghayr ja'iz) elements, does the invalidity of the impermissible part spread to the permissible part? The answer is not uniform; it depends on the nature of the act and the degree of indivisibility. The text follows a sequence of chapters, applying the principle to various contracts and actions.

The discussion begins with waqf: if a waqf is a mosque, the ruling of being 'free' (not owned) applies to the inhabited part, not the ruined part, showing that the ruling does not spread to the whole. Then in sales: a condition of option beyond three days invalidates the entire sale, unless the invalid condition is dropped before it takes effect. Mixing known and unknown items in a sale may or may not invalidate the whole depending on whether the unknown leads to dispute.

In ijarah (hire): it is like sale; a corrupt condition invalidates the whole, e.g., renting a house monthly for a fixed amount is valid only for the first month. The author notes an unresolved case: hiring a weaver with specific dimensions, and he deviates; the author does not find a ruling, indicating doubt.

In kafalah (suretyship) and ibra (discharge): the principle should not transfer to the permissible part. Example: 'I guarantee your monthly maintenance' is valid for one month only.

Hibah (gift): not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so the impermissible does not spread.

In gifts to a judge: if the increase is in quantity, only the increase is returned; if in kind (e.g., silk instead of linen), the author suggests returning the whole because it is not separable.

In wasiyyah (bequest): if made to both a non-heir and an heir, the bequest to the heir is invalid but the non-heir gets half, showing partial invalidity. Similarly for iqrar (acknowledgment): according to al-Zayla'i, if acknowledged to an heir and a non-heir, both are invalid; but another view in al-Majma' validates the non-heir's portion if they deny partnership.

In shahadah (testimony): the key principle is that testimony is indivisible. If it is invalid for one party, it is invalid for all. This is illustrated by cases of testifying for one's own children and for neighbors in waqf. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf allows partial validity in testimony, Muhammad insists on total invalidity. The text also discusses exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah.

In qada' (judgment): if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest (similar to testimony).

In ibadat (worship): intending to fast the whole month is valid only for the first day (since fasting requires separate intentions). But paying zakat early for two years is valid for both if the nisab is owned at the time of payment. Intending two hajj together: the person enters both, but there is disagreement on abandoning one. Tayammum for two obligatory prayers: valid because one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers.

Praying over a living and dead person: valid for the dead.

Cleaning with a stone: if semen touches the garment after istinja, it is not purified by rubbing because the madhi (pre-ejaculate) that precedes it is not purified by rubbing, and semen follows it. This is problematic, but the author points out the difficulty.

Overall, the passage reinforces that the spread of invalidity is not mechanical; it depends on the structure and indivisibility of the legal act.

Key Terms
الجائز (al-ja'iz): The permissible or valid part of a combination.
غير الجائز (ghayr al-ja'iz): The impermissible or invalid part of a combination.
يتعدى (yata'adda): To spread or transfer; the impermissible ruling affecting the permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person rents a house for a monthly payment and includes a corrupt condition?
A) The contract is valid for the entire period.
B) The contract is void ab initio for all months.
C) The contract is valid only for the first month.
D) The contract is valid but the condition is ignored.

Key Takeaway
The spread of invalidity is not automatic; it depends on the indivisibility of the contract and the nature of the impermissible element.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
10 min
Testimony and Acknowledgment: Indivisibility of Statements
Applications of the maxim to testimony and acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of indivisibility of testimony and iqrar in Hanafi law and identify the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Testimony is one statement: if invalid for part, it is invalid for all, except in some cases per Abu Yusuf.

This lesson focuses on the application of the spread of invalidity principle to testimony and acknowledgment. The key debate is whether a single statement can be partially valid. Imam Muhammad holds total indivisibility, while Abu Yusuf allows partial validity in certain contexts. The text presents several case studies, including testimony for one's own children and acknowledgment to an heir and non-heir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testimonial or acknowledgment act
Locate the case: e.g., testimony for poor neighbors where witnesses also benefit, or iqrar to a heir and non-heir.
2
Determine if the act is indivisible
Testimony is a single utterance. If rejected for one part, it is rejected entirely according to Muhammad. Abu Yusuf allows partial rejection.
This is the core ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the ruling according to each Imam
For testimony: if invalid for one party, invalid for all (Muhammad); may be partially valid (Abu Yusuf). For iqrar: total invalidity (al-Zayla'i) or partial validity (al-Majma').
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a real case, the mufti must know which view is relied upon. Later fatwa often follows Abu Yusuf for testimony in waqf cases.

وملك، والأصح أنه لا الفساد إلى الملك لأن الوقف مال نعم إذا كان مسجدا يسري عامرًا فهو كالحرّ بخلاف الغامر بالمعجمة أي الخراب فكالمدبر. ومن هذا القبيل ما إذا شرط الخيار فيه أكثر من ثلاثة فإنه لا يصح في الثلاثة ويبطل فيما زاد، بل يبطل في الكل، لكن إذا أسقط الزائد قبل دخوله انقلب البيع صحيحًا .
ومنها ما إذا جمع بين مجهول ومعلوم في البيع فإن كان المجهول لا تُفضي جهالته إلى المنازعة لا يضرّ وإلا فسد في الكل كما علم في البيوع . ومنها الإجارة ؛ فهي كالبيع لاشتراكهما في أنهما يبطلان بالشرط الفاسد وصرَّحوا بأنه لو استأجر دارًا في كل شهر بكذا فإنه يصح في الشهر الأول فقط . ولم أرَ الآن حكم ما إذا استأجر نساجًا لينسج له ثوبًا طوله كذا، وعرضه كذا فخالف بزيادة أو نقصان. هل يستحق بقدره أو لا يستحق أصلا؟ ومنها الكفالة والإبراء وينبغي أن لا يتعدى إلى الجائز. وقالوا لو قال لها ضمنت لك نفقتك كل شهر فإنه يصح في شهر واحد.
ومنها الهبة وهي لا تبطل بالشرط الفاسد فلا يتعدى إلى الجائز .
ومنها الإهداء ؛ قالوا لو أهدي إلى القاضي من له عادة بالإهداء له قبل القضاء وزاد، يردّ القاضي الزائد لا الكل كما في فتح القدير، فلم يتعد إلى الجائز. وظاهر كلامه أنه إن زاد في القدر. وأما إذا زاد في المعنى كما إذا كانت عادته إهداء ثوب كتان فأهدى ثوبا حريرًا لم أره الآن لأصحابنا رحمهم الله. وينبغي وجوب ردّ الكل لا بقدر ما زاد في قيمته لعدم تمييزها من الجائز .

(انتهى). وفي القنية : أخ وأخت ادعيا أرضا وشهد زوجها ورجل آخر ترد شهادتهما في حق الأخت والأخ ؛ فإن الشهادة متى ردّ بعضها ترد كلها. وفي روضة الفقهاء إذا شهد لمَن لا تجوز له الشهادة ولغيره لا تجوز لمن لا تجوز له الشهادة بالاتفاق واختلف في حق الآخر فقيل تبطل وقيل لا تبطل. (انتهى).
وكتبنا في شرح الكنز أن شهادة العدو لا تُقبَل إذا كانت لأجل الدنيا؛ سواء كانت على عدوّه أو غيره بناء على أنها فسق وهو لا يتجزى. ومن هذا القبيل اختلاف الشاهدين مانع من قبولها لأن أحدهما طابق الدعوى والآخر خالفها. وكتبنا في الفوائد ذلك . المستثنى من البزازية .
ومنها القضاء ؛ فإذا امتنع القضاء للبعض امتنع للباقين، كما في شهادات
ومنها باب العبادات ؛ فلو نوى صوم جميع الشهر بطل فيما عدا اليوم الأول. وليس منه ما إذا عجل زكاة سنتين فإنه إن كان بعد ملك النصاب فهو صحيح فيهما وإلا فلا فيهما . وليس منه أيضًا ما إذا نوى حجتين وأحرم بهما معا؛ فإنَّا نقول بدخوله فيهما لكن اختلفوا في وقت رفضه لإحديهما كما علم في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وليس منه ما إذا نوى التيمم لفرضين، لأنَّا نقول يجوز له أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل .
ومنها : ما إذا صلى على حي وميت، وينبغي أن تصح على الميت.
ومنها : ما إذا استنجى للبول بحجر ثم نام فاحتلم فأمنى فأصاب ثوبه لم يظهر بالفرك لأن البول لا يطهر به فلا يطهر المني كما صرحوا به، ولهذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله : مسألة المنيّ مشكلة لأن كل فحل يمذي أولاً والمذي لا يطهر بالفرك إلا أن يجعل تبعا له. (انتهى).
And ownership, and the correct opinion is that invalidity does not transfer to ownership because waqf is property. Yes, if it is a mosque, it extends to the inhabited part, so it is like a free person, unlike the ruined (al-ghamir with a jeem, meaning ruin) which is like a mudabbar. Of this type is: if one stipulates an option more than three days, it is not valid for three days and becomes void for the extra, rather it becomes void entirely, but if he drops the extra before it enters, the sale becomes valid. And among them: if one combines an unknown and a known in a sale: if the unknown does not lead to dispute, it does not harm; otherwise the whole is invalidated, as known in sales. And among them: ijarah; it is like a sale in that both are invalidated by a corrupt condition. They explicitly stated that if one rents a house for each month for a certain amount, it is valid only for the first month. I have not seen now the ruling if one hires a weaver to weave a cloth of such length and width and he deviates by increase or decrease: does he deserve payment proportional to it or not at all? And among them: kafalah and ibra'; it should not transfer to the permissible. They said: if he said to her 'I guarantee your maintenance each month,' it is valid for one month. And among them: hibah; it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so it does not transfer to the permissible. And among them: iqra' (giving gifts); they said: if a gift is given to a judge by someone who customarily gave gifts before his judgeship and (the gift) increased, the judge returns the increase, not the whole, as in Fath al-Qadir. So it did not transfer to the permissible. The apparent meaning of his words is if the increase is in quantity. But if the increase is in kind, as if his custom was to gift a linen garment and he gifted a silk one, I have not seen it now from our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). And it should be obligatory to return the whole, not just the amount of increase in value, because it is not distinguishable from the permissible. And among them: wasiyyah; if one bequeaths to a non-relative and to his heir, the non-relative gets half, and (the bequest) is invalid for the heir, as in al-Kanz. Similarly, if one bequeaths to a killer and to a non-relative. And among them: iqrar; al-Zayla'i said: regarding one who acknowledges a specific property or debt to his heir and to a non-relative, it is not valid for the non-relative either. (End). And in al-Majma' from iqrar: if one acknowledges to an heir and a non-relative and they both deny partnership, it is considered valid for the non-relative. (End). And among them: the chapter of testimony: if one combines in it one whose testimony is acceptable and one whose testimony is not acceptable; in al-Zahiriyyah from it: a man died and bequeathed something to poor neighbors and the heirs denied his will. Two men from among the neighbors whose children are needy testified to the will. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: their testimony is not accepted because they testified for their children regarding what pertains to their children, so their testimony in that matter is invalidated, and if their testimony regarding the children is invalidated, it is invalidated entirely because testimony is one. Similarly, if they testify against a man that he slandered their slave woman and (also) a certain woman, their testimony is not accepted. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in Waqf al-Asl: if one made a waqf for poor neighbors and two poor neighbors testified to that, their testimony is valid. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth (may Allah have mercy on him) said: what was mentioned in waqf is the view of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him); but by analogy to Muhammad's (may Allah have mercy on him) view, it should not be accepted in waqf either, because according to Abu Yusuf, it is possible that testimony is invalidated in part and remains in part, whereas according to Muhammad, it is not accepted at all. It is possible that what he mentioned in waqf is interpreted as when they are few enough to be counted. (End). And in al-Qunyah: a brother and sister claimed land, and her husband and another man testified; their testimony is rejected regarding the sister and the brother, because whenever part of testimony is rejected, all of it is rejected. And in Rawdat al-Fuqaha: if one testifies for someone whose testimony is not acceptable and for another, it is not acceptable for the one whose testimony is not acceptable by consensus, but for the other there is disagreement: some say it is invalidated, others say it is not. (End). And we wrote in Sharh al-Kanz that the testimony of an enemy is not accepted if it is for worldly purposes, whether against his enemy or another, based on it being fisq (immorality), which is indivisible. Of this type is the disagreement of two witnesses preventing acceptance, because one conforms to the claim and the other contradicts it. We wrote that in al-Fawa'id. The exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah. And among them: the chapter of qada'; if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest, as in testimonies. And among them: the chapter of worship; if one intends to fast the whole month, it is invalid for days other than the first. Not from this is if one pays zakat early for two years: if it is after owning the nisab, it is valid for both; otherwise it is not valid for either. Nor is it from this if one intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together; we say he enters both, but they differed on the time of abandoning one of them, as known in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram. Nor is it from this if one intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers, because we say he can perform as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes with one tayammum. And among them: if one prays over a living and a dead person; it should be valid for the dead. And among them: if one cleans after urine with a stone and then sleeps, has a wet dream, ejaculates, and it gets on his garment, it does not become pure by rubbing, because urine is not purified by it, so semen is not purified by it either, as they explicitly stated. Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: the issue of semen is problematic because every male first releases madhi, and madhi is not purified by rubbing unless it is made subsidiary to it. (End).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exploration of a central qawida in Hanafi fiqh: When a contract or legal transaction combines both permissible (ja'iz) and impermissible (ghayr ja'iz) elements, does the invalidity of the impermissible part spread to the permissible part? The answer is not uniform; it depends on the nature of the act and the degree of indivisibility. The text follows a sequence of chapters, applying the principle to various contracts and actions.

The discussion begins with waqf: if a waqf is a mosque, the ruling of being 'free' (not owned) applies to the inhabited part, not the ruined part, showing that the ruling does not spread to the whole. Then in sales: a condition of option beyond three days invalidates the entire sale, unless the invalid condition is dropped before it takes effect. Mixing known and unknown items in a sale may or may not invalidate the whole depending on whether the unknown leads to dispute.

In ijarah (hire): it is like sale; a corrupt condition invalidates the whole, e.g., renting a house monthly for a fixed amount is valid only for the first month. The author notes an unresolved case: hiring a weaver with specific dimensions, and he deviates; the author does not find a ruling, indicating doubt.

In kafalah (suretyship) and ibra (discharge): the principle should not transfer to the permissible part. Example: 'I guarantee your monthly maintenance' is valid for one month only.

Hibah (gift): not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so the impermissible does not spread.

In gifts to a judge: if the increase is in quantity, only the increase is returned; if in kind (e.g., silk instead of linen), the author suggests returning the whole because it is not separable.

In wasiyyah (bequest): if made to both a non-heir and an heir, the bequest to the heir is invalid but the non-heir gets half, showing partial invalidity. Similarly for iqrar (acknowledgment): according to al-Zayla'i, if acknowledged to an heir and a non-heir, both are invalid; but another view in al-Majma' validates the non-heir's portion if they deny partnership.

In shahadah (testimony): the key principle is that testimony is indivisible. If it is invalid for one party, it is invalid for all. This is illustrated by cases of testifying for one's own children and for neighbors in waqf. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf allows partial validity in testimony, Muhammad insists on total invalidity. The text also discusses exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah.

In qada' (judgment): if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest (similar to testimony).

In ibadat (worship): intending to fast the whole month is valid only for the first day (since fasting requires separate intentions). But paying zakat early for two years is valid for both if the nisab is owned at the time of payment. Intending two hajj together: the person enters both, but there is disagreement on abandoning one. Tayammum for two obligatory prayers: valid because one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers.

Praying over a living and dead person: valid for the dead.

Cleaning with a stone: if semen touches the garment after istinja, it is not purified by rubbing because the madhi (pre-ejaculate) that precedes it is not purified by rubbing, and semen follows it. This is problematic, but the author points out the difficulty.

Overall, the passage reinforces that the spread of invalidity is not mechanical; it depends on the structure and indivisibility of the legal act.

Key Terms
الشهادة واحدة (al-shahadah wahidah): Testimony is one indivisible statement.
الفسق لا يتجزى (al-fisq la yatajazza): Immorality (fisq) is indivisible; a fasiq's testimony is rejected entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling if two witnesses testify, and one of them is disqualified?
A) The testimony is accepted from the qualified witness only.
B) The entire testimony is invalid.
C) The testimony is valid if the disqualified witness withdraws.
D) The testimony is split: valid for one party and invalid for the other.

Key Takeaway
Testimony and iqrar are considered indivisible statements, but Abu Yusuf allows partial validity; the mufti must be aware of both views.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
intermediate
8 min
Worship and Mixed Intentions: Fasting, Zakat, Hajj, Tayammum
Applications of the maxim to acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of spread of invalidity to acts of worship involving multiple intentions or mixed valid/invalid elements.

Core Idea
In worship, each act often requires a separate intention; mixing invalid intentions does not necessarily invalidate the entire worship.

This lesson covers the application of the general qawida to acts of worship. The key is that worship acts often involve separable intentions (e.g., each day of fasting requires its own intention), so the invalidity of one part does not automatically spread. However, there are exceptions like zakat paid early and tayammum, which are considered complete acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of worship and its elements
E.g., fasting the whole month with one intention; intending two hajj; paying zakat early; making tayammum for multiple prayers.
2
Determine if the act is separable
If each part requires its own intention (like days of fasting), then invalidity does not spread. If the act is one (like tayammum), it covers all.
Fasting: each day is independent. Zakat: two years can be intended separately. Tayammum: one purification suffices.
3
Apply the ruling
Intending to fast whole month: valid only for first day. Intending two hajj: both entered, but must abandon one. Zakat early: both valid if nisab owned. Tayammum for two prayers: valid for both.
4
Note exceptions
The principle that invalidity does not spread is illustrated; the exceptions (hibah, zakat, tayammum) are not about worship in this context but show the opposite rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملك، والأصح أنه لا الفساد إلى الملك لأن الوقف مال نعم إذا كان مسجدا يسري عامرًا فهو كالحرّ بخلاف الغامر بالمعجمة أي الخراب فكالمدبر. ومن هذا القبيل ما إذا شرط الخيار فيه أكثر من ثلاثة فإنه لا يصح في الثلاثة ويبطل فيما زاد، بل يبطل في الكل، لكن إذا أسقط الزائد قبل دخوله انقلب البيع صحيحًا .
ومنها ما إذا جمع بين مجهول ومعلوم في البيع فإن كان المجهول لا تُفضي جهالته إلى المنازعة لا يضرّ وإلا فسد في الكل كما علم في البيوع . ومنها الإجارة ؛ فهي كالبيع لاشتراكهما في أنهما يبطلان بالشرط الفاسد وصرَّحوا بأنه لو استأجر دارًا في كل شهر بكذا فإنه يصح في الشهر الأول فقط . ولم أرَ الآن حكم ما إذا استأجر نساجًا لينسج له ثوبًا طوله كذا، وعرضه كذا فخالف بزيادة أو نقصان. هل يستحق بقدره أو لا يستحق أصلا؟ ومنها الكفالة والإبراء وينبغي أن لا يتعدى إلى الجائز. وقالوا لو قال لها ضمنت لك نفقتك كل شهر فإنه يصح في شهر واحد.
ومنها الهبة وهي لا تبطل بالشرط الفاسد فلا يتعدى إلى الجائز .
ومنها الإهداء ؛ قالوا لو أهدي إلى القاضي من له عادة بالإهداء له قبل القضاء وزاد، يردّ القاضي الزائد لا الكل كما في فتح القدير، فلم يتعد إلى الجائز. وظاهر كلامه أنه إن زاد في القدر. وأما إذا زاد في المعنى كما إذا كانت عادته إهداء ثوب كتان فأهدى ثوبا حريرًا لم أره الآن لأصحابنا رحمهم الله. وينبغي وجوب ردّ الكل لا بقدر ما زاد في قيمته لعدم تمييزها من الجائز .
ومنها الوصية ؛ فلو أوصى لأجنبي ووارثه فللأجنبي نصفها وبطلت للوارث؛ كما في الكنز، وكذا لو أوصى للقاتل وللأجنبي.
ومنها الإقرار ؛ قال الزيلعي فيما لو أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه ولأجنبي لم يصح في حق الأجنبي أيضًا. (انتهى). وفي المجمع من الإقرار لو أقر لوارث مع أجنبي فتكاذبا الشركة صححه في الأجنبي. (انتهى) .
ومنها باب الشهادة، فإذا جمع فيها بين مَن تجوز شهادته ومَن لا تجوز؛ ففي الظهيرية منها : رجل مات وأوصى لفقراء جيرانه بشيء وأنكرت الورثة وصيته فشهد على الوصية رجلان من جيرانه لهما أولاد محاويج . قال محمد رحمه الله : لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما شهدا لأولادهما فيما يخص أولادهما فبطلت شهادتهما في ذلك، فإذا بطلت شهادتهما في حق الأولاد بطلت أصلاً لأن الشهادة واحدة، كما لو شهدا على رجل أنه قذف أمتهما وفلانة لا تقبل شهادتهما. وذكر محمد رحمه الله في وقف الأصل؛ إذا وقف على فقراء جيرانه فشهد بذلك فقيران من جيرانه جازت شهادتهما ؛ قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله ما ذكر في الوقف قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله، أما على قياس قول محمد رحمه الله فينبغي ألا تقبل في الوقف أيضًا لأن عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله يجوز أن تبطل الشهادة في البعض وتبقى في البعض وعلى قول محمد رحمه الله لا تقبل أصلاً ويحتمل أن ما ذكره في الوقف محمول على ما إذا كانوا قليلين يحصون. (انتهى). وفي القنية : أخ وأخت ادعيا أرضا وشهد زوجها ورجل آخر ترد شهادتهما في حق الأخت والأخ ؛ فإن الشهادة متى ردّ بعضها ترد كلها. وفي روضة الفقهاء إذا شهد لمَن لا تجوز له الشهادة ولغيره لا تجوز لمن لا تجوز له الشهادة بالاتفاق واختلف في حق الآخر فقيل تبطل وقيل لا تبطل. (انتهى).
وكتبنا في شرح الكنز أن شهادة العدو لا تُقبَل إذا كانت لأجل الدنيا؛ سواء كانت على عدوّه أو غيره بناء على أنها فسق وهو لا يتجزى. ومن هذا القبيل اختلاف الشاهدين مانع من قبولها لأن أحدهما طابق الدعوى والآخر خالفها. وكتبنا في الفوائد ذلك . المستثنى من البزازية .
ومنها القضاء ؛ فإذا امتنع القضاء للبعض امتنع للباقين، كما في شهادات
ومنها باب العبادات ؛ فلو نوى صوم جميع الشهر بطل فيما عدا اليوم الأول. وليس منه ما إذا عجل زكاة سنتين فإنه إن كان بعد ملك النصاب فهو صحيح فيهما وإلا فلا فيهما . وليس منه أيضًا ما إذا نوى حجتين وأحرم بهما معا؛ فإنَّا نقول بدخوله فيهما لكن اختلفوا في وقت رفضه لإحديهما كما علم في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وليس منه ما إذا نوى التيمم لفرضين، لأنَّا نقول يجوز له أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل .
ومنها : ما إذا صلى على حي وميت، وينبغي أن تصح على الميت.
ومنها : ما إذا استنجى للبول بحجر ثم نام فاحتلم فأمنى فأصاب ثوبه لم يظهر بالفرك لأن البول لا يطهر به فلا يطهر المني كما صرحوا به، ولهذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله : مسألة المنيّ مشكلة لأن كل فحل يمذي أولاً والمذي لا يطهر بالفرك إلا أن يجعل تبعا له. (انتهى).
And ownership, and the correct opinion is that invalidity does not transfer to ownership because waqf is property. Yes, if it is a mosque, it extends to the inhabited part, so it is like a free person, unlike the ruined (al-ghamir with a jeem, meaning ruin) which is like a mudabbar. Of this type is: if one stipulates an option more than three days, it is not valid for three days and becomes void for the extra, rather it becomes void entirely, but if he drops the extra before it enters, the sale becomes valid. And among them: if one combines an unknown and a known in a sale: if the unknown does not lead to dispute, it does not harm; otherwise the whole is invalidated, as known in sales. And among them: ijarah; it is like a sale in that both are invalidated by a corrupt condition. They explicitly stated that if one rents a house for each month for a certain amount, it is valid only for the first month. I have not seen now the ruling if one hires a weaver to weave a cloth of such length and width and he deviates by increase or decrease: does he deserve payment proportional to it or not at all? And among them: kafalah and ibra'; it should not transfer to the permissible. They said: if he said to her 'I guarantee your maintenance each month,' it is valid for one month. And among them: hibah; it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so it does not transfer to the permissible. And among them: iqra' (giving gifts); they said: if a gift is given to a judge by someone who customarily gave gifts before his judgeship and (the gift) increased, the judge returns the increase, not the whole, as in Fath al-Qadir. So it did not transfer to the permissible. The apparent meaning of his words is if the increase is in quantity. But if the increase is in kind, as if his custom was to gift a linen garment and he gifted a silk one, I have not seen it now from our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them). And it should be obligatory to return the whole, not just the amount of increase in value, because it is not distinguishable from the permissible. And among them: wasiyyah; if one bequeaths to a non-relative and to his heir, the non-relative gets half, and (the bequest) is invalid for the heir, as in al-Kanz. Similarly, if one bequeaths to a killer and to a non-relative. And among them: iqrar; al-Zayla'i said: regarding one who acknowledges a specific property or debt to his heir and to a non-relative, it is not valid for the non-relative either. (End). And in al-Majma' from iqrar: if one acknowledges to an heir and a non-relative and they both deny partnership, it is considered valid for the non-relative. (End). And among them: the chapter of testimony: if one combines in it one whose testimony is acceptable and one whose testimony is not acceptable; in al-Zahiriyyah from it: a man died and bequeathed something to poor neighbors and the heirs denied his will. Two men from among the neighbors whose children are needy testified to the will. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: their testimony is not accepted because they testified for their children regarding what pertains to their children, so their testimony in that matter is invalidated, and if their testimony regarding the children is invalidated, it is invalidated entirely because testimony is one. Similarly, if they testify against a man that he slandered their slave woman and (also) a certain woman, their testimony is not accepted. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in Waqf al-Asl: if one made a waqf for poor neighbors and two poor neighbors testified to that, their testimony is valid. It is possible that what he mentioned in waqf is interpreted as when they are few enough to be counted. (End). And in al-Qunyah: a brother and sister claimed land, and her husband and another man testified; their testimony is rejected regarding the sister and the brother, because whenever part of testimony is rejected, all of it is rejected. And in Rawdat al-Fuqaha: if one testifies for someone whose testimony is not acceptable and for another, it is not acceptable for the one whose testimony is not acceptable by consensus, but for the other there is disagreement: some say it is invalidated, others say it is not. (End). And we wrote in Sharh al-Kanz that the testimony of an enemy is not accepted if it is for worldly purposes, whether against his enemy or another, based on it being fisq (immorality), which is indivisible. Of this type is the disagreement of two witnesses preventing acceptance, because one conforms to the claim and the other contradicts it. We wrote that in al-Fawa'id. The exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah. And among them: the chapter of qada'; if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest, as in testimonies. And among them: the chapter of worship; if one intends to fast the whole month, it is invalid for days other than the first. Not from this is if one pays zakat early for two years: if it is after owning the nisab, it is valid for both; otherwise it is not valid for either. Nor is it from this if one intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together; we say he enters both, but they differed on the time of abandoning one of them, as known in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram. Nor is it from this if one intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers, because we say he can perform as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes with one tayammum. And among them: if one prays over a living and a dead person; it should be valid for the dead. And among them: if one cleans after urine with a stone and then sleeps, has a wet dream, ejaculates, and it gets on his garment, it does not become pure by rubbing, because urine is not purified by it, so semen is not purified by it either, as they explicitly stated. Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: the issue of semen is problematic because every male first releases madhi, and madhi is not purified by rubbing unless it is made subsidiary to it. (End).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exploration of a central qawida in Hanafi fiqh: When a contract or legal transaction combines both permissible (ja'iz) and impermissible (ghayr ja'iz) elements, does the invalidity of the impermissible part spread to the permissible part? The answer is not uniform; it depends on the nature of the act and the degree of indivisibility. The text follows a sequence of chapters, applying the principle to various contracts and actions.

The discussion begins with waqf: if a waqf is a mosque, the ruling of being 'free' (not owned) applies to the inhabited part, not the ruined part, showing that the ruling does not spread to the whole. Then in sales: a condition of option beyond three days invalidates the entire sale, unless the invalid condition is dropped before it takes effect. Mixing known and unknown items in a sale may or may not invalidate the whole depending on whether the unknown leads to dispute.

In ijarah (hire): it is like sale; a corrupt condition invalidates the whole, e.g., renting a house monthly for a fixed amount is valid only for the first month. The author notes an unresolved case: hiring a weaver with specific dimensions, and he deviates; the author does not find a ruling, indicating doubt.

In kafalah (suretyship) and ibra (discharge): the principle should not transfer to the permissible part. Example: 'I guarantee your monthly maintenance' is valid for one month only.

Hibah (gift): not invalidated by a corrupt condition, so the impermissible does not spread.

In gifts to a judge: if the increase is in quantity, only the increase is returned; if in kind (e.g., silk instead of linen), the author suggests returning the whole because it is not separable.

In wasiyyah (bequest): if made to both a non-heir and an heir, the bequest to the heir is invalid but the non-heir gets half, showing partial invalidity. Similarly for iqrar (acknowledgment): according to al-Zayla'i, if acknowledged to an heir and a non-heir, both are invalid; but another view in al-Majma' validates the non-heir's portion if they deny partnership.

In shahadah (testimony): the key principle is that testimony is indivisible. If it is invalid for one party, it is invalid for all. This is illustrated by cases of testifying for one's own children and for neighbors in waqf. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf allows partial validity in testimony, Muhammad insists on total invalidity. The text also discusses exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah.

In qada' (judgment): if judgment is prevented for some, it is prevented for the rest (similar to testimony).

In ibadat (worship): intending to fast the whole month is valid only for the first day (since fasting requires separate intentions). But paying zakat early for two years is valid for both if the nisab is owned at the time of payment. Intending two hajj together: the person enters both, but there is disagreement on abandoning one. Tayammum for two obligatory prayers: valid because one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers.

Praying over a living and dead person: valid for the dead.

Cleaning with a stone: if semen touches the garment after istinja, it is not purified by rubbing because the madhi (pre-ejaculate) that precedes it is not purified by rubbing, and semen follows it. This is problematic, but the author points out the difficulty.

Overall, the passage reinforces that the spread of invalidity is not mechanical; it depends on the structure and indivisibility of the legal act.

Key Terms
نية الصوم (niyyat al-sawm): Intention for fasting; required for each day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers?
A) Invalid; each prayer requires separate tayammum.
B) Valid for the first prayer only.
C) Valid for both prayers because one tayammum suffices.
D) Valid only if the person renews intention for the second.

Key Takeaway
Acts of worship with separable parts (like fasting days) require separate intentions; invalidity of one part does not spread, but each part stands alone.

Exceptions in Judiciary, Fasting, and Zakat
List of exceptions to the rule of partial invalidity: judiciary, fasting, zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the exceptions to the rule of partial invalidity in cases of judiciary, fasting, and zakat.

Core Idea
Partial invalidity does not always entail total invalidity; these three cases show where the rule is set aside.

This lesson begins the enumeration of exceptions to the maxim 'if something is invalid in part, it is invalid in whole' as recorded in al-Bazzaziyyah. We examine the first three exceptions: judiciary, where disqualification for some cases blocks all; fasting, where a single intention for the month fails except for the first day; and zakat, where early payment for two years is either fully valid or fully invalid based on ownership of nisab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the qawida: partial invalidity entails total invalidity. Recognize that the passage lists exceptions where this rule does not apply.
This is a foundational maxim in Hanafi fiqh, but with many mustathnayat.
2
Analyze the judiciary exception
Examine why a judge disqualified from some cases is disqualified from all: the office is indivisible, similar to testimonies.
The rule applies fully here; it is an exception because partial disqualification leads to total disqualification, but the mechanism is different.
3
Examine the fasting exception
Understand why intending to fast the entire month only validates the first day: each day requires a separate intention (niyyah).
This shows the ruling is not invalidity but limiting validity to the first day.
4
Apply the zakat exception
Learn the condition for early zakat: if nisab was owned at time of payment, it is valid for both years; otherwise invalid for both.
This is a conditional exception where the presence of nisab determines validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المستثنى من البزازية . ومنها القضاء ؛ فإذا امتنع القضاء للبعض امتنع للباقين، كما في شهادات ومنها باب العبادات ؛ فلو نوى صوم جميع الشهر بطل فيما عدا اليوم الأول. وليس منه ما إذا عجل زكاة سنتين فإنه إن كان بعد ملك النصاب فهو صحيح فيهما وإلا فلا فيهما . وليس منه أيضًا ما إذا نوى حجتين وأحرم بهما معا؛ فإنَّا نقول بدخوله فيهما لكن اختلفوا في وقت رفضه لإحديهما كما علم في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وليس منه ما إذا نوى التيمم لفرضين، لأنَّا نقول يجوز له أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل . ومنها : ما إذا صلى على حي وميت، وينبغي أن تصح على الميت. ومنها : ما إذا استنجى للبول بحجر ثم نام فاحتلم فأمنى فأصاب ثوبه لم يظهر بالفرك لأن البول لا يطهر به فلا يطهر المني كما صرحوا به، ولهذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله : مسألة المنيّ مشكلة لأن كل فحل يمذي أولاً والمذي لا يطهر بالفرك إلا أن يجعل تبعا له. (انتهى). وقد يقال يمكن جعل البول الباقي بعد الاستجمار تبعًا له أيضًا. وجوابه أن التبعية فيما هو لازم له وهو المذي، بخلاف البول ولم أرَ مَن نبَّه عليه . ومنها باب الطلاق والعتاق ؛ فلو طلق زوجته وغيرها أو أعتق عبده وعبد غيره أو طلقها أربعا نفذ فيما يملكه . ومنها: لو استعار شيئًا ليرهنه على قدر معين فرهنه بأزيد قال في الكنز : ولو عيّن قدرًا أو جنسا أو بلدا فخالف ضمن المعير المستعير والمرتهن . (انتهى). واستثنى الشارح ما إذا عيّن له أكثر من قيمته فرهنه بأقل من ذلك بمثل قيمته أو أكثر؛ فإنه لا يضمن لكونه خلافا إلى خير. (انتهى). ومنها : لو شرط الواقف ألا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة، فزاد الناظر عليها؛ فظاهر المدة لا فيما زاد على المشروط لأنها كالبيع لا يقبل تفريق الصفقة وصرّح به في فتاوى قارىء الهداية ثم قال : والعقد إذا فسد في بعضه فسد في جميعه . تنبيه : وليس من القاعدة; ما إذا اجتمع في العبادات جانب الحضر وجانب السفر فإنَّا لا نغلب جانب الحضر. ومقتضاها تغليبه لأنه اجتمع المبيح والمحرم لأن أصحابنا رحمهم الله قالوا في المسح على الخُفَّين: ولو ابتدأ وهو مقيم فسافر قبل إتمام يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى مدة المسافر فيمسح ثلاثا، ولو كان على عكسه انتقلت إلى مدة المقيم. ومقتضاها اعتبار مدة الإقامة فيهما تغليبًا لجانب الحضر، وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله وعنده لو أحد الخُفَّين حضرًا والآخر سفرًا فكذلك على الأصح طردًا للقاعدة، وأما عندنا فلا خفاء في أن مدته مدة المسافر وأما لو أحرم قاصرًا فبلغت سفينته دار إقامته فإنه يتم، ولو شرع في الصلاة في دار الإقامة فسارت سفينته فليس له القصر، ولم أرهما الآن. وعندنا فائتة السفر إذا قضاها في الحضر يقضيها ركعتين وعكسه يقضيها أربعًا لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. وأما باب الصوم فإذا صام مقيما فسافر في أثناء النهار أو عكسه حرم الفطر .
Exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah. Among them: judiciary (qada): if judgment is withheld for some, it is withheld for the rest, as in testimonies. Among them: chapter of acts of worship (ibadat): if one intends to fast the entire month, it is invalid except for the first day. And it is not from this rule: if one hastens zakat for two years, if after possessing the nisab it is valid for both, otherwise invalid for both. And it is also not from it: if one intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together, we say he enters both, but they differed on the time of renouncing one of them as known in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram. And it is not from it: if one intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers, we say he may pray with one tayammum as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes. Among them: if one prays over a living and a dead person, it should be valid for the dead. Among them: if one cleanses himself from urine with a stone, then sleeps, has a wet dream, emits semen, and it touches his garment, it is not purified by rubbing because urine is not purified by [dry] rubbing, so semen is not purified by it, as they stated. Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The matter of semen is problematic because every male emits madhy first, and madhy is not purified by rubbing unless it is made subsidiary to it. (End.) It may be said that the remaining urine after istijmar can also be made subsidiary to it. The answer is that subsidiary applies to what is necessary for it, which is madhy, unlike urine, and I have not seen anyone point this out. Among them: chapter of divorce and emancipation: if one divorces his wife and another, or emancipates his slave and another's slave, or divorces her four times, it takes effect regarding what he owns. Among them: if one borrows something to pawn it for a specific amount and then pawns it for more, al-Kanz says: if he specifies an amount, type, or place and violates, he is liable to the lender, borrower, and pawnbroker. (End.) The commentator excepted if he specified more than its value and pawned it for less than that, equal to or more than its value; then he is not liable because it is a violation for good. (End.) Among them: if the endower stipulates that his endowment should not be rented for more than a year, and the overseer exceeds it; then the [invalidity] is apparent for the period [exceeding] not for what exceeds the condition because it is like a sale that does not accept splitting the package, and it is stated in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidayah, then he said: The contract, if it becomes invalid in part, becomes invalid entirely. Note: And it is not from the rule: when in acts of worship the factor of residence and the factor of travel come together, we do not give preponderance to the factor of residence. Its implication is to give it preponderance because the permissive and prohibitive factors come together. Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding wiping over khuffain: If he begins while a resident and then travels before completing a day and a night, his period is transferred to the traveler's period, so he wipes for three days; if the opposite, it is transferred to the resident's period. Its implication is to consider the period of residence in both, giving preponderance to the factor of residence, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said the same. According to him, if one khuff is for residence and the other for travel, likewise on the correct view, consistently applying the rule. But according to us, there is no doubt that his period is the traveler's period. And as for if he enters ihram as a qasir [shortening] and then his ship reaches the place of residence, he completes [the prayer], and if he begins prayer in the place of residence and then his ship moves, he does not shorten [the prayer], and I have not seen these two [cases] now. According to us, a missed prayer of travel when made up in residence is performed as two rak'ahs, and the opposite as four because the makeup mimics the original performance. As for the chapter of fasting: if one fasts as a resident and then travels during the day, or vice versa, breaking the fast is prohibited.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an extensive collection of exceptions (mustathnayat) to the general maxim that when something is invalid in part, it is invalid in whole. It is drawn from al-Bazzaziyyah, a famous Hanafi fatwa collection. The text methodically goes through various chapters of fiqh, showing where the rule applies and where it does not. Key examples: In judiciary (qada), if a judge is disqualified for some cases, he is disqualified for all. In acts of worship, if one intends to fast the entire month but only the first day is valid (because intention must be renewed). Exceptions include: accelerated zakat becomes valid for both years if nisab was owned at the time of payment; intention for two hajj together results in both being entered, but the ruling on renunciation differs; tayammum for multiple prayers is valid because one tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers. Other chapters include prayer over living and dead, istinja and impurity, divorce and emancipation, loans and pawning, and endowment rental. Finally, a note (tanbih) clarifies that the case of mixing residence and travel in worship is not an exception to this rule; rather, the school often gives preference to the travel factor, but also gives examples where residency prevails. This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning in applying and restricting general maxims.

Key Terms
المستثنى (al-mustathnā): Exceptions to the general rule of partial invalidity.
البزازية (al-Bazzāziyyah): A Hanafi fatwa collection by al-Bazzazi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah, if someone intends to fast the entire month of Ramadan with one intention, what is the ruling?
A) The entire month's fast is valid.
B) Only the first day is valid.
C) The fast is invalid for all days.
D) It depends on whether the person is a resident or traveler.

Key Takeaway
Exceptions to the rule of partial invalidity are established by specific evidence; muftis must know these exceptions to issue correct fatwas.

Exceptions in Hajj, Tayammum, and Prayer on Living and Dead
Exceptions to partial invalidity in hajj, tayammum, and combined funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply exceptions to partial invalidity in cases of combined hajj intentions, multiple prayers with one tayammum, and combined funeral prayer.

Core Idea
Some acts accept partial validity even when intended in combination; these exceptions prevent total invalidity.

This lesson continues the list from al-Bazzaziyyah, covering three more exceptions where the rule of total invalidity does not apply: entering ihram for two hajj simultaneously, performing multiple prayers with one tayammum, and praying over both a living and dead person. In each case, the act is partially valid or entirely valid, contrary to the general maxim.

Guided Path
1
Examine the hajj exception
Understand that if someone intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together, both are entered; the invalidity does not spread because the intention is valid.
There is ikhtilaf on when to renounce one; that does not affect the core exception.
2
Analyze the tayammum exception
Learn that one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers (obligatory and supererogatory); thus partial invalidity does not occur because the act is fully valid.
This is an exception because the rule would suggest using tayammum for each prayer separately if partial invalidity were applied.
3
Apply the funeral prayer exception
If one prays over both a living and a dead person, the prayer for the dead is valid; the invalidity regarding the living does not affect the dead.
Here, part of the act (for the living) is invalid, but the part for the dead remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(انتهى). واستثنى الشارح ما إذا عيّن له أكثر من قيمته فرهنه بأقل من ذلك بمثل قيمته أو أكثر؛ فإنه لا يضمن لكونه خلافا إلى خير. (انتهى). ومنها : لو شرط الواقف ألا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة، فزاد الناظر عليها؛ فظاهر المدة لا فيما زاد على المشروط لأنها كالبيع لا يقبل تفريق الصفقة وصرّح به في فتاوى قارىء الهداية ثم قال : والعقد إذا فسد في بعضه فسد في جميعه . تنبيه : وليس من القاعدة; ما إذا اجتمع في العبادات جانب الحضر وجانب السفر فإنَّا لا نغلب جانب الحضر. ومقتضاها تغليبه لأنه اجتمع المبيح والمحرم لأن أصحابنا رحمهم الله قالوا في المسح على الخُفَّين: ولو ابتدأ وهو مقيم فسافر قبل إتمام يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى مدة المسافر فيمسح ثلاثا، ولو كان على عكسه انتقلت إلى مدة المقيم. ومقتضاها اعتبار مدة الإقامة فيهما تغليبًا لجانب الحضر، وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله وعنده لو أحد الخُفَّين حضرًا والآخر سفرًا فكذلك على الأصح طردًا للقاعدة، وأما عندنا فلا خفاء في أن مدته مدة المسافر وأما لو أحرم قاصرًا فبلغت سفينته دار إقامته فإنه يتم، ولو شرع في الصلاة في دار الإقامة فسارت سفينته فليس له القصر، ولم أرهما الآن. وعندنا فائتة السفر إذا قضاها في الحضر يقضيها ركعتين وعكسه يقضيها أربعًا لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. وأما باب الصوم فإذا صام مقيما فسافر في أثناء النهار أو عكسه حرم الفطر .

Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding wiping over khuffain: If he begins while a resident and then travels before completing a day and a night, his period is transferred to the traveler's period, so he wipes for three days; if the opposite, it is transferred to the resident's period. Its implication is to consider the period of residence in both, giving preponderance to the factor of residence, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said the same. According to him, if one khuff is for residence and the other for travel, likewise on the correct view, consistently applying the rule. But according to us, there is no doubt that his period is the traveler's period. And as for if he enters ihram as a qasir [shortening] and then his ship reaches the place of residence, he completes [the prayer], and if he begins prayer in the place of residence and then his ship moves, he does not shorten [the prayer], and I have not seen these two [cases] now. According to us, a missed prayer of travel when made up in residence is performed as two rak'ahs, and the opposite as four because the makeup mimics the original performance. As for the chapter of fasting: if one fasts as a resident and then travels during the day, or vice versa, breaking the fast is prohibited.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an extensive collection of exceptions (mustathnayat) to the general maxim that when something is invalid in part, it is invalid in whole. It is drawn from al-Bazzaziyyah, a famous Hanafi fatwa collection. The text methodically goes through various chapters of fiqh, showing where the rule applies and where it does not. Key examples: In judiciary (qada), if a judge is disqualified for some cases, he is disqualified for all. In acts of worship, if one intends to fast the entire month but only the first day is valid (because intention must be renewed). Exceptions include: accelerated zakat becomes valid for both years if nisab was owned at the time of payment; intention for two hajj together results in both being entered, but the ruling on renunciation differs; tayammum for multiple prayers is valid because one tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers. Other chapters include prayer over living and dead, istinja and impurity, divorce and emancipation, loans and pawning, and endowment rental. Finally, a note (tanbih) clarifies that the case of mixing residence and travel in worship is not an exception to this rule; rather, the school often gives preference to the travel factor, but also gives examples where residency prevails. This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning in applying and restricting general maxims.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as substitute for wudu.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for hajj or umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone prays over a living and a dead person together, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) Both are invalid.
B) It is valid for the dead.
C) It is valid for the living.
D) It is invalid for both.

Key Takeaway
These exceptions demonstrate that the general rule yields to specific evidence and custom, allowing partial validity in combined acts.

Exceptions in Purity, Divorce, Emancipation, and Loan
Exceptions to partial invalidity in purity, family law, and transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply exceptions to partial invalidity in cases of impurity transfer, combined divorce/emancipation, and loan pawning violations.

Core Idea
Even in purity and contracts, partial invalidity does not always spread; subsidiary impurities and combined intentions are treated separately.

This lesson covers a diverse set of exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah, including the problematic case of semen impurity following istinja, combined divorce and emancipation, and loan pawning violations. Each shows how the Hanafi school limits the spread of invalidity based on subsidiary relationships or independent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the purity exception
Analyze the case: after istinja (cleaning from urine with a stone), if one then emits semen (due to wet dream) and it touches the garment, does the earlier urine purification affect the semen? The rule that partial invalidity spreads would suggest yes, but the school says no because urine impure remains and semen is independent.
Al-Sarakhsi notes the problem of madhy being first; the impurity of semen is not removed by rubbing like urine.
2
Examine the divorce/emancipation exception
If one divorces his wife and another person's wife (or emancipates his slave and another's), it takes effect only on what he owns. The invalid part (regarding others) does not affect his own.
This is because the act is divisible by ownership.
3
Apply the loan pawning exception
If someone borrows an item to pawn for a specific amount but pawns it for more, he is liable. However, an exception: if he pawns for less than the specific amount but more than the value, he is not liable because he acted for betterment (khayr).
This shows that partial violation (exceeding the amount) does not always lead to full liability when it is for good.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المستثنى من البزازية . ومنها القضاء ؛ فإذا امتنع القضاء للبعض امتنع للباقين، كما في شهادات ومنها باب العبادات ؛ فلو نوى صوم جميع الشهر بطل فيما عدا اليوم الأول. وليس منه ما إذا عجل زكاة سنتين فإنه إن كان بعد ملك النصاب فهو صحيح فيهما وإلا فلا فيهما . وليس منه أيضًا ما إذا نوى حجتين وأحرم بهما معا؛ فإنَّا نقول بدخوله فيهما لكن اختلفوا في وقت رفضه لإحديهما كما علم في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام وليس منه ما إذا نوى التيمم لفرضين، لأنَّا نقول يجوز له أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض والنوافل . ومنها : ما إذا صلى على حي وميت، وينبغي أن تصح على الميت. ومنها : ما إذا استنجى للبول بحجر ثم نام فاحتلم فأمنى فأصاب ثوبه لم يظهر بالفرك لأن البول لا يطهر به فلا يطهر المني كما صرحوا به، ولهذا قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي رحمه الله : مسألة المنيّ مشكلة لأن كل فحل يمذي أولاً والمذي لا يطهر بالفرك إلا أن يجعل تبعا له. (انتهى). وقد يقال يمكن جعل البول الباقي بعد الاستجمار تبعًا له أيضًا. وجوابه أن التبعية فيما هو لازم له وهو المذي، بخلاف البول ولم أرَ مَن نبَّه عليه . ومنها باب الطلاق والعتاق ؛ فلو طلق زوجته وغيرها أو أعتق عبده وعبد غيره أو طلقها أربعا نفذ فيما يملكه . ومنها: لو استعار شيئًا ليرهنه على قدر معين فرهنه بأزيد قال في الكنز : ولو عيّن قدرًا أو جنسا أو بلدا فخالف ضمن المعير المستعير والمرتهن . (انتهى). واستثنى الشارح ما إذا عيّن له أكثر من قيمته فرهنه بأقل من ذلك بمثل قيمته أو أكثر؛ فإنه لا يضمن لكونه خلافا إلى خير. (انتهى). ومنها : لو شرط الواقف ألا يؤجر وقفه أكثر من سنة، فزاد الناظر عليها؛ فظاهر المدة لا فيما زاد على المشروط لأنها كالبيع لا يقبل تفريق الصفقة وصرّح به في فتاوى قارىء الهداية ثم قال : والعقد إذا فسد في بعضه فسد في جميعه . تنبيه : وليس من القاعدة; ما إذا اجتمع في العبادات جانب الحضر وجانب السفر فإنَّا لا نغلب جانب الحضر. ومقتضاها تغليبه لأنه اجتمع المبيح والمحرم لأن أصحابنا رحمهم الله قالوا في المسح على الخُفَّين: ولو ابتدأ وهو مقيم فسافر قبل إتمام يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى مدة المسافر فيمسح ثلاثا، ولو كان على عكسه انتقلت إلى مدة المقيم. ومقتضاها اعتبار مدة الإقامة فيهما تغليبًا لجانب الحضر، وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله وعنده لو أحد الخُفَّين حضرًا والآخر سفرًا فكذلك على الأصح طردًا للقاعدة، وأما عندنا فلا خفاء في أن مدته مدة المسافر وأما لو أحرم قاصرًا فبلغت سفينته دار إقامته فإنه يتم، ولو شرع في الصلاة في دار الإقامة فسارت سفينته فليس له القصر، ولم أرهما الآن. وعندنا فائتة السفر إذا قضاها في الحضر يقضيها ركعتين وعكسه يقضيها أربعًا لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. وأما باب الصوم فإذا صام مقيما فسافر في أثناء النهار أو عكسه حرم الفطر .
Exceptions from al-Bazzaziyyah. Among them: judiciary (qada): if judgment is withheld for some, it is withheld for the rest, as in testimonies. Among them: chapter of acts of worship (ibadat): if one intends to fast the entire month, it is invalid except for the first day. And it is not from this rule: if one hastens zakat for two years, if after possessing the nisab it is valid for both, otherwise invalid for both. And it is also not from it: if one intends two hajj and enters ihram for both together, we say he enters both, but they differed on the time of renouncing one of them as known in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram. And it is not from it: if one intends tayammum for two obligatory prayers, we say he may pray with one tayammum as many obligatory and supererogatory prayers as he wishes. Among them: if one prays over a living and a dead person, it should be valid for the dead. Among them: if one cleanses himself from urine with a stone, then sleeps, has a wet dream, emits semen, and it touches his garment, it is not purified by rubbing because urine is not purified by [dry] rubbing, so semen is not purified by it, as they stated. Hence Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The matter of semen is problematic because every male emits madhy first, and madhy is not purified by rubbing unless it is made subsidiary to it. (End.) It may be said that the remaining urine after istijmar can also be made subsidiary to it. The answer is that subsidiary applies to what is necessary for it, which is madhy, unlike urine, and I have not seen anyone point this out. Among them: chapter of divorce and emancipation: if one divorces his wife and another, or emancipates his slave and another's slave, or divorces her four times, it takes effect regarding what he owns. Among them: if one borrows something to pawn it for a specific amount and then pawns it for more, al-Kanz says: if he specifies an amount, type, or place and violates, he is liable to the lender, borrower, and pawnbroker. (End.) The commentator excepted if he specified more than its value and pawned it for less than that, equal to or more than its value; then he is not liable because it is a violation for good. (End.) Among them: if the endower stipulates that his endowment should not be rented for more than a year, and the overseer exceeds it; then the [invalidity] is apparent for the period [exceeding] not for what exceeds the condition because it is like a sale that does not accept splitting the package, and it is stated in Fatawa Qari' al-Hidayah, then he said: The contract, if it becomes invalid in part, becomes invalid entirely. Note: And it is not from the rule: when in acts of worship the factor of residence and the factor of travel come together, we do not give preponderance to the factor of residence. Its implication is to give it preponderance because the permissive and prohibitive factors come together. Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding wiping over khuffain: If he begins while a resident and then travels before completing a day and a night, his period is transferred to the traveler's period, so he wipes for three days; if the opposite, it is transferred to the resident's period. Its implication is to consider the period of residence in both, giving preponderance to the factor of residence, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said the same. According to him, if one khuff is for residence and the other for travel, likewise on the correct view, consistently applying the rule. But according to us, there is no doubt that his period is the traveler's period. And as for if he enters ihram as a qasir [shortening] and then his ship reaches the place of residence, he completes [the prayer], and if he begins prayer in the place of residence and then his ship moves, he does not shorten [the prayer], and I have not seen these two [cases] now. According to us, a missed prayer of travel when made up in residence is performed as two rak'ahs, and the opposite as four because the makeup mimics the original performance. As for the chapter of fasting: if one fasts as a resident and then travels during the day, or vice versa, breaking the fast is prohibited.

Exceptions in Endowments and Travel/Residence Worship
Exceptions in endowments and clarification of travel/residence worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply exceptions to partial invalidity in endowment rentals and explain why the mixing of residence and travel factors is not an exception to the general rule.

Core Idea
Endowment contracts do not allow partial invalidity in duration, and the travel/residence cases are governed by their own principles, not the general rule.

This final lesson covers two important sections: first, an exception regarding endowment leasing beyond the stipulated term, and second, a lengthy note (tanbih) clarifying that cases combining residence and travel (such as wiping over khuffs or qasr prayer) are not part of the exceptions to the rule of partial invalidity; rather, they follow the principle of giving weight to the predominant factor. This distinction is crucial for the mufti to avoid conflating different legal maxims.

Guided Path
1
Understand the endowment exception
If the endower stipulates that the endowment should not be rented for more than a year, and the overseer rents it for a longer period, the lease is valid for the first year but invalid for the excess. This is an exception because the contract does not accept splitting the package (saffqah) like a sale.
The invalidity of the excess does not retroactively affect the first year.
2
Analyze the travel/residence cases
The rule of partial invalidity does not apply when residency and travel factors combine in worship. Instead, the school gives preference to the factor that is more restrictive or more lenient depending on the situation. Examples: wiping over khuffs when changing from resident to traveler or vice versa; completing prayer when entering residence; qasr when traveling; and fasting while traveling.
This is a different mechanism: 'taghlib' (giving preponderance) rather than spread of invalidity.
3
Apply the fasting case
If one is fasting as a resident and travels during the day, or vice versa, breaking the fast is prohibited (haram). The partial change (from resident to traveler) does not invalidate the fast.
This shows that the worship is continuous and not split.
4
Distinguish from the general rule
The passage explicitly says 'whichever is not from the rule' (وليس من القاعدة). These are not exceptions but separate principles.
Muftis must not confuse the two sets of rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage is an extensive collection of exceptions (mustathnayat) to the general maxim that when something is invalid in part, it is invalid in whole. It is drawn from al-Bazzaziyyah, a famous Hanafi fatwa collection. The text methodically goes through various chapters of fiqh, showing where the rule applies and where it does not. Key examples: In judiciary (qada), if a judge is disqualified for some cases, he is disqualified for all. In acts of worship, if one intends to fast the entire month but only the first day is valid (because intention must be renewed). Exceptions include: accelerated zakat becomes valid for both years if nisab was owned at the time of payment; intention for two hajj together results in both being entered, but the ruling on renunciation differs; tayammum for multiple prayers is valid because one tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers. Other chapters include prayer over living and dead, istinja and impurity, divorce and emancipation, loans and pawning, and endowment rental. Finally, a note (tanbih) clarifies that the case of mixing residence and travel in worship is not an exception to this rule; rather, the school often gives preference to the travel factor, but also gives examples where residency prevails. This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning in applying and restricting general maxims.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf): Endowment: dedicating property for charitable use.
التنبيه (al-tanbih): A note or alert from the author clarifying a point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tanbih in this passage, when a resident travels during the day while fasting, what is the ruling?
A) He may break his fast because he is now a traveler.
B) He must continue fasting; breaking is prohibited.
C) The fast is invalidated partially.
D) He must break and make up later.

Key Takeaway
Not every combined ruling is an exception to the partial invalidity rule; the tanbih is critical for correct fatwa issuance.
