Rule on Combining Residence and Travel in Worship
Clarifying an exception to a previous qawida when worship combines residence and travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida on combining residence and travel in worship to new cases and identify which ruling prevails.

Core Idea
When residence and travel combine in worship, the Hanafi school does not always give precedence to the residence side.

This passage is a reminder (tanbih) from Ibn Nujaym, clarifying an exception to a previous qawida. The earlier maxim might suggest that the more restrictive element (residence) should dominate, but in acts of worship where both residence and travel are present, the Hanafi school often applies a nuanced approach. Through examples from wiping over khuffs, prayer, and fasting, you will see how the school balances the two states without always preferring residence.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Extract the core maxim from the passage: 'When in worship the side of residence and the side of travel come together, we do not give precedence to the side of residence.' Note that this is a nathr (miscellaneous) rule at the wusta (intermediate) level.
The maxim is explicitly given in the source.
2
Identify the scope
The rule applies to ibadat (worship), specifically purification (masah), prayer (qasr and qada), and fasting (sawm). It governs situations where both states coexist.
3
Work through each furu'
For each example in the text, state the fact pattern, the ruling, and why it follows or illustrates the qawida. Note the cross-madhhab comparison with al-Shafi'i.
The furuat are listed in the qawida_panel.
4
Identify the underlying rationale
The passage mentions that the mubih (permitter) and muharram (prohibiter/obligator) come together. The Hanafi approach is to not automatically prioritize the more restrictive (residence) but to balance based on the specific sequence and context.
The rationale is talil-based.
5
Apply to a new case
Using the qawida, derive the ruling for a case not explicitly mentioned, e.g., a traveler who begins wiping over socks in the third day and then returns home before completing the three days.
Think about whether the period transfers again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : وليس من هذه القاعدة؛ ما إذا اجتمع في العبادات جانب الحضر وجانب السفر فإنَّا لا نغلب جانب الحضر. ومقتضاها تغليبه لأنه اجتمع المبيح والمحرم لأن أصحابنا رحمهم الله قالوا في المسح على الخُفَّين: ولو ابتدأ وهو مقيم فسافر قبل إتمام يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى مدة المسافر فيمسح ثلاثا، ولو كان على عكسه انتقلت إلى مدة المقيم. ومقتضاها اعتبار مدة الإقامة فيهما تغليبًا لجانب الحضر، وبه قال الشافعي رحمه الله وعنده لو أحد الخُفَّين حضرًا والآخر سفرًا فكذلك على الأصح طردًا للقاعدة، وأما عندنا فلا خفاء في أن مدته مدة المسافر وأما لو أحرم قاصرًا فبلغت سفينته دار إقامته فإنه يتم، ولو شرع في الصلاة في دار الإقامة فسارت سفينته فليس له القصر، ولم أرهما الآن. وعندنا فائتة السفر إذا قضاها في الحضر يقضيها ركعتين وعكسه يقضيها أربعًا لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. وأما باب الصوم فإذا صام مقيما فسافر في أثناء النهار أو عكسه حرم الفطر.
A Reminder: Not from this rule is when in worship the side of residence and the side of travel come together, for we do not give precedence to the side of residence. Its implication would be to give it precedence because the permitted and the prohibited have come together, because our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding wiping over the khuffs: if one begins while a resident and then travels before completing a day and a night, his period transfers to the period of the traveler, so he wipes three days; and if the opposite, it transfers to the period of the resident. Its implication is to consider the period of residence in both, giving precedence to the side of residence, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said the same. In his view, if one khuff is put on while a resident and the other while a traveler, likewise according to the sound opinion, extending the rule. As for us, there is no doubt that his period is that of the traveler. And if one enters ihram while shortening prayer, but his ship reaches his place of residence, then he completes; and if he begins prayer in the place of residence and then his ship departs, he does not shorten; I have not seen these two now. And according to us, a missed prayer of travel if made up in residence is made up as two rak'ahs, and the opposite is made up as four, because the makeup replicates the performance. As for the chapter of fasting: if he fasts as a resident and then travels during the day, or vice versa, breaking the fast is prohibited.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a 'Tanbih' (reminder) from the author, Ibn Nujaym, indicating an exception to a previously stated qawida (legal maxim). The previous qawida likely gave precedence to the more restrictive element (hazar) when there is a conflict. However, in the case of worship that combines aspects of residence (hadar) and travel (safar), the Hanafi school does not automatically give precedence to the residence side. The author provides several examples: (1) Wiping over khuffs: If one starts wiping as a resident and then travels before completing one day and one night, the period shifts to that of a traveler (three days). If the opposite, it shifts to a resident's period (one day and one night). (2) Prayer: If one enters ihram as a traveler but then reaches his home port, he must complete (i.e., perform full prayer). If he starts prayer as a resident and then his ship departs, he does not shorten. (3) Make-up prayers: A missed travel prayer is made up as two rak'ahs even if performed in residence, and vice versa. (4) Fasting: If one is fasting as a resident and then travels during the day, or vice versa, it is prohibited to break the fast (i.e., the fast remains valid and must be completed). The passage also mentions that the Shafi'i school generally follows the principle of giving precedence to residence, but the Hanafi position differs in certain details. The author notes that he has not seen two specific sub-cases explicitly stated by his predecessors.

Key Terms
حضر (ḥaḍar): Residence; the state of being not traveling.
سفر (safar): Travel; a journey that meets the legal distance (approx. 48 miles) permitting concessions.
مبيح (mubīḥ): The element that makes something permissible (here, travel permits concessions).
محرم (muḥarram): The element that makes something prohibited or obligatory.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Make-up prayer performed after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He continues as a resident and wipes for one day and one night.
B) His period transfers to that of a traveler, so he wipes three days.
C) He must remove the khuffs and perform full ablution.
D) He wipes for the remainder of the first day only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida that residence is not given automatic precedence when combined with travel in worship is supported by specific examples in masah, prayer, and fasting.

The Qawida: When Preventer and Requirer Conflict
Establishing a qawida with examples and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal maxim 'When the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given precedence' to new cases, identify exceptions, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the washing of a junub martyr.

Core Idea
When a preventer and a requirer clash, the preventer wins — but the rule has exceptions where the requirer overrides.

This lesson introduces a foundational qawida that governs how Hanafi jurists resolve conflicts between preventing and requiring factors. Through concrete examples from purification, retaliation, and property rights, you will see how the preventer is generally given precedence. The passage also presents critical exceptions and an intra-madhhab dispute, which will sharpen your ability to apply the rule accurately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its core statement
Read the opening sentence: when the preventer (man'i) and the requirer (muqtadi) conflict, the preventer is given precedence. This is the general rule that will be applied across fiqh chapters.
Memorize the Arabic: إذا تعارض المانع والمقتضي فإنه يقدم المانع
2
List the illustrative furu' (cases) and explain why the man'i prevails
The passage gives examples: insufficient time/water for sunan of taharah (man'i = scarcity, muqtadi = sunnah), two wounds causing death (man'i = accidental component, muqtadi = intentional injury). For each, state clearly which factor is the man'i and why it overrides.
In the wound case, the accidental element prevents qisas even though the intentional element would require it.
3
Examine the mustathniyat (exceptions) and understand why the muqtadi is given precedence
The passage lists two exceptions: washing a junub martyr (Abu Hanifa's view) and the detailed ruling for mixed Muslim-disbeliever dead. Identify the man'i and muqtadi in each exception and see why the muqtadi wins here.
The exception for junub martyr is disputed: Sahibayn follow the general rule, but Abu Hanifa gives precedence to the requirement of washing due to janabah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on junub martyr
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa says wash because janabah (muqtadi) outweighs martyrdom (man'i). Sahibayn say do not wash because martyrdom prevents washing. Determine which position is mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as stated in later fatwa works.
5
Apply the qawida to property rights cases
The passage applies the rule to ownership disputes: lower/upper floors, pawner/lessor disposal. Here ownership is absolute but another's right is a preventer; the right (man'i) is given precedence over ownership (muqtadi). Understand the rationale: only benefit is lost by delay, not substance.
This shows the rule's application in mu'amalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : تدخل في هذه القاعدة قاعدة إذا تعارض المانع والمقتضي فإنه يقدم المانع؛ فلو ضاق الوقت أو الماء عن سُنن الطهارة حرم فعلها ولو جرحه جرحين عمدا وخطأ أو مضمونًا وهدرا ومات بهما فلا قصاص وخرجت عنها مسائل : الأولى : لو استشهد الجنب فإنه يغسل عند الإمام ومقتضاها ألا يغسل كقولهما. الثانية : لو اختلط موتى المسلمين بموتى الكفار فمقتضاها عدم التغسيل للكل . والشافعية قالوا بتغسيل الكل ولم يفصلوا، فأصحابنا رحمهم الله فصلوا فقال الحاكم في الكافي من كتاب التحرّي: وإذا اختلط موتى المسلمين وموتى الكفَّار فمن كانت عليه علامة المسلمين صلي عليه ومَن كانت عليه علامة الكفَّار ترك، فإن لم تكن عليهم علامة والمسلمون أكثر غُسلوا وكُفّنوا وصُلِّي عليهم وينوون بالصلاة والدعاء للمسلمين دون الكفَّار ويدفنون في مقابر المسلمين وإن كان الفريقان سواء لو كانت الكفَّار أكثر لم يصلّ عليهم ويغسلون ويكفنون ويدفنون في مقابر المشركين . (اهـ). وقد رجحوا المانع على المقتضى في مسألة سفل لرجل وعلو لآخر. فإن كلا منهما ممنوع عن التصرّف في ملكه لحق الآخر فملكه مطلق له وتعلق حق الآخر به مانع وكذا تصرف الراهن والمؤجر في المرهون والعين المؤجرة منع لحق المرتهن والمستأجر، وإنما قدَّم الحق هنا على الملك لأنه لا يفوت به إلا منفعة بالتأخير، وفي تقديم الملك تفويت عين على الآخر. وتمامه في العمادية من مسائل الحيطان.
Chapter: Included in this rule is the rule: when the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given precedence. So, if time or water becomes insufficient for the sunan of purification, performing them becomes prohibited. And if he wounds him with two wounds, one intentional and one by mistake, or one liable for compensation and one without, and he dies from both, there is no retaliation. And there are exceptions from it: first: if a junub is martyred, he is washed according to Abu Hanifa, but the implication of the rule would be that he is not washed, like the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Second: if the dead of Muslims are mixed with the dead of disbelievers, the implication would be not washing any of them. The Shafi'is said to wash all without distinction. Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) distinguished. Al-Hakim said in al-Kafi from the book of Taharri: if the dead of Muslims and the dead of disbelievers are mixed, whoever has a sign of Muslims is prayed over, and whoever has a sign of disbelievers is left; if they have no sign and the Muslims are more numerous, they are washed, shrouded, and prayed over, intending prayer and supplication for the Muslims exclusively, and buried in Muslim cemeteries; if the two groups are equal, (they are treated the same); if the disbelievers are more numerous, they are not prayed over, but are washed, shrouded, and buried in the cemetery of the polytheists. (End). And they gave precedence to the preventer over the requirer in the issue of the lower floor belonging to one person and the upper floor to another. Each is prevented from disposing of his property due to the right of the other; his ownership is absolute, but the attachment of the other's right is a preventer. Likewise, the disposal of the pawner and lessor over the pawned item and leased item is prevented due to the right of the pledgee and lessee. And here the right is given precedence over ownership because only benefit is lost by delay, whereas giving precedence to ownership would result in loss of the substance itself for the other. Its completion is in al-‘Imadiyya from the chapter of walls.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage introduces a new qawida within a larger discussion: when a preventing factor (mani) and a requiring factor (muqtadi) conflict, the preventing factor is given precedence. The author then provides three illustrations: (1) If time or water is insufficient to perform the sunan of wudu, it becomes prohibited to perform them (the time constraint prevents). (2) If a person inflicts two wounds, one intentional and one accidental, and the victim dies from both, no qisas is imposed because the preventing factor (accidental wound mixed with intentional) prevents retaliation. (3) Exceptions (mustathniyat) are then listed: a junub martyr is washed according to Imam Abu Hanifa despite the general rule that martyrs are not washed. Also, in the case of mixed Muslim and disbeliever dead, the detailed ruling from al-Kafi shows that signs and majority determine treatment. The passage then applies the rule to property rights: a person with ownership may be prevented from disposing of his property due to another's right (e.g., lower/upper floors, pawned items, leases). The right is given precedence over ownership because only benefit is delayed, while ownership precedence would cause loss of the substance. The reference to al-‘Imadiyya indicates further details.

Key Terms
مانع (māni‘): A factor that prevents the application of a ruling or impedes its effect.
مقتضي (muqtaḍī): A factor that requires or necessitates a ruling.
تغسيل (taghsīl): Ghusl of the deceased (washing the body).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They become recommended.
B) They become prohibited.
C) They become obligatory.
D) They remain sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida 'When the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given precedence' is a powerful tool for resolving conflicting factors, but it must be applied with awareness of its exceptions, such as the washing of a junub martyr.

The Rule on Ithar in Acts of Worship: When Altruism Becomes Disrespect
This passage introduces and explores the third qawida: whether ithar in acts of worship is disliked, with supporting furuat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'no ithar in acts of worship' to distinguish between permissible altruism in worldly matters and impermissible giving away of worship-related obligations.

Core Idea
Ithar (preferring others) is commendable in worldly matters but impermissible in acts of worship because worship is for Allah's glorification.

In this lesson, we examine a subtle qawida from the Hanafi tradition: may one give preference to another person in an act of worship? For example, should you give your wudu water to someone else if that would cause you to miss prayer? The Shafi'is explicitly state it is makruh, and the Hanafi jurists, though less explicit, rule similarly based on the purpose of worship. We'll explore the reasoning and its applications through concrete furuat.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its scope
Understand what ithar in worship means and which acts it applies to (qurbat, devotional acts).
The qawida is not explicitly found in early Hanafi texts but is derived from furuat.
2
Identify the underlying rationale
Recognize that worship is for tazim (veneration) and ijlal (glorification) of Allah, so preferring others contradicts that purpose.
Shaykh ‘Izz al-Dīn: 'the purpose of worship is veneration and glorification'.
3
Examine the furuat
Work through the four cases: wudu water, mosque seating, imam's spot, and food for survival.
Each case illustrates when ithar is prohibited (water, imam's spot) or allowed (voluntary standing, food in dire need).
4
Understand the exception
Ithar in worldly matters is commendable (based on Quran 59:9).
The Quranic verse praises altruism for material needs, not acts of worship.
5
Apply the qawida to a new scenario
Test your understanding by determining the ruling for a novel case, such as giving a spare Quran to a friend when you need it for recitation.
Consider whether the act is a qurbah and whether your own obligation would be compromised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاعدة الثالثة : هل يُكره الإيثار بالقرب؟ لم أرها الآن لأصحابنا رحمهم الله، وأرجو من كرم الفتّاح أن يفتح بها أو بشيء من مسائلها ؛ وهي الإيثار في القُرْب. وقال الشافعية الإيثار في القُرْب مكروه وفي غيرها محبوب قال الله تعالى: ﴿ويُؤْثِرُون عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِم وَلَوْ كَانَ﴾ [الحشر : ۹] . وقال الشيخ عزّ الدين : لا إيثار في القربات فلا إيثار بماء الطهارة ولا بستر العورة ولا بالوصف الأول لأن الغرض بالعبادات التعظيم والإجلال؛ فمن آثر به فقد ترك إجلال الإله وتعظيمه وقال الإمام : لو دخل الوقت ومعه ماء يتوضأ به فوهبه لغيره ليتوضأ له لم يجز، لا أعرف فيه خلافا لأن الإيثار إنما يكون فيما يتعلق بالنفوس لا فيما يتعلق بالقرب والعبادات. وقال في شرح المهذب في باب الجمعة : لا يُقام أحد من مجلسه ليجلس في موضعه فإن قام باختياره لم يكره فإن انتقل إلى من الإمام كره. قال أصحابنا رحمهم الله لأنه آثر بالقربة. وقال الشيخ أبو محمد في الفروق : من دخل عليه وقت الصلاة ومعه ماء يكفيه لطهارته وهناك من يحتاجه للطهارة لم يجز له الإيثار ولو أراد المضطر إيثار غيره بالطعام لا استبقاء مهجته كان له ذلك وإن خاف فوات مهجته والفرق أن الحق في الطهارة الله تعالى فلا يسوغ فيه.
The third rule: Is ithar (giving preference) in acts of worship disliked? I have not seen it now among our companions (may Allah have mercy on them), and I hope from the generosity of al-Fattah that He may open it or something of its issues. And it is ithar in acts of worship. The Shafi'is said: ithar in worship is disliked, and in other than it, it is beloved. Allah Most High says: {And they give preference over themselves, even though they are in need} [al-Hashr: 9]. And Shaykh ‘Izz al-Din said: There is no ithar in acts of devotion; so there is no ithar concerning water for purification, nor covering the ‘awrah, nor the first attribute, because the purpose of worship is veneration and glorification; whoever gives preference in it has left the veneration and glorification of Allah. And Imam al-Quduri said: If time enters and he has water to perform wudu with, then he gives it as a gift to someone else to perform wudu, it is not permissible; I know of no disagreement regarding it, because ithar only relates to matters of human desire, not matters of worship and devotion. And it is said in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab in the chapter of Jumu‘ah: no one should be made to stand from his place so that someone else sits in his spot; but if he stands voluntarily, it is not disliked; if he moves away from the imam, it is disliked. Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said: because he gave preference in an act of worship. And Shaykh Abu Muhammad said in al-Furuq: When the time for prayer enters and he has water sufficient for his purification, and there is someone else who needs it for purification, it is not permissible for him to give it away. But if a person in dire need wants to give his food to another to preserve his life, he may do so even if he fears losing his own life; the difference is that the right in purification belongs to Allah, so ithar is not permitted.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage introduces the third qawida: whether ithar (preferring others over oneself) is disliked (makruh) in acts of worship (qurb). The author notes that he has not seen an explicit statement from Hanafi scholars on this specific question, but he hopes to find it. He then presents the Shafi'i position that ithar in worship is makruh, while in worldly matters it is commendable (mahbub). The proof is the Quranic verse (al-Hashr: 9) which praises ithar in worldly needs. Shaykh ‘Izz al-Din explains that worship is about glorifying Allah, so giving preference to others in worship items (like water for wudu or covering one's ‘awrah) undermines that glorification. Imam al-Quduri (the Hanafi mujtahid) rules that if prayer time enters and one has sufficient water for wudu, it is impermissible to gift that water to another for wudu; there is no known disagreement. This is because ithar pertains to personal desires, not to duties owed to Allah. The passage then cites from Sharh al-Muhadhdhab the example of standing from one's seat in the mosque for another: if done voluntarily, it's not disliked, but if done for the imam's seat, it is disliked because it involves preferring another in a qurbah (seeking proximity to Allah). Finally, Shaykh Abu Muhammad in al-Furuq distinguishes between worship and worldly necessities: giving away water needed for one's own purification is not allowed, but giving away food to save another's life is allowed even at the risk of one's own life, because the right in purification belongs to Allah, not to the individual.

Key Terms
الإيثار (al-īthār): Preferring others over oneself, especially in acts of devotion or worldly matters.
القرب (al-qurb): Acts of worship that draw one nearer to Allah (qurbat).
التعظيم والإجلال (al-ta‘ẓīm wa al-ijlāl): Veneration and glorification (of Allah), the essence of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person has water sufficient for his own wudu but gives it to someone else during prayer time, what is the ruling?
A) Commendable because of altruism.
B) Not permissible because the right in purification belongs to Allah.
C) Permissible only if the other person is in greater need.
D) Obligatory if the other person cannot find water elsewhere.

Key Takeaway
The qawida 'لا إيثار في القربات' means that in acts of worship, one cannot give preference to another if it compromises one's own obligation, because worship is a right of Allah.

Ithar in Worship: When Giving Preference is Disliked
Presenting the rule that ithar (giving preference) is disliked in acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ithar is disliked in acts of worship and identify its exceptions in worldly matters.

Core Idea
Ithar in worship undermines Allah's right; ithar in worldly matters is encouraged unless harmful to self.

This lesson unpacks a subtle but crucial Hanafi maxim from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: giving preference to others in acts of worship is legally disliked (makruh). The rule rests on a fundamental distinction between rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and personal rights. We will explore its proof, its application across several fiqh chapters, and its exceptions, while also comparing the Shafi'i viewpoint.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
Read the opening of the passage. The rule asks: 'Is ithar in acts of worship disliked?' The answer is yes. This applies to all acts of worship (qurbat) where the primary purpose is exaltation of Allah.
The author notes he saw no explicit Hanafi text but relies on the principle.
2
Distinguish between rights of Allah and personal rights
The key distinction: worship involves Allah's right; ithar in worship means diminishing reverence. In worldly matters, the right is the individual's, so ithar is generally praiseworthy (within limits).
This is the illa behind the ruling.
3
Apply the maxim to specific furuat
Work through the cases: giving wudu water after time enters, displacing someone from a mosque seat, student giving turn in reading, pulling someone from first row. All are disliked because they involve a qurbah.
Voluntary leaving of a seat is not disliked; only ithar is.
4
Identify exceptions (istithna')
Not all ithar is disliked. Exceptions: giving food to save a desperate life (personal right, not worship), and a poor person giving dirhams if he can bear hardship. The reason is the right belongs to the individual.
If hardship is severe, spending on self is better.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and handle cross-madhhab differences
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that ithar is disliked in worship. The Shafi'is agree it is disliked in worship but differ in some applications. The practical thamarah is minimal, but the methodology highlights how usul principles derive rulings.
The Quranic verse (59:9) is used by Shafi'is to support general permissibility of ithar, but Hanafis restrict it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاعدة الثالثة : هل يُكره الإيثار بالقرب؟ خصاصة لم أرها الآن لأصحابنا رحمهم الله، وأرجو من كرم الفتّاح أن يفتح بها أو بشيء من مسائلها ؛ وهي الإيثار في القُرْب. وقال الشافعية الإيثار في القُرْب مكروه وفي غيرها محبوب قال الله تعالى: ﴿ويُؤْثِرُون عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِم وَلَوْ كَانَ [الحشر : ۹] . وقال الشيخ عزّ الدين : لا إيثار في القربات فلا إيثار بماء الطهارة ولا بستر العورة ولا بالوصف الأول لأن الغرض بالعبادات التعظيم والإجلال؛ فمن آثر به فقد ترك إجلال الإله وتعظيمه وقال الإمام : لو دخل الوقت ومعه ماء يتوضأ به فوهبه لغيره ليتوضأ له لم يجز، لا أعرف فيه خلافا لأن الإيثار إنما يكون فيما يتعلق بالنفوس لا فيما يتعلق بالقرب والعبادات. وقال في شرح المهذب في باب الجمعة : لا يُقام أحد من مجلسه ليجلس في موضعه فإن قام باختياره لم يكره فإن انتقل إلى من الإمام كره. قال أصحابنا رحمهم الله لأنه آثر بالقربة. وقال الشيخ أبو محمد في الفروق : من دخل عليه وقت الصلاة ومعه ماء يكفيه لطهارته وهناك من يحتاجه للطهارة لم يجز له الإيثار ولو أراد المضطر إيثار غيره بالطعام لا استبقاء مهجته كان له ذلك وإن خاف فوات مهجته والفرق أن الحق في الطهارة الله تعالى فلا يسوغ فيه الإيثار والحق في حال المخمصة لنفسه وكره إيثار الطالب غيره بنوبته في القراءة لأن قراءة العلم والمسارعة إليه قربة والإيثار بالقرب مكروه. قال الأسيوطي: من المشكل على هذه القاعدة؛ مَن جاء ولم يجد في الصف الأول فرجة فإنه يجر شخصا بعد الإحرام ويندب للمجرور أن يساعده ؛ فهذا يفوت على نفسه قربة وهي أخر الصف الأول . (انتهى). ثم رأيت في الهبة من منية المفتي: فقير محتاج معه دراهم فأراد أن يؤثر على نفسه، إن علم أنه يصبر على الشدَّة فالإيثار أفضل، وإلا فالإنفاق على نفسه أفضل. (انتهى). تدخل فيها قواعد :
The Third Rule: Is ithar (giving preference) in acts of worship disliked? I have not seen a specific text for our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) regarding this, and I hope from the generosity of the Opener that He opens it or some of its issues. It is ithar in acts of worship. The Shafi'is said: ithar in acts of worship is disliked, but in other matters it is beloved. Allah said: 'And they give preference over themselves even if they are in need' (Hashr 9). Shaykh 'Izz al-Din said: There is no ithar in acts of worship; so there is no ithar in water for purification, nor in covering the 'awrah, nor in the first row, because the purpose of worship is reverence and exaltation. Whoever gives preference in these has abandoned reverence for Allah. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: If the time enters and one has water for wudu, and he gives it as a gift to another to perform wudu, it is not permissible. I know of no disagreement on this, because ithar pertains to worldly matters, not to acts of worship. In Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, in the chapter of Jumu'ah: One should not be made to stand from his seat for another to sit. If he leaves voluntarily, it is not disliked; but if he moves to the imam's place, it is disliked. Our companions said: because he gives preference in an act of worship. Shaykh Abu Muhammad in al-Furuq said: If the time for prayer enters and one has water sufficient for his purification, and there is another who needs it, he may not give preference. If a desperate person wants to give preference to another with food to save his life, he may do so even if he fears his own death. The difference is that the right in purification belongs to Allah, so ithar is not permissible; the right in extreme hunger is for oneself. And it is disliked for a student to give preference to another in his turn for reading, because studying and hastening to it is an act of worship, and ithar in worship is disliked. Al-Asyuti said: One problematic issue for this rule: someone comes and does not find a gap in the first row, so he pulls a person after the takbir, and it is recommended for the pulled person to help; this causes him to miss an act of worship (the front row). (End). Then I saw in al-Hiba from Munyat al-Mufti: A poor needy person has dirhams and wants to give preference to others over himself; if he knows he can bear hardship, ithar is better; otherwise, spending on himself is better. (End). Included in this are rules:

Commentary
This passage presents the third legal maxim concerning ithar (giving preference to others) in acts of worship. The author notes he hasn't seen a clear Hanafi text on this, but hopes for divine opening. The Shafi'is rule that ithar is disliked in worship but beloved in worldly matters, citing Quran 59:9. Shaykh 'Izz al-Din explains: worship aims at exaltation of Allah, so giving preference to others in the means of worship (like water for wudu or the first row) undermines that reverence. Imam Abu Hanifa explicitly forbids giving away one's water for wudu when time has entered. The principle is: ithar applies to personal worldly rights, not to Allah's rights in worship. Exceptions exist for life-saving food. The passage also discusses problematic cases, like pulling someone from the first row, which still involves ithar. The final quote from Munyat al-Mufti clarifies that even in worldly matters, ithar is not always better; one must consider his own strength. This rule has many applications across fiqh chapters.

Key Terms
الإيثار (al-ithar): Giving preference to others over oneself in something beneficial.
القربة (al-qurbah): An act that brings one closer to Allah, i.e., an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it impermissible to give away one's water for wudu when prayer time has entered?
A) Because the water becomes impure after giving.
B) Because ithar in acts of worship is disliked and the right belongs to Allah.
C) Because the other person does not need it.
D) Because it causes delay in prayer.

Key Takeaway
Ithar is disliked in acts of worship because the right belongs to Allah, not to the individual.

The Follower Follows and Its Four Sub-Maxims
Presentation of the maxim 'al-tabi' tabi' and its four sub-maxims with furuat and istithna'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-tabi' tabi' and its four sub-maxims to identify when a follower can be isolated, when it falls, when it cannot precede, and when tolerances are granted, using the Hanafi furuat and istithna'at.

Core Idea
The follower follows the master in ruling, but exceptions arise when a specific cause, need, or original right exists.

This lesson unpacks one of the most versatile legal maxims in Hanafi fiqh: 'al-tabi' tabi' (the follower follows). The passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents four sub-maxims with a rich collection of furuat (branches) and istithna'at (exceptions) that demonstrate how the maxim operates across ibadat, muamalat, and inheritance. Understanding these sub-maxims equips the mufti with precise tools for determining when an accessory retains its dependent status and when it can be independently ruled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its four sub-maxims
List the four sub-maxims stated in the text: (1) not isolated, (2) falls with the followed, (3) does not precede, (4) tolerance in followers.
2
Extract furuat for each sub-maxim
For each sub-maxim, note the branches given (fetus, right of way, sunan prayers, etc.) and the ruling.
Pay attention to conditions that trigger exceptions.
3
Identify istithna'at (exceptions)
For the first two sub-maxims, note the cases where the follower is isolated or does not fall (e.g., emancipation of fetus, stipends for descendants, mute's obligation).
These exceptions are justified by specific causes (sabab) or necessity.
4
Apply to a new scenario using fatwa hierarchy
Given a modern case, determine which sub-maxim governs and whether any exception applies. Cite the maxim, its source, and the mufta bihi position.
Use the fatwa hierarchy to weigh conflicting principles if necessary.

The fourth rule: The follower follows.
First: It is not isolated in a ruling; among its branches: the fetus enters the sale of the mother as a follower and is not isolated in sale and gift like the sale. The most apparent.
And among them: the right of drink and way enter the sale of land as followers and are not isolated in sale according to the most apparent.

And there are exceptions: it is valid to emancipate a fetus without its mother on condition that she gives birth to it in less than six months. And it is valid to isolate it in a will with the mentioned condition.
And among them: it is valid to make a bequest to it even if it is an animal's fetus, and among them: it is valid to acknowledge it if the acknowledger provides a valid reason and it is born in less than six months.

And among them: it is valid to acknowledge it even if no reason is given if she gives birth within the minimum period in humans and within a period determined by experts in animals. And among them: the validity of its tadbir. And among them: the establishment of lineage. So the statement of the author of Al-Hidayah in the chapter of li'an that rulings are not established for a fetus before its delivery is not absolute, because you know that rulings are established for it before delivery; rather the meaning is some of them as indicated in Al-Inayah. And there are also exceptions: if the debtor said I have canceled the term or I have revoked it or I have made the debt due immediately, then the term is invalidated as in Al-Khaniyah and others; even though it is a description of the debt and the description follows its described, so it is not isolated in a ruling. And among the exceptions: if he drops the quality, then it is valid because it is his right as in Al-Asl, and among the exceptions: if he drops his right to imprison the pawn, they said it is valid, mentioned by al-Imadi in al-Fusul.

Among them: if the rider dies, the horse falls, not the opposite. And there are exceptions: those who have a right in the treasury of kharaj like fighters, scholars, their students, muftis, and jurists, their children are granted a stipend as followers and it does not fall with the death of the original, as encouragement. We have explained it in Sharh al-Kanz. Commentary
This passage belongs to the genre of qawaid fiqhiyyah (legal maxims) from the Hanafi work Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. The text begins with a concluding discussion on the maxim of al-ithar (preferring others), including a problematic case from al-Asyuti and guidance from Munyat al-Mufti. The core of the passage then introduces the fourth major maxim: 'al-tabi' tabi' (the follower follows). Under this, four sub-maxims are elaborated with numerous furuat (applications) and istithna'at (exceptions).

The first sub-maxim states that a follower is not isolated in a ruling; it is not independently subject to a legal disposition. The main application is the fetus (haml): it follows the mother in sale, gift, etc., but cannot be sold alone. Exceptions include independent emancipation, will, acknowledgment, inheritance, and diyah distribution under specific conditions. The text also addresses issues of debt term, quality, and securing payment: dropping the term or quality is allowed if it is one's own right, but these are also followers of the debt; the Hanafi position agrees with Shafi'is on pawn and guarantee but differs on term and quality because those are not typically isolated in contracts.

The second sub-maxim: the follower falls when the followed falls. Examples include missed sunan prayers during insanity (since the fard is not made up, its sunan also lapse), and missed Hajj rituals. Exceptions include stipends for descendants of military scholars, etc., which continue even after the original's death. The mute person's obligation to move tongue in takbir and talbiyah is an exception because speaking (the followed) is impossible, yet the follower (movement) is still required. The notification adds that sometimes the branch is established without the root, as in surety when the principal denies but the surety is bound, or khul' where the divorce occurs without property.

The third sub-maxim: the follower does not precede the followed. Illustrated by a follower (muqtadi) not preceding the imam in takbir or actions.

The fourth sub-maxim: what is not tolerated in non-followers is tolerated in followers. This is similar to the maxim that incidental matters are more lenient. An example from Jami' al-Fusulain is briefly noted but cut off.

Throughout, the author uses the structure of furuat and istithna'at to refine the maxim. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions are those marked as al-mukhtar or al-ashar.

Key Terms
التابع (al-tābi‘): Something that follows its master (mattabū‘) in legal status and is not independently ruled
المتبوع (al-matbū‘): The primary thing that the follower depends upon
الإيثار (al-īthār): Preferring others over oneself in matters of acts of worship or worldly benefit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the sub-maxim 'التابع لا يفرد بالحكم', which of the following is an exception?
A) Selling a pregnant animal separately from its fetus
B) Emancipating a fetus without its mother if born within six months
C) Including the right of way in a land sale without mention
D) Claiming that a fetus inherits without being born alive

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-tabi' tabi' provides a framework for determining the legal status of accessories, but exceptions based on specific causes (sabab) must always be considered.

When a Description is Independent: The Qawida and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explanation of the qawida and its application to pawn, guarantor, and the ikhtilaf with Shafi'is.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-wasf idha ufrida bi al-ʿaqd ufrida bi al-hukm' to distinguish subsidiaries from independent conditions, and evaluate the Shafi'i differing position.

Core Idea
A description that can be the subject of a contract is treated independently; mere descriptions are not.

In Hanafi legal theory, certain conditions and descriptions in contracts are considered subsidiary; they automatically fall when the principal falls. However, this rule has a key limitation: if the description itself can be the subject of an independent contract, it is given independent ruling. This passage from the Ashbah wa al-Nazair illustrates this principle and discusses an ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its condition
Read the passage and locate the verbalised rule: 'al-wasf idha ufrida bi al-ʿaqd ufrida bi al-hukm'. Note that the condition for independent treatment is that the description can be the subject of a contract.
2
Recognise the exceptions
The passage mentions exceptions: dropping the right to detain a pawn and releasing a guarantor. These are valid because the pawn and guarantor can be independently contracted upon.
These exceptions illustrate the qawida in action.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'is analogise time and quality to pawn and guarantor, arguing they are subsidiaries that fall with the principal.
The dispute is about which descriptions are independent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish: time and quality can be made the subject of a contract (e.g., a forward sale), so they are not mere subsidiaries. Pawn and guarantor are distinct because they are independently contractable.
The thamarah al-khilaf: time and quality stand even if the principal falls.
5
Apply the qawida to new cases
Test the rule with hypotheticals: e.g., a condition of payment in installments can be independently contracted (like a deferred payment sale), so it would not automatically fall.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجودة فإنه يصح لأنها حقه كما في الأصل، ومما خرج عنها لو أسقط حقه في حبس الرهن قالوا صح ذكره العمادي في الفصول.، ومنها الكفيل لو أبرأه الطالب صح، مع أن الرهن والكفيل تابعان للدين وهو باق ووافقنا الشافعية في الرهن والكفيل على الأصح وخالفونا في الأجل والجودة فارقين بأن شرط القاعدة ألا يكون الوصف مما يفرد بالعقد، فإن أفرد كالرهن والكفيل أفرد بالحكم.
Quality, for it is valid because it is his right as in the original. Among its exceptions: if he drops his right to detain the pawn, they said it is valid, mentioned by al-Imadi in al-Fusul. And among them: the guarantor, if the creditor releases him, it is valid, even though the pawn and guarantor are subsidiaries of the debt which remains. We agree with the Shafi'is on the pawn and guarantor according to the soundest opinion, and they disagree with us on the term and quality, distinguishing that the condition of the rule is that the description is not something that can be the subject of a contract. If it can be, like the pawn and guarantor, it is given independent ruling.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a discussion on the qawida that when a condition (wasf) can be the subject of a contract, it is given independent ruling. It discusses the example of quality (joda) as a right that can be dropped. It then gives exceptions: dropping the right to detain the pawn is valid, and releasing the guarantor is valid. It also notes the ikhtilaf with the Shafi'is: they agree on pawn and guarantor being subsidiaries but disagree on time and quality. The distinction is that if the description can be the subject of a contract, it is treated independently.

Key Terms
الوصف (al-wasf): A description or condition that is not capable of being the subject of an independent contract.
يفرد بالعقد (yufradu bi al-ʻaqd): The ability to be made the sole subject of a contract, like pawn or guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why is releasing a guarantor (kafil) valid even though the debt remains?
A) Because the guarantor is not a subsidiary of the debt.
B) Because the guarantor can be the subject of an independent contract.
C) Because the debt is also released.
D) Because the creditor has the right to release any part of the contract.

Key Takeaway
A description that can be the subject of a contract is given independent ruling; mere descriptions fall with the principal.

Subsidiary Does Not Precede Principal (Third Rule)
Qawida with one furu' from Qadi Khan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida 'The subsidiary does not precede the principal,' identify its application in prayer, and apply it to a novel furu' using the same rationale.

Core Idea
The follower cannot precede the imam – the rule of subsidiary-preceding-principal invalidates the act.

This third qawida from Ibn Nujaym's Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir establishes a foundational principle for acts where a subsidiary depends on a principal. In prayer, it means the follower must not precede the imam in any action. We will examine the rule, its primary application, and a furu' from Qadi Khan that extends it to ruku' and sujud in a four-rakat prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its core meaning
Begin by memorizing the maxim: 'التابع لا يتقدم على المتبوع'. Understand that it prohibits any subsidiary action from occurring before the principal action.
The relationship is hierarchical; the subsidiary's validity depends on the principal.
2
Identify the primary application: takbir and pillars in prayer
The text explicitly states that the follower cannot validly say the opening takbir or perform any pillar (ruku, sujud, etc.) before the imam begins that action. If he does, his act is invalid.
This is the default ruling; intent does not affect it.
3
Analyze Qadi Khan's furu' - what if follower precedes in ruku' and sujud?
Qadi Khan extends the ruling: if a follower in a four-rakat prayer precedes the imam in ruku' and sujud, that rak'ah is invalidated. The follower must make it up by repeating the rak'ah or following the imam's completion.
This shows the maxim applies to partial precedence as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة : التابع لا يتقدم على المتبوع ; فلا يصح تقدم المأموم على إمامه في تكبيرة الافتتاح ولا في الأركان إن انتقل قبل مشاركة الإمام وفرع عليه قاضي خان في فتاواه ما إذا سبق إمامه في الركوع والسجود في الرباعية.
The third: The subsidiary does not precede the principal; so it is not valid for the follower to precede his imam in the opening takbir nor in the pillars if he moves before the imam's participation. And Qadi Khan derived from it in his Fatawa: what if he precedes his imam in ruku' and sujud in a four-rakat prayer?
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is the third qawida: the subsidiary does not precede the principal. The text gives the example from prayer: the follower cannot precede the imam in the opening takbir or in the pillars if he acts before the imam. Qadi Khan adds a case of preceding in ruku and sujud in a four-rakat prayer, implying that such precedence invalidates that rak'ah or requires adjustment.

Key Terms
التقدم (al-taqaddum): Precedence in action before the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a follower in prayer says the opening takbir before the imam?
A) It is valid but disliked.
B) It is not valid; the follower must repeat the takbir after the imam.
C) The prayer is invalid.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
The principle that the subsidiary cannot outpace the principal governs the validity of the follower's actions in prayer and is applied by Qadi Khan to ruku' and sujud.

The Maxim 'The Subsidiary Falls When the Principal Falls'
Qawida with furuat: Many examples of the rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-tabi' yasqut bi-suqt al-matbu'' to identify when a subsidiary ruling falls and when it remains, and distinguish exceptions.

Core Idea
A subsidiary right or ruling falls with its principal, unless the subsidiary can stand independently or is retained by policy.

This lesson unpacks one of the key Hanafi legal maxims: 'The subsidiary falls when the principal falls.' You will see how this principle applies across ibadat and mu'amalat, and learn to recognize its exceptions—critical for accurate fatwa. The passage enumerates concrete furuat and a tanbih on the branch sometimes standing without the root.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its elements
State the Arabic maxim aloud and identify the two key terms: 'al-tabi'' (the subsidiary) and 'al-matbu'' (the principal). Understand that the maxim's scope is all fiqh chapters.
Memorize the maxim: التابع يسقط بسقوط المتبوع
2
Classify the subsidiary in each furu'
For each example from the passage, determine whether the subsidiary is an inherent part of the principal or a separate element that may be independently contracted. This classification decides whether the maxim applies strictly or has exceptions.
Examples: sunan are subsidiary to fard, ramy/mabit are subsidiary to wuquf, the horse is subsidiary to the horseman.
3
Apply the maxim to each furu'
Walk through each furu' and verify that the subsidiary falls when the principal is dropped. Note any cases where the subsidiary does not follow (istithna').
The mute's takbir is required even though speech is lost—this is an exception due to the independent nature of takbir.
4
Analyze the exceptions (istithna'at)
Identify two types of exceptions: (a) those based on policy (e.g., allowances for dependents), and (b) those where the branch is established without the principal (e.g., guarantor liability). Understand the reasoning behind each.
Refer to the istithna'at in the qawida_panel for details.
5
Synthesize the tanbih and related qawaid
The tanbih adds the nuance that the branch may be established without the principal. Connect this to related maxims like 'الوصف الذي لا يفرد بالعقد تابع' and 'التبرعات لا تقبل التبعيض'.
This step is crucial for fatwa: you must check if the subsidiary can be the subject of an independent contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : التابع يسقط بسقوط المتبوع منها من فاتته صلوات في أيام الجنون وقلنا بعدم القضاء لا يقضي سُننها الرواتب، ومنها من فاته الحج وتحلل بأفعال العمرة لا يأتي بالرمي والمبيت لأنهما تابعان للوقوف وقد سقط، ومنها لو مات الفارس سقط الفرس لا عكسه وخرج عنها من له حق في ديوان الخراج كالمقاتلة والعلماء وطلبتهم والمفتين والفقهاء يفرض لأولادهم تبعًا ولا يسقط بموت الأصل ترغيبا، وقد أوضحناه في شرح الكنز، ومما خرج عنها : الأخرس يلزمه تحريك اللسان في تكبيرة الافتتاح والتلبية على القول به أما بالقراءة فلا على المختار مع أن المتبوع قد وهو التلفظ. ومنها إجراء الموسى على رأس الأقرع فإنه واجب على المختار . تنبيه : يقرب من ذلك ما قيل ؛ يسقط الفرع إذا سقط الأصل. ومن فروعه قولهم : إذا برأ الأصيل برأ الكفيل بخلاف العكس وقد يثبت الفرع وإن لم يثبت الأصل. ومن فروعه لو قال لزيد على عمرو ألف وأنا ضامن به فأنكر عمرو لزم الكفيل إذا ادعاها زيد دون الأصيل كما في الخانية ومنها لو ادَّعى الزوج الخلع فأنكرت المرأة بانت ولم يثبت المال الذي هو الأصل في الخلع ومنها لو قال بعت عبدي من زيد فأنكر زيد عتق العبد ولم يثبت المال ومنها لو قال بعته من نفسه فأنكر العبد عتق العبد بلا عوض.
The second: The subsidiary falls when the principal falls. From it: one who missed prayers during days of insanity and we said no making up does not perform their sunan. From it: one who missed Hajj and performed Umrah actions does not do ramy and mabit because they are subsidiaries of wuquf which has fallen. From it: if the horseman dies, the horse falls, not vice versa. Excluded from it: those who have a right in the diwan of kharaj, like soldiers, scholars, their students, muftis, and jurists, an allowance is assigned to their children as a subsidiary and does not fall with the death of the original out of encouragement, as we clarified in Sharh al-Kanz. Among its exceptions: the mute is required to move his tongue in the opening takbir and talbiyah according to the opinion about it, but as for recitation, no, according to the chosen, even though the principal, which is uttering, has fallen. From it: passing the razor over a bald head is wajib according to the chosen. A note: close to that is what is said: the branch falls when the root falls. Among its branches: their saying: if the principal is absolved, the guarantor is absolved, unlike the opposite. And the branch may be established even if the principal is not established. Among its branches: if one says: Zayd has a thousand against Amr and I am a guarantor for it, then Amr denies, the guarantor is bound if Zayd claims it without the principal, as in al-Khaniyya. From it: if the husband claims khul', and the woman denies, she is separated but the property, which is the principal in khul', is not established. From it: if one says: I sold my slave to Zayd, and Zayd denies, the slave is freed but the money is not established. From it: if one says: I sold it to himself, and the slave denies, the slave is freed without consideration.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is the second qawida: the subsidiary falls when the principal falls. The text provides several examples: a person who missed prayers during insanity does not need to make up the sunan because the principal (fard) is dropped. Similarly, one who missed Hajj and performed umrah does not need to do rami and mabit because they are subsidiary to wuquf. If a horseman dies, the horse is dropped but not vice versa. Exceptions include allowances for dependents of soldiers and scholars where the allowance continues after death. Also, the mute must move his tongue for takbir but not for recitation, even though the principal (speaking) is dropped. Also, the requirement to pass a razor over a bald head is wajib on the relied-upon position. Then a note (tanbih) adds that the branch falls when the root falls, with examples from guarantor, divorce, and sale. Note that sometimes the branch is established even if the principal is not established, as when the guarantor is bound even if the principal debtor denies the debt.

Key Terms
التابع (al-tabi'): A legal ruling or right that is subsidiary to another (the matbu').
المتبوع (al-matbu'): The principal ruling or right that the subsidiary depends on.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a mute person regarding the opening takbir and recitation if the ability to speak is lost?
A) Both takbir and recitation are waived.
B) Takbir is required, recitation is waived.
C) Recitation is required, takbir is waived.
D) Both are required.

Key Takeaway
The maxim التابع يسقط بسقوط المتبوع is a powerful tool for a mufti, but it has crucial exceptions: the subsidiary may remain if it can be independently contracted or if policy retains it.

What is Overlooked in Subsidiaries (Fourth Rule)
Qawida with furuat and related maxim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'يغتفر في التوابع ما لا يغتفر في غيرها' and its sub-maxim 'يغتفر في الشيء ضمنا ما لا يغتفر قصدًا' to classify actions as subsidiary or primary, and determine when implicit actions are valid in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
What is overlooked implicitly is not overlooked intentionally – subsidiary matters permit what primaries prohibit.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi legal maxim that distinguishes between subsidiary (tawabi') and primary (ghayruha) matters. The maxim states that defects or relaxations allowed in subsidiaries are not allowed in primaries. A closely related sub-maxim extends this to implicit (dimnan) versus intentional (qasdan) actions. Through eight practical furuat from contracts, marriage, agency, and judicial rulings, you will see how this maxim operates across fiqh. Understanding this maxim is essential for a mufti to correctly apply the law in complex, multi-layered transactions.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the maxims
Commit to memory both the main maxim and its sub-maxim. The main maxim permits in subsidiaries what is not permitted in primaries; the sub-maxim permits implicitly what is not permitted explicitly.
These are part of the five major Hanafi qawaid.
2
Distinguish subsidiaries from primaries
Identify in each furu' which element is subsidiary (tabi') and which is primary. The subsidiary is often an action or consequence that is logically inseparable from the primary.
E.g., the co-owner's payment of compensation is subsidiary to the act of freeing.
3
Apply the sub-maxim to each furu'
For each case, determine whether the action was implicit (dimnan) or explicit (qasdan). The ruling will differ based on this distinction.
The seller measuring grain is implicit; the buyer explicitly appointing him is invalid.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
One furu' involves an ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the option of sight. Understand both positions and how the maxim supports each.
This shows that even within the school, qawaid can be interpreted differently.
5
Relate to complementary maxims
The text cites two related qawaid: 'He whose ratification is invalid initially is valid subsequently' and 'The subsidiary does not precede the principal.' Understand how they restrict or complement the main maxim.
These ensure the maxim is not applied indiscriminately.
6
Modern application
Practice applying the maxim to a contemporary scenario, such as an online agent executing transactions without explicit per-item authorization.
The implicit validity principle is crucial in Islamic fintech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة : يغتفر في التوابع ما لا يغتفر في غيرها. وقريب منها؛ يغتفر في الشيء ضمنا ما لا يغتفر قصدًا، وفي الفصل التاسع والثلاثين من جامع الفصولين فيما يثبت ضمنًا وحكمًا ولا يثبت قصدًا منه قن لهما أعتقه أحدهما وهو موسر فلو شرى المعتق نصيب الساكت لم يجز ولا يمكن الساكت من نقل ملكه إلى أحد، لكن لو أدى المعتق الضمان إلى الساكت ملك نصيبه ومنه غصب قنا فأبق من يده وضمنه المالك يملكه الغاصب ولو شراه قاصدًا لم يجز. ومنه فضولي زوجة امرأة يرضاها ثم وكله بعده بأن يزوجه امرأة فقال نقضت ذلك النكاح لم ينتقض ولو لم ينقضه قولاً، ولكن زوجه إياها بعد ذلك انتقض النكاح الأول. ومنه لو شرى كرير عينا وأمر المشتري البائع بقبضه للمشتري لم يصح، ولو دفع إليه غرارة وأمره أن يكيله فيها صح إذ البائع لا يصلح وكيلاً عن المشتري في القبض قصدًا ويصلح ضمنا وحكما لأجل الغرارة. ومنه شرى ما لم يره فوكل وكيلاً بقبضه فقال الوكيل قد أسقطت الخيار، أعني خيار الرؤية، لم يسقط خيار الموكل ولو قبضه الوكيل وهو يراه سقط خيار رؤية موكله عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله خلافًا لهما. وقريب من هذا الجنس من لا تجوز إجازته ابتداء وتجوز انتهاء. ومنه القاضي إذا استخلف مع أن الإمام لم يفوض له الاستخلاف لم يجز، ومع هذا لو حكم خليفته وهو يصلح أن يكون قاضيًا وأجاز القاضي أحكامه يجوز ومنه أن الوكيل بالبيع لا يملك التوكيل به ويملك إجازة بيع بائعه فضولي؛ والمعنى فيه أنه إذا أجاز يحيط علمه بما أتى به خليفته ووكيل الوكيل كذلك، فتكون إجازته في الانتهاء عن بصيرة بخلاف الإجازة في الابتداء. ومنه القاضي لو قضى في كل أسبوع يومين بأن كان له ولاية القضاء في يومين من كل أسبوع لا غير ; فقضى في الأيام التي لم تكن له ولاية القضاء فإذا جاءت نوبته أجاز ما قضى جازت إجازته . (انتهى).
The fourth: What is overlooked in subsidiaries is not overlooked in others. And close to it: what is overlooked implicitly is not overlooked intentionally. In the thirty-ninth chapter of Jami' al-Fusulain: regarding things that are established implicitly and by effect but not intentionally. From it: a slave owned by two, one of them frees him and he is wealthy. If the freeing one buys the share of the silent one, it is not permissible. And the silent one cannot transfer his ownership to anyone. But if the freeing one pays compensation to the silent one, he owns his share. From it: a usurped slave runs away from his hand and the owner guarantees him; the usurper owns him, but if he buys him intentionally, it is not permissible. From it: a guardian (fuduli) marries a woman who is pleased, then afterwards appoints him as agent to marry him a woman; if he says: I cancel that marriage, it is not cancelled. But if he does not cancel it verbally but then marries her to him, the first marriage is cancelled. From it: if one buys a sack of grain and orders the seller to take delivery for the buyer, it is not valid. But if he gives him a sack and orders him to measure it into it, it is valid, because the seller is not fit as agent for the buyer in taking delivery intentionally, but he is fit implicitly and by effect because of the sack. From it: one buys something he has not seen, then appoints a deputy to take delivery. If the deputy says: I have dropped the option, meaning the option of sight, the option of the principal is not dropped. But if the deputy takes delivery while seeing it, the option of sight of the principal drops according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two. Close to this type: one whose ratification is not valid initially but is valid subsequently. From it: if a judge appoints a deputy when the imam did not authorize him to do so, it is not permissible. But if his deputy rules and he is fit to be a judge, then the judge ratifies his rulings, it is permissible. From it: the agent for sale does not have the right to appoint an agent, but he has the right to ratify the sale of a fuduli seller. The meaning is that when he ratifies, he becomes aware of what his deputy did, and the deputy's agent likewise. So his ratification at the end is based on insight, unlike ratification at the beginning. From it: if a judge rules only two days a week, he has jurisdiction only those days. If he rules on days he has no jurisdiction, then when his turn comes, he ratifies what he ruled, his ratification is permissible. (End.)
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is the fourth qawida and a related maxim: what is overlooked in subsidiaries is not overlooked in others, and what is overlooked implicitly is not overlooked intentionally. The text provides numerous applications from various chapters of fiqh. For example, if one of two co-owners frees a slave, the freeing owner cannot buy the other share directly, but if he pays compensation, he can own it. A usurper who is liable for a runaway slave owns him implicitly but cannot buy him intentionally. A fuduli guardian's marriage is not cancelled by a later statement but is cancelled by the actual subsequent marriage. A seller can act as agent for delivery implicitly if given a sack. An agent who drops the option of sight does not affect the principal, but if he takes delivery while seeing, the principal's option drops according to Abu Hanifa. A judge can ratify the rulings of a deputy appointed without authorization. An agent for sale can ratify a fuduli sale even though he cannot delegate. A judge can ratify decisions made outside his jurisdiction when his turn comes.

Key Terms
يغتفر (yughtafaru): To be overlooked, excused, or considered valid despite a defect.
ضمنًا (dimnan): Implicitly, by indirect means, or by effect.
قصدًا (qasdan): Intentionally, directly, or explicitly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The principal's option is not affected.
B) The principal's option drops.
C) The agent's action is invalid.
D) The principal must see it himself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi legal system operates on the principle that subsidiary and implicit matters are treated with greater leniency than primary and explicit ones, facilitating transactions while preserving juristic rigor.

Exceptions to the Maxim of Continuity: Two Cases Where Beginning Differs from Endurance
Two exceptions to the common maxim about continuity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two exceptions to the general rule that what is valid initially remains valid, and apply the maxim 'يغتفر في الابتداء ما لا يغتفر في البقاء' to new cases in judgeship and slave permission.

Core Idea
What is overlooked at the start may become fatal later — two exceptions prove the rule.

This passage presents a valuable benefit (faa'idah) from the Hanafi tradition: two cases where the opposite of the common maxim holds true. In general, a legal situation that is valid at its inception continues to be valid. However, in the appointment of a judge and in granting permission to a slave, the beginning and continuation are judged differently. Understanding these exceptions sharpens one's application of legal maxims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its reversal
First, recall the well-known Hanafi maxim: what is valid at the beginning remains valid (ما صح في الابتداء يصح في البقاء). The passage introduces an opposite maxim: 'What is overlooked in the beginning is not overlooked in continuation.' This means that certain defects tolerated at the start become unacceptable later.
The new maxim is a dabt (restrictive rule), not a general principle.
2
Examine the first exception: judge's sin
The passage states that it is valid (sahih) to appoint a sinful person (fasiq) as a judge initially. However, if a just judge becomes sinful after appointment, he is dismissed. The beginning allows what the continuation does not. Ibn Kamal notes that the fatwa is on dismissal.
This reflects public interest: once corruption manifests, it invalidates continuity.
3
Examine the second exception: runaway slave
If a slave already has permission to trade (ma'dhun) and then runs away (abaqa), his permission is revoked. Conversely, if one grants permission to a slave who is already a runaway, the permission is valid initially. Again, the beginning is more lenient.
Qadi Khan restricts this case to the slave having property 'in his hand' (fi yadihi).
4
Synthesize the underlying principle
Both exceptions involve a change in condition after the initial act. In judgeship, continued justice is required; in slavery, continued trust is needed. The maxim 'Consideration is given to endings' (العبرة بالخواتيم) parallels this idea: the final state may override the initial validity.
The Hanafi approach balances initial leniency with ongoing integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة : ظفرت بمسألتين؛ يغتفر في الابتداء ما لا يغتفر في البقاء، عكس القاعدة المشهورة. الأولى : يصح تقليد الفاسق القضاء ابتداء ولو كان عدلاً ابتداء ففسق انعزل عند بعض المشايخ. وذكر ابن الكمال أن الفتوى عليه. الثانية : لو أبق المأذون انحجر، ولو أذِنَ للآبق صح، كما في قضاء المعراج. وقيده قاضيخان بما في يده.
A benefit: I came across two issues: what is overlooked in the beginning is not overlooked in continuation, opposite the well-known maxim. The first: it is valid to appoint a sinful person as a judge initially, but if he was just initially and then committed sin, he is dismissed according to some scholars. Ibn Kamal mentioned that the fatwa is on that. The second: if a permitted slave runs away, his permission is revoked; but if one grants permission to a slave who is already a runaway, it is valid, as in Qada' al-Mi'raj. Qadi Khan restricted it to what is in his hand [i.e., if he has property in hand?].
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This is a benefit (faa'idah) noting two exceptions to the common maxim that what is valid in the beginning is valid in continuation. Here, it is the opposite. First, a sinful person can be appointed as a judge initially, but if a just judge becomes sinful, he is dismissed. Second, if a slave with permission to trade runs away, the permission is revoked; however, if someone grants permission to a slave who is already a runaway, it is valid. Qadi Khan restricts this to property in the slave's hand.

Key Terms
الابتداء (al-ibtida'): The initial state or beginning of a legal situation.
البقاء (al-baqa'): The continuation or persistence of a legal situation.
الانعزال (al-in'izal): The automatic dismissal or removal from office, here of a judge.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave who has been given permission (idhn) by his master to engage in trade.
الآبق (al-abiq): A runaway slave ('abd abiq).
قضاء المعراج (Qada' al-Mi'raj): A work on endowment and related rulings by al-Mi'raj (?)
قاضيخان (Qadi Khan): A Hanafi jurist and author of al-Fatawa al-Kubra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is automatically freed.
B) His permission to trade is revoked.
C) Nothing changes; the permission remains.
D) He must be sold.

Key Takeaway
Two Hanafi exceptions show that what is tolerated at the beginning may become unacceptable in continuation, refining the general rule of continuity.

Judicial Orders and Waqf Appointments: The Prohibition of Unauthorized Positions
A legal maxim with applied furu' on waqf appointments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'Amr al-Qāḍī lā yanfudh illā idhā wāfaqa al-shar‘' to waqf scenarios and distinguish between valid and invalid appointments by the judge.

Core Idea
A judge’s order is void if it violates Shari'ah; creating unauthorized waqf positions is prohibited even for essential roles.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Ashbāh wa al-Naẓā'ir presents a foundational rule for judges: their orders are only effective when aligned with divine law. The text then tests this principle against several real-world waqf (endowment) cases, showing how even a seemingly beneficial appointment by a judge can be invalid if it exceeds the founder's stipulations. Here, you will learn to apply this maxim and understand its exceptions through concrete fatwa examples.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the general principle at the beginning: 'Amr al-qāḍī lā yanfudh illā idhā wāfaqa al-shar‘' (The judge's order is not executed unless it agrees with the Shariah). Recognize it as a kubra (major) maxim.
This principle founds the entire discussion.
2
Apply the first fur‘: the farāsh case
The text gives the example of a judge appointing a servant (farāsh) for a mosque without the waqf founder's condition. Determine why this is prohibited: it violates the founder's stipulation and the principle of waqf sanctity.
The judge cannot add new obligations on the waqf.
3
Understand qiyas awlawī (a fortiori analogy)
The text argues that if a necessary servant cannot be appointed without condition, then creating new jobs (waẓā’if) or salaries (muratbāt) is prohibited with greater reason. Identify the common illa: all exceed the founder's terms.
This is a classic use of qiyas jaliy.
4
Analyze the nuance for poor-endowment appointments
The passage introduces a fatwa: if the endowment is specifically for the poor, the judge's appointment of a salary is valid but not binding—the guardian can change it unless the judge makes a binding ruling. Note the exception (istithna') and its condition.
Validity here is procedural, not substantive entitlement.
5
Apply the surplus rule
The final question deals with surplus (fā’iḍ) of a silent waqf. The text rules that surplus cannot be given to the poor or another waqf; it must be invested to generate income for the original waqf. See why this follows from the same qawida.
The founder’s silence does not grant discretion to waste the surplus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا اعلم أن أمر القاضي لا ينفذ إلا إذا وافق الشرع وصرّح في الذخيرة والولوالجية وغيرهما بأن القاضي إذا قرر فراشًا للمسجد بغير شرط الواقف لم يحلّ للقاضي ذلك ولم يحلّ للفراش تناول المعلوم . (اهـ). مع و به علم حرمة إحداث الوظائف بالأوقاف بالطريق الأولى؛ لأن المسجد احتياجه للفراش لم يجز تقريره لإمكان استئجار فراش بلا تقرير، فتقرير غيره من الوظائف لا يحل بالأولى وبه علم أيضًا حرمة إحداث المرتبات بالأوقاف بالأولى، وقد سئلت عن تقرير القاضي المرتبات بالأوقاف فأجبت بأنه إن كان من وقف مشروط للفقراء فالتقرير صحيح لكنه ليس بلازم وللناظر الصرف إلى غيره وقطع الأول إلا إذا حكم القاضي بعدم تقرير غيره ; فحينئذ يلزم وهي في أوقاف الخصاف وغيره، وإن لم يكن من وقف الفقراء لم يصح ولم يحل ، وكذا إن كان من وقف الفقراء وقرّره لمن يملك نصابًا . ثم سُئِلت: لو قرر من فائض وقف سكت الواقف عن مصرف فائضه فهل يصح ؟ فأجبت بأنه لا يصح أيضًا لما في التاتارخانية : إن فائض الوقف لا يصرف للفقراء، وإنما يُشتَرى به المتولي مستغلاً. وصرح في البزازية وتبعه في الدرر والغرر بأنه لا يصرف فائض وقف لوقف آخر اتحد واقفهما أو اختلف . (اهـ).
By this, know that the order of the judge is not executed unless it agrees with the Shariah. And it is explicitly stated in al-Dhakhīrah, al-Walwālijiyyah, and others that if the judge appoints a servant (farāsh) for the mosque without the condition of the waqf founder, it is not permissible for the judge to do that, nor is it permissible for the servant to take the stipend. Moreover, by this, the prohibition of creating new jobs (waẓā’if) from endowments is known in the first place (bi l-ūlā). Because the mosque's need for a servant did not permit his appointment since it is possible to hire a servant without an appointment (taqrīr), so appointing other jobs is not permissible with greater reason. And by this, the prohibition of creating new salaries (muratbāt) from endowments is known with greater reason. And I was asked about the judge's appointment of salaries from endowments: I answered that if the endowment is restricted for the poor, the appointment is valid but not binding; the guardian (nāẓir) may divert to others and discontinue the first, unless the judge rules that no other appointment is made — then it becomes binding. This is in the endowments of al-Khaṣṣāf and others. But if it is not from the endowment of the poor, it is not valid and not permissible. Similarly, if it is from the endowment of the poor and he appoints it for someone who possesses nisāb (minimum wealth), it is invalid. Then I was asked: If he appoints from the surplus (fā’iḍ) of an endowment whose founder was silent about the disposal of its surplus, is it permissible? I answered that it is also not valid, because according to al-Tātārkhāniyyah: The surplus of an endowment is not disbursed to the poor; rather, the mutawallī buys with it income-generating property. And it is stated in al-Bazāziyyah and followed by al-Durar wa al-Ghurar that the surplus of one endowment is not disbursed to another endowment, whether the founders are the same or different.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling that begins with the principle: a judge's order is only effective if it conforms to Shariah (waftaqa al-shar‘). It then applies this principle to endowments. The first application: a judge cannot appoint a servant (farāsh) for a mosque without such condition in the waqf deed; if he does, the servant's stipend is illegal because it exceeds the waqf's terms. By analogy (qiyās awlawī — a fortiori), creating new job positions (waẓā’if) or salaries (muratbāt) from waqf funds is also prohibited. The reasoning is that if even a necessary position like a janitor cannot be appointed when the deed is silent, then less essential positions are even more prohibited. The text then provides a fatwa regarding the judge's appointment of salaries from endowments: if the endowment is specifically for the poor, the appointment is technically valid but not binding; the guardian can change it. However, if the judge explicitly rules that no other appointment is made, it becomes binding. If the endowment is not for the poor, or if the appointee is wealthy (owns nisāb), the appointment is invalid. The passage also addresses surplus funds from a silent waqf: they cannot be spent on the poor or on another waqf; instead, the mutawallī must use them to purchase income-generating property.

Key Terms
الفراش (al-farāsh): A servant or janitor appointed to maintain a mosque
الوظائف (al-waẓā’if): Jobs or positions created from endowment funds
فائض الوقف (fā’iḍ al-waqf): Surplus income from waqf after expenses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid and recommended
B) Invalid; the servant cannot take the stipend
C) Valid but not binding
D) Valid only if the mosque is large

Key Takeaway
A judge's order in waqf matters is strictly limited by the founder's stipulations; any appointment not authorized by the waqf deed is invalid, and surplus must be invested, not spent on new positions.
